Before I propose structure, I want to make sure I understand what you're carrying over and what's genuinely different \u2014 because the carrier project's shape is quite specific, and copying it wholesale would probably be wrong.\n\n## What's portable from the carrier project\n\nThe skeleton is sound and worth keeping:\n\n- **Two SOPs + a router skill file + reference docs + scripts** as the project-knowledge layout. This separation (rules in SOPs, lookups in reference markdown, tools in scripts, scaffolding in SKILL.md) works.\n- **Pull-fresh-every-batch + re-derive-column-map** discipline for any backend that you actively edit between sessions.\n- **URL verification gate** (HTTP 200 + content presence + soft-error detection) as a hard requirement before anything goes in an output workbook. Terminals research will hit the same paywall/Cloudflare/stale-link problems.\n- **Cluster-coherence + canonical-name normalization** for entities that appear under many variants (owners, charterers \u2192 developers, operators, JV partners).\n- **Confidence labels (green/yellow/red) tied to source tier + corroboration count**, with primary/regulatory as a stand-alone green.\n- **The two-workflow split**: fill-existing-rows vs discover-new-entities. Terminals will likely want the same split.\n- **Negative-result logging** so a failed search doesn't get re-run identically next batch.\n\n## What's almost certainly different for LNG terminals\n\nA few things I want to flag before we design anything:\n\nThe carrier workflow leans hard on **one canonical source (ChinaShipBuild)** for the most critical field (hull number), with a fallback ladder when CSB doesn't have it. Terminals have no equivalent single canonical orderbook. The closest analogs \u2014 GEM's own GOGET/GIOGET dataset, IGU's World LNG Report, GIIGNL, FERC/DOE filings for US, regulatory filings per country \u2014 are all partial. So the \"Ring A authoritative\" concept probably becomes \"Ring A is country-specific regulators.\"\n\nTerminals have a **lifecycle with many more states** than carriers (announced, pre-FID, FID, under construction, commissioning, operating, mothballed, decommissioned, cancelled), and the state transitions are themselves contested in the press. Carriers basically have on-order / delivered / scrapped. The confidence model and conflict-handling rules will need more nuance.\n\n**Capacity is multi-dimensional** (nameplate vs sendout vs storage; mtpa vs bcm/y vs m\u00b3 LNG storage; per-train vs total). Carriers just have m\u00b3 cargo capacity. Unit-conversion and source-disagreement handling will be a bigger deal.\n\n**FSRUs and floating liquefaction (FLNG)** straddle the carrier/terminal boundary \u2014 you may already touch them in the carrier project, and you'll need a rule for which project owns which records.\n\n**GEM is the destination, not the source.** The carrier project pulls from a Google Sheet that the user owns. For terminals you're updating GEM's database \u2014 which has its own schema, its own publication cadence, its own internal review process. The \"backend pull\" step probably becomes \"fetch the current published GIOGET/GOGET CSV and use it as the baseline,\" and the output isn't an xlsx of citations but a submission package in whatever format GEM accepts.\n\n## What I need from you before drafting structure\n\nA few questions so I'm not building this on guesses:",

If you're also working the carrier project, we should write a rule for which project owns the record, or how they sync.     "text": "Useful \u2014 that doc is essentially an empty template with one stub entry (New Zealand). So the \"country resources\" infrastructure exists but is mostly unpopulated. That changes my thinking a bit: a useful by-product of any batch run should be *contributing back* to that doc, not just consuming it.\n\nOK, here's my proposal. I'll keep it at the level of structure and key decisions rather than drafting full SOPs, so you can push back before I commit to anything.\n\n## What carries over from the carrier project, and what changes\n\nThe carrier scaffolding had a clean separation: **rules** (SOPs) / **lookups** (reference markdown) / **tools** (scripts) / **router** (SKILL.md). That separation is worth keeping. But the specifics change a lot.\n\nThe biggest structural difference: the carrier project's \"fill blank [ref] cells in existing rows\" workflow has no clean analog here. GEM's database doesn't have separately citeable `[ref]` cells per field \u2014 it has datasource fields attached to logical groups (capacity has one datasource field, cost has one, location has one). And the unit of work is fundamentally different: in carriers it's a row; here it's a **unit within a project**, with project-level and unit-level data on different timescales, plus a status timeline that's append-only.\n\nSo I think you want **three** workflows, not two:\n\n1. **Update existing terminals** \u2014 confirm or revise data on units already in the database (status timeline append, capacity revision, cost update, ownership refresh). This is the bread-and-butter of the annual cycle.\n2. **Discover new terminals** \u2014 find projects not yet in the database (the carrier discovery analog).\n3. **Triage / scoping** \u2014 decide *which* terminals/countries to look at this batch, given quarterly cadence + global scope. Carriers didn't need this because the backend was small and the unit of work obvious. Terminals does.\n\n## Proposed file inventory\n\nMirroring the carrier project's layout, with substitutions:\n\n**SOPs (rules):**\n- `lng_terminal_update_sop.md` \u2014 the \"update existing units\" workflow, including the status timeline append rules from the manual, capacity-revision rules, FAQ-derived edge cases (debottlenecking, dead-and-revived proposals, inferred shelved\u2192cancelled, etc.), confidence labels, and the URL verification gate.\n- `lng_terminal_discovery_sop.md` \u2014 the \"find new projects\" workflow, including the \"sufficient information to add\" threshold from the manual (sponsor + approximate location + concrete step), and the Possible Updates handling.\n- `lng_terminal_triage_sop.md` \u2014 the \"which countries/projects this batch\" workflow, including the per-quarter region rotation and the inferred shelved/cancelled sweep (which is itself a triggerable batch type \u2014 projects with no updates for 2+ years).\n\n**Router:**\n- `SKILL.md` \u2014 same idea as the carrier project's. Routes phrasing to workflow, lists the file inventory, hard requirements.\n\n**Reference docs (the \"lookups\"):**\n- `gem_db_schema.md` \u2014 column-to-canonical-field map for the all-fields CSV. The carrier project's `csb_yard_urls.md` was a small fixed table; this is bigger because GEM's CSV has ~115 columns. Should also document the difference between project-level and unit-level fields and how they appear in the export.\n- `source_roster.md` \u2014 like the carrier version, but reorganized:\n  - **Tier 1 global**: GIIGNL, IGU (with the FAQ caveats about their inconsistencies), LNG Prime\n  - **Tier 1 by region**: FERC/DOE filings (US), EU PCI lists (Europe), METI/JOGMEC (Japan), MOTIE/KOGAS (Korea), MOPNG (India), CNPC/Sinopec/CNOOC IR (China), etc.\n  - **Tier 2**: trade press (Reuters, S&P Global Commodity Insights, Argus, Upstream, Offshore Technology, etc.)\n  - **Tier 3**: regional press\n  - **Forbidden / cautioned**: BNEF (per FAQ), pre-October-2025 wiki auto-citations (per FAQ)\n- `country_research_notes.md` \u2014 pre-seeded from the GEM Google doc, but designed so that batch findings *feed back into it*. This is the deliverable to GEM that's separate from the database edits.\n- `entity_canonical_map.md` \u2014 analog of `owner_charterer_map.md`. For terminals this is mostly **developers/sponsors** (TotalEnergies, Cheniere, Venture Global, Petronas, NLNG, Adnoc Gas, Sempra, etc.). Critical because GEM has an entity system shared across trackers and creating a duplicate entity is a real cost.\n- `lifecycle_rules.md` \u2014 the status-timeline state machine derived from the manual. Worth pulling out as its own reference because the rules are intricate (inferred shelved at 2yr, inferred cancelled at 4yr, FAQ on shelved\u2192cancelled, FAQ on dead-and-revived, \"closest non-planned-non-FID status to bottom of timeline wins\").\n- `unit_conventions.md` \u2014 the unit subdivision rules from the manual (single vs. multi-unit, phase vs. train, \"largest subdivisions trackable without losing information\"), plus naming conventions.\n- `sop_pointers.md` \u2014 same purpose as in the carrier project, mapping rules to SOP sections for quick lookup.\n\n**Scripts:**\n\nDirect analogs of carrier scripts:\n- `pull_backend.py` \u2192 **`pull_gem_db.py`** \u2014 wraps the upload's `gem_export_via_web.py`. Adds the column-map derivation step (the manual notes the CSV is ~115 columns).\n- `normalize.py` \u2192 **kept**, but the maps are different \u2014 country names, entity names, capacity units.\n- `dedup_index.py` \u2192 **kept conceptually**, but indexes are different: `(country, project_name_normalized)`, `(country, sponsor_normalized, lifecycle_state)`, plus a unit-level index for catching expansion-vs-new-project ambiguity.\n- `url_verifier.py` \u2192 **mostly unchanged**. Same \u00a73.8-style gate. The soft-error patterns will differ (paywall stubs from S&P Global, GIIGNL members-only redirects, EU PCI portal SSO walls) but the harness stays.\n- `csb_fetch.py` \u2192 **dropped**. No single canonical orderbook for terminals. Per-regulator fetchers would each be small and brittle \u2014 better handled as per-batch web searches with the verifier doing the heavy lifting.\n- `imo_tracker.py` \u2192 **dropped for terminals**, *unless* we need to track FSRU vessels \u2014 which the manual says we do at the project level (Vessel Operator, Vessel Owner fields). So this one might actually port over, used in a much narrower context. Worth flagging.\n- `build_workbook.py` \u2192 **replaced by `build_review_package.py`** \u2014 produces a pre-commit review xlsx (per-project, what's changing, what sources, what confidence) that you eyeball before applying edits to the live database. Even with direct edit access, a staging artifact is valuable for tricky batches.\n- `recalc.py` \u2192 **kept** as a sanity check on the review xlsx.\n\nNew scripts that the carrier project didn't need:\n- **`capacity_normalize.py`** \u2014 mtpa \u2194 bcm/y \u2194 m\u00b3 LNG storage conversion, range-handling (manual says: \"record max value in spreadsheet, range on wiki\"), per-train vs. total reconciliation.\n- **`status_timeline.py`** \u2014 derives current status from a timeline per the manual's \"closest non-planned-non-FID status to bottom\" rule, validates legal state transitions, detects timeline anomalies (e.g., operating without prior construction).\n- **`stale_sweep.py`** \u2014 for the \"inferred shelved at 2yr, inferred cancelled at 4yr\" workflow. Reads the timeline + last-updated date, produces a candidate list.\n- **`entity_lookup.py`** \u2014 queries the GEM entity system to avoid creating duplicates (the manual is emphatic about this).\n\n## Key decisions I want your input on before I draft anything\n\nA few things where the carrier conventions don't translate cleanly and I'd rather not guess:",

The vessel exists whether or not it's currently deployed at a regas site.\n- **Terminals project**: cares about FSRUs as *terminals* \u2014 country, location, lifecycle status, sendout capacity (mtpa/bcm/y), terminal operator, gas grid connection. The terminal exists at a specific port, and the FSRU vessel docked there is one attribute (Vessel Owner, Vessel Operator fields per the manual).\n\nThe clean separation: **each project owns its own fields**, and the two records are linked by IMO + vessel name. Specifically:\n\n| Field type | Owned by | Examples |\n|---|---|---|\n| Vessel identity & technical specs | Carriers | IMO, builder, hull, m\u00b3 LNG, propulsion, delivery year, vessel owner, vessel operator |\n| Terminal identity & operations | Terminals | Country, port, terminal name, sendout capacity (mtpa/bcm), terminal operator, lifecycle status, location, sponsor |\n| Linking fields (both records must agree) | Sync rule | Vessel name, IMO |\n\nThe **sync rule** is the discipline that keeps the link from rotting:\n\n1. When a terminals batch adds or updates an FSRU terminal, the Vessel Name and IMO go in the staging xlsx with a note flagging it as a sync-touchpoint.\n2. When a carriers batch adds or updates an FSRU vessel that's deployed (i.e. has a terminal assignment), the terminal name + country go in the carrier xlsx with the same flag.\n3. Once per batch, run a cross-check script that diffs the two backends on (IMO \u2194 terminal name) pairs and surfaces mismatches. Mismatches go to a sync-conflicts sheet in whichever xlsx is the current deliverable.\n4. Reassignments (FSRU moves from terminal A to terminal B) are explicitly modeled \u2014 the terminal A record gets an \"Idled\" status timeline entry, terminal B gets the new vessel, and the carrier record's deployment field updates. The script catches the case where one side updates and the other doesn't.\n\nTwo things this rule doesn't try to settle, intentionally:\n\n- **FSU and FRU** (the manual mentions these as variants \u2014 floating storage only, or floating regas only without storage). They behave the same way for sync purposes; same rule applies.\n- **Deepwater Port LNG terminals** (offshore but not floating, per the manual). These are *terminals only* \u2014 no vessel record. No sync needed. The cross-check script should know to skip them.\n\nIf this looks right, I'll codify it in both project's SKILL.md files as a short cross-reference block, with a script (`fsru_sync_check.py`) in the terminals project that reads both backends and produces the diff.\n\n## What I'd produce next\n\nAssuming the FSRU rule above is roughly right (or you correct it), the next step is to actually draft the files. The sheet list I'm thinking:\n\n- `README` \u2014 batch parameters, methodology summary, what was done\n- `updates` \u2014 rows for existing terminals being updated (one row per affected unit, with old \u2192 new value diffs and citations)\n- `new_terminals` \u2014 rows for newly discovered projects (project-level fields) with paired `new_units` for unit-level\n- `new_units` \u2014 unit-level data for new terminals, and new units within existing terminals (expansions)\n- `status_timeline_additions` \u2014 append-only by design per the manual, so this gets its own sheet\n- `entity_additions` \u2014 new immediate owners/operators/vessel-owners to be created in the entity system, with duplicate-check flags\n- `fsru_sync` \u2014 the cross-check output (matches, mismatches, reassignments) if the batch touches any FSRUs; omitted otherwise\n- `qa_review` \u2014 per-cell citation log, conflicts, defects, verification log, negative-result log\n- `stale_sweep` \u2014 output of the inferred-shelved/cancelled sweep if that ran as part of this batch\n- `country_notes_contributions` \u2014 drafted additions to the GEM country-resource doc, for you to copy over manually\n\nThat's nine sheets. Probably too many for small batches \u2014 I'll add a rule that empty sheets get omitted.\n\n**Same color scheme** means I'll port the carrier conventions: green fill for high-confidence cells (primary/regulatory source OR two corroborating sources agreeing on value), yellow for entity-level confirmation with value implied/contested, red for single weak source (prefer leaving blank). One adjustment for terminals specifically: a **fourth color** \u2014 blue \u2014 for cells that are *unchanged from existing DB value but re-verified this batch*. Carriers didn't need this because the carrier `[ref]`-fill batches only touched blank cells. For terminals, a lot of work is \"checked, no change\" (the manual literally has a \"no changes\" option in the Record of Full Updates field), and that should be visually distinct from \"changed to green-confidence value.\"\n\n**`gem_db_schema.md` from the actual export** is the right call. I'd rather work from real column names than guess. The 115-col export will also let me see which columns are project-level vs unit-level (the export probably duplicates project-level fields across all unit rows for a multi-unit project, but I should verify rather than assume), and how the status timeline is encoded in flat CSV \u2014 that's a non-obvious schema question I can't answer from the manual alone.\n\nWhen you upload the CSV, two things I'll be looking for specifically:\n\n1. **Row structure** \u2014 one row per unit, or one row per project with units serialized into columns? The manual implies the former but the all-fields export might do either.\n2. **Status timeline encoding** \u2014 the manual describes timelines as ordered lists with sub-statuses and notes. In a flat CSV that probably collapses to either (a) a JSON blob in one cell, (b) multiple parallel columns like `status_1`, `status_year_1`, `status_substatus_1`, ..., or (c) the current-status only, with timeline history not in the export at all. If it's (c), the staging xlsx workflow needs to handle the case where we can't see prior timeline entries from the export alone, and the SOP needs a rule about pulling timeline history from the live DB on a per-project basis.\n\nUpload when ready.",

Let me think through what makes it distinct before slotting it in.\n\n## Why it's its own SOP\n\nUpdate, discovery, and triage are all **outward-looking** \u2014 start from a project or country, search the web, find sources, propose changes. Reconciliation is **inward-looking** \u2014 start from one authoritative source document, walk through it line by line, diff against the database. Different shape of work:\n\n- Input is **bounded and known** (one PDF or dataset), not \"search the web until satisfied\"\n- The unit of work is a **row in GIIGNL**, not a row in the GEM database\n- The output is a **three-way diff**: matches, GIIGNL-has-GEM-doesn't, GEM-has-GIIGNL-doesn't, plus value-disagreements on matched rows\n- Confidence labeling works differently \u2014 GIIGNL is a single source with known biases (the FAQ explicitly warns about GIIGNL/IGU inconsistencies), so \"two corroborating sources\" doesn't apply the same way\n- The manual already encodes a precedence rule: GIIGNL is the default, but a more specific/current source overrides it. Reconciliation has to respect that \u2014 not every GEM/GIIGNL disagreement is a GEM bug\n\n## How it interacts with the other workflows\n\nReconciliation produces three outputs, and each routes to a different downstream workflow rather than handling everything itself:\n\n| Reconciliation finding | Routes to |\n|---|---|\n| GIIGNL has a project GEM doesn't | Discovery workflow (verify it's real, in-scope, and meets the \"sufficient information to add\" threshold) |\n| GEM has a project GIIGNL doesn't | Update workflow (likely fine \u2014 GIIGNL has known gaps \u2014 but log it; could also indicate a GEM project should be merged or reclassified) |\n| Both have it, values disagree | Update workflow (with GIIGNL as one source in a conflict, not automatically authoritative) |\n| Both have it, values agree | Log as cross-check confirmation; bump confidence on the GEM record |\n\nSo reconciliation is upstream of update/discovery, not parallel to them. The SOP describes how to do the diff cleanly; the *fixes* go through the existing workflows. This keeps the rules in one place.\n\n## Where it fits in the cycle\n\nThe methodology doc says GIIGNL is published around June and is \"a key resource supporting the update\" during the Q2\u2013Q3 annual cycle. So reconciliation is naturally an **annual workflow**, run once when the new GIIGNL report drops, feeding work into the quarterly update/discovery batches that follow. It's not something you'd run every quarter.\n\nWorth being explicit about this in the triage SOP too \u2014 \"is there a fresh GIIGNL we haven't reconciled against?\" becomes one of the triage inputs.\n\n## What the SOP needs to cover\n\nSketching the section list:\n\n1. **Inputs and parameters** \u2014 GIIGNL edition year, what GEM export to diff against (always the freshest), scope (operating only? include under-construction? include proposed?). GIIGNL coverage varies by section and the SOP needs to be clear about which GIIGNL tables we're using.\n2. **Extracting GIIGNL into structured form** \u2014 the report is a PDF with tables. Need a script (`giignl_extract.py`) that parses the relevant tables into a normalized CSV with the same column conventions as the GEM export (so the diff is column-aligned). Probably tractable since GIIGNL tables are stable year-over-year.\n3. **Matching algorithm** \u2014 fuzzy name match within country, with manual review for ambiguous cases. This is where `entity_canonical_map.md` and the country normalization in `normalize.py` earn their keep.\n4. **Disagreement classification rules** \u2014 capacity disagreements (often unit conversion or per-train vs total), start year disagreements (often planned vs actual), owner disagreements (often immediate vs ultimate parent). Each class has a default resolution but not an automatic one.\n5. **Output structure** \u2014 adds two sheets to the standard workbook: `giignl_diff` (the row-level diff) and `giignl_to_action` (the findings routed to update/discovery for follow-up).\n6. **Documenting GIIGNL errata** \u2014 when GIIGNL is wrong and GEM is right, log it. Over years this builds a useful record of GIIGNL's failure modes.\n\n## Updated file inventory\n\nAdds:\n- `lng_terminal_reconciliation_sop.md` \u2014 the SOP\n- `giignl_extract.py` \u2014 PDF\u2192CSV extractor for GIIGNL tables\n- `giignl_diff.py` \u2014 three-way diff against the GEM export\n\nThe `build_review_package.py` script gets two more conditional sheets (`giignl_diff`, `giignl_to_action`) for reconciliation batches.\n\nThe drafting order I proposed becomes:\n\n1. `SKILL.md` (now describing four workflows, not three)\n2. `gem_db_schema.md`\n3. `lifecycle_rules.md`\n4. `lng_terminal_update_sop.md`\n5. `lng_terminal_discovery_sop.md`\n6. `lng_terminal_reconciliation_sop.md` \u2190 new, fits naturally after discovery since it routes findings into both\n7. `lng_terminal_triage_sop.md`\n8.     "text": "Excellent \u2014 that resolves the schema questions and reveals some important things I had wrong:\n\n**The earlier wc -l count of 2,119 was bytes-with-newlines-in-cells, not rows.** Real count: 1,263 unit-rows across 859 terminals. About 75% are single-unit, 25% are multi-unit, with a long tail up to 13 units.\n\n**Row structure is one row per unit.** Project-level fields (TerminalName, Country/Area, Location, Owner, Parent, etc.) are duplicated across every unit-row in a multi-unit project. That's a real fact about the schema with consequences \u2014 if a batch updates a project-level field like the Operator, the script needs to apply it to every unit-row of that project, not just one. The carrier project never had this distinction because every row was independent.\n\n**Status timeline does NOT come out in the export.** The CSV has *anchor years* (ProposalYear, ConstructionYear, OriginalPlannedStartYear, LatestPlannedStartYear, ActualStartYear, ActualStartYear2, ActualStartYear3, ShelvedYear, CancelledYear, StopYear, FIDYear) plus the current Status and Substatus. The full ordered timeline with notes is database-only. This is option (c) from my earlier guess \u2014 and it means the SOP needs an explicit rule: **when a status update is part of a batch, you must pull the current timeline from the live DB before staging the new entry**, because the export alone can't show you what's already there. I'll need to add a `fetch_timeline.py` script that takes a UnitID and pulls the timeline via the web UI (probably scraping the unit edit page, since there's no API). Worth flagging now because it adds work to every status-update path.\n\n**The \"FacilityType [ref]\" pattern confirms separately-citeable fields.** The export has 21 `[ref]` columns (Status [ref], Owner [ref], Capacity [ref], Location [ref], Cost [ref], Floating Vessel Name [ref], etc.). The workflows are (1) update existing terminals, (2) discover new terminals, (3) reconcile against the annual GIIGNL report, and (4) triage (decide what to work on this batch). Use this skill whenever the user asks for a terminals batch, a GIIGNL diff, a stale-sweep, a discovery run, an FSRU sync check, or any work that produces or modifies the staging xlsx (lng_terminals_batch_YYYYMMDD.xlsx). The skill is the executable scaffolding \u2014 the project's research rules live in GEM's published methodology doc (the \"LNG Terminals Manual\"), which is authoritative for what counts as a terminal, what the lifecycle states mean, and how units are named. The SOPs in this project are operational \u2014 they describe how to do the work, citing the methodology rather than restating it.\n---\n\n# LNG Terminals \u2014 Backend Scaffolding\n\n## How this file fits in the project\n\nThis is project-knowledge scaffolding for an agentic research workflow that helps a GEM contractor update the Global Gas Infrastructure Tracker's LNG terminals dataset. The user has direct edit access to the live GEM database but does NOT delegate writes to the agent \u2014 every batch produces a staging xlsx that the user reviews and applies manually.\n\nThe project knowledge contains:\n\n- **The GEM LNG Terminals Manual** (Google Doc, read into context at session start) \u2014 the authoritative rules of what to research and how. Sometimes called \"the methodology doc.\"\n- **Four SOPs** \u2014 the operational rules for each workflow:\n  - `lng_terminal_update_sop.md` \u2014 update existing terminals (the bread-and-butter of the annual cycle); folds in [ref]-fill work\n  - `lng_terminal_discovery_sop.md` \u2014 find new terminals not yet in the database\n  - `lng_terminal_reconciliation_sop.md` \u2014 three-way diff against GIIGNL (generic body, GIIGNL-specific appendix; future IGU SOP reuses the body)\n  - `lng_terminal_triage_sop.md` \u2014 decide what to work on this batch\n- **This file** \u2014 the workflow router\n- **6 reference docs** (`gem_db_schema.md`, `lifecycle_rules.md`, `source_roster.md`, `entity_canonical_map.md`, `unit_conventions.md`, `country_research_notes.md`, `sop_pointers.md`)\n- **~10 Python scripts** under `scripts/` \u2014 the tools\n\n### How project knowledge appears in context\n\nFiles in claude.ai project knowledge appear as conversation context (loaded in the `<documents>` block at the start of a chat), NOT as files mounted on the bash filesystem. The `<file_path>` tags like `/mnt/project/gem_db_schema.md` are descriptive labels \u2014 `cat` and `cp` will not find them. Reading via the `view` tool also won't work for these files.\n\n**To run the scripts**, materialize them to disk first by writing the content from project context into a working directory:\n\n```bash\nmkdir -p /home/claude/work\n```\n\nThen for each script the workflow needs, use `create_file` (or `cat > path << 'EOF' ... EOF` in bash) to write its content from the project_files context into `/home/claude/work/<script>.py`. After that the scripts can be invoked directly (`cd /home/claude/work && python pull_gem_db.py`).\n\nThe reference markdown files don't need materializing \u2014 read them directly from context whenever the workflow says \"see `<file>.md`\".\n\n### Two exceptions to \"everything is in context\"\n\nTwo artifacts are too large to live in conversation context and need to be fetched at batch start instead:\n\n1. **The fresh GEM database export** \u2014 pulled via `pull_gem_db.py` at the start of every batch. The user maintains session-cookie env vars (see `gem_export_via_web.py`); the script wraps that to also derive the column-index map.\n2. **The GIIGNL report** \u2014 when present in the project files (e.g. `/mnt/project/GIIGNL2026AnnualReport*.pdf`), it arrives as a zip of per-page JPEG images + per-page OCR text + a manifest, NOT as a parseable PDF. `giignl_extract.py` reads the OCR text files. Confirm the file shape with `file <path>` before assuming `.pdf` means PDF.\n\n## Read the methodology + relevant SOPs first\n\nThe methodology doc is authoritative. The SOPs are operational. Before any batch:\n\n1. Confirm the methodology doc is in context (it's a long Google Doc \u2014 if it's not visible, ask the user to re-share). Note its \"Last updated\" line.\n2. View the SOPs relevant to the workflow being run (one to three of them, depending on batch type).\n3. Check `sop_pointers.md` for a quick rule lookup map.\n4. If an SOP cites a methodology section that no longer exists or has changed, flag to the user before proceeding \u2014 the methodology is what GEM staff will review your edits against, so the SOPs must stay aligned.\n\n## Workflow router\n\n### Update existing terminals (most common)\n\nTrigger phrases: \"update terminals in [country/region]\", \"refresh the [country] entries\", \"fill blank refs for terminals X to Y\", \"annual update for [country]\", \"check what's stale in [country]\", \"go through [country] terminals\".\n\nWorkflow (assuming scripts have been copied to a working directory per the section above):\n\n1. `python pull_gem_db.py` \u2192 fresh CSV at `/home/claude/gem_export.csv`, prints derived column-index map. **Re-derive on every run** \u2014 the schema can drift between GEM database revisions.\n2. Confirm batch scope per Update SOP \u00a72 (which terminals/countries, depth of update, whether [ref]-fill is in scope, whether status updates are in scope).\n3. `python dedup_index.py` \u2192 builds project/unit indexes per Update SOP \u00a73.\n4. For each terminal in scope:\n   a. Pull the unit-level timeline from the live DB (`python fetch_timeline.py <UnitID>`) if any status changes are anticipated \u2014 the export does NOT contain timeline history, only anchor years and current status.\n   b. Source-search per Update SOP \u00a74 \u2014 using `source_roster.md` for tier selection and `country_research_notes.md` for country-specific tips.\n   c. Apply lifecycle state machine per `lifecycle_rules.md` \u2014 especially the planned-vs-actual sub-status logic and the \"closest non-planned-non-FID status to bottom\" rule for deriving current status.\n   d. For [ref]-fill: identify blank `[ref]` columns paired with **filled** data values (the equivalent of carrier-project Rule F \u2014 no orphan citations).\n5. `python url_verifier.py <url> <expected1> <expected2> ...` on every URL before it goes in the xlsx. Or import as a module \u2014 see the script's docstring.\n6. `python capacity_normalize.py` on any capacity changes \u2014 mtpa/bcm/y/m\u00b3 conversions, range handling per methodology (\"record max in spreadsheet, range in wiki Background\").\n7. `python entity_lookup.py \"<owner name>\" \"<country>\"` before staging any new owner/operator \u2014 the methodology is emphatic about not creating duplicate entities.\n8. **If any FSRU terminal is touched**: `python fsru_sync_check.py` \u2014 see \"FSRU sync rule\" below.\n9. `python build_review_package.py --mode update --batch-id <YYYYMMDD>` \u2192 `/mnt/user-data/outputs/lng_terminals_batch_<YYYYMMDD>.xlsx`.\n10. `python recalc.py /mnt/user-data/outputs/lng_terminals_batch_<YYYYMMDD>.xlsx` \u2192 confirm zero formula errors.\n11. `present_files`.\n\n### Discover new terminals\n\nTrigger phrases: \"find new terminals in [country/region]\", \"discovery run\", \"what's missing from GEM in [region]\", \"catch-up sweep for [country]\", \"any new proposals in [region]\".\n\nWorkflow:\n\n1. Confirm parameters per Discovery SOP \u00a72 (region/country scope, gap window if any, whether to include early-stage proposals that may not meet the \"sufficient information to add\" threshold from the methodology FAQ).\n2. `python pull_gem_db.py` \u2192 fresh CSV; `python dedup_index.py` \u2192 indexes used for matching candidates against existing records.\n3. **Country-level regulatory sweep** \u2014 Discovery SOP \u00a74 lists per-country regulators (FERC/DOE for US, EU PCI portal + national TSOs for Europe, METI/JOGMEC for Japan, MOTIE for Korea, CNPC/Sinopec/CNOOC IR for China, etc.). Use `country_research_notes.md` to seed the search and contribute findings back.\n4. **Trade press sweep** \u2014 per Discovery SOP \u00a75, using `source_roster.md`. LNG Prime, Reuters, S&P Global Commodity Insights, Argus, Upstream are the workhorses.\n5. **Sponsor IR sweep** \u2014 for known LNG developers (Cheniere, Venture Global, TotalEnergies, Sempra, Adnoc Gas, QatarEnergy, Petronas, NLNG, NextDecade, etc.) \u2014 per Discovery SOP \u00a76 and `entity_canonical_map.md`.\n6. For each candidate: apply the \"sufficient information to add\" threshold from the methodology FAQ (sponsor identified + approximate location + concrete step taken). Candidates that don't meet the threshold go in a `monitor_list` sheet, not `new_terminals`.\n7. `python url_verifier.py` on all URLs; `python entity_lookup.py` on every new owner/operator/parent.\n8. **If any candidate is an FSRU**: `python fsru_sync_check.py` against both the GEM terminals and (if available) the LNG carrier project's backend.\n9. `python build_review_package.py --mode discovery --batch-id <YYYYMMDD>` \u2192 staging xlsx.\n10. `python recalc.py`, then `present_files`.\n\n### Reconcile against GIIGNL (annual, triggered by report release)\n\nTrigger phrases: \"reconcile against GIIGNL\", \"GIIGNL diff\", \"compare GEM to the new GIIGNL\", \"process the [year] GIIGNL report\".\n\nWorkflow:\n\n1. Confirm the GIIGNL report is in project files. `file <path>` to confirm format (the 2026 report came as a zip of JPEG + OCR text per page, NOT a parseable PDF). Note the edition year.\n2. Confirm scope per Reconciliation SOP \u00a72 (which GIIGNL tables \u2014 terminal-list, capacity-by-country, country-summary; which lifecycle states to include).\n3. `python pull_gem_db.py` \u2192 fresh CSV.\n4. `python giignl_extract.py /mnt/project/GIIGNL*.pdf --output /home/claude/giignl_normalized.csv` \u2192 flat CSV with GEM-aligned column names per Reconciliation SOP \u00a73 (Appendix A for GIIGNL-specific table parsing).\n5. `python report_diff.py --gem /home/claude/gem_export.csv --report /home/claude/giignl_normalized.csv --output /home/claude/giignl_diff.json` \u2192 three-way diff (matches, GIIGNL-only, GEM-only, value-disagreements).\n6. Route findings per Reconciliation SOP \u00a74:\n   - GIIGNL-only \u2192 Discovery workflow (verify candidate is real and in-scope before adding)\n   - GEM-only \u2192 log in `giignl_to_action` sheet, usually no action (GIIGNL has known gaps per the methodology FAQ)\n   - Value-disagreement \u2192 Update workflow (GIIGNL is one source in a conflict, NOT automatically authoritative \u2014 the methodology FAQ says a more specific or current source takes priority)\n   - Match \u2192 confidence bump on the GEM record\n7. **DO NOT auto-apply GIIGNL values to the GEM record.** Every value-disagreement requires resolution through the Update workflow's normal source-search and confidence-labeling process.\n8. `python build_review_package.py --mode reconciliation --report giignl --year <YEAR>` \u2192 staging xlsx with `giignl_diff` and `giignl_to_action` sheets in addition to the standard sheets.\n9. `python recalc.py`, then `present_files`.\n\n(A future IGU reconciliation SOP will reuse this workflow body with `igu_extract.py` and `--report igu`.)\n\n### Triage (decide what to work on this batch)\n\nTrigger phrases: \"what should we work on this quarter\", \"what's stale\", \"plan the [Q1/Q2/Q3/Q4] batch\", \"where are the gaps\", \"what hasn't been touched in a while\".\n\nWorkflow:\n\n1. `python pull_gem_db.py` \u2192 fresh CSV.\n2. `python stale_sweep.py` \u2192 for each terminal/unit, compute LastUpdated age and lifecycle-rule-driven flags:\n   - Proposed/Construction units with LastUpdated > 12 months \u2192 due for refresh\n   - Proposed units with no updates > 2 years \u2192 candidates for inferred shelved (per methodology)\n   - Shelved units with no updates > 4 years \u2192 candidates for inferred cancelled (per methodology)\n   - Operating units with LastUpdated > 18 months \u2192 due for refresh (lower priority than active development)\n3. Pull triage inputs per Triage SOP \u00a73:\n   - Stale-sweep results (above)\n   - Recent news scan (last quarter) for activity in countries that haven't been touched recently\n   - GIIGNL reconciliation backlog (any unprocessed findings from a prior reconciliation batch)\n   - User priorities (existing GEM team commitments, upcoming publications)\n   - Whether a fresh GIIGNL/IGU report has dropped since the last reconciliation\n4. Produce a triage memo (markdown, not xlsx) with recommended batch composition. The user decides scope before any Update or Discovery batch starts.\n\n## FSRU sync rule (cross-project)\n\nFSRUs are tracked in both the GEM terminals tracker and (if the user is also running it) the LNG carrier project. Each project owns its own fields:\n\n| Field type | Owned by | Examples |\n|---|---|---|\n| Vessel identity & technical specs | Carriers | IMO, builder, hull, m\u00b3 LNG capacity, propulsion, delivery year, vessel owner, vessel operator |\n| Terminal identity & operations | Terminals | Country, port, terminal name, sendout capacity (mtpa/bcm), terminal operator, lifecycle status, location, sponsor |\n| Linking fields (both records must agree) | Sync rule | Vessel name, IMO |\n\n**Sync rule mechanics:**\n\n1. When a terminals batch adds or updates an FSRU terminal, the FloatingVesselName + (IMO if known) go in the staging xlsx with a sync-touchpoint flag.\n2. When a carriers batch updates an FSRU vessel that's deployed, the terminal name + country go in the carrier xlsx with the same flag.\n3. `fsru_sync_check.py` diffs both backends on (IMO \u2194 terminal name) pairs and surfaces mismatches. Mismatches go in a `fsru_sync` sheet of whichever xlsx is the current deliverable.\n4. **Vessel reassignment** (FSRU moves from terminal A to terminal B) is a real and observed pattern \u2014 at least one terminal in the export has three FSRUs in sequence. The script handles it by modeling: terminal A's prior FSRU gets an \"Idled\" or \"Retired\" status timeline entry on the unit-row; terminal B (or a new unit on terminal A) gets the new FSRU. The carrier record's deployment field updates correspondingly.\n\nEdge cases:\n- **FSU / FRU** (floating storage only / floating regas only) \u2014 same rule applies.\n- **Deepwater Port LNG terminals** (offshore but not floating) \u2014 terminals only, no vessel record, no sync needed. The script skips them.\n\nIf the user isn't running the carrier project, `fsru_sync_check.py` short-circuits to \"skipped \u2014 no carrier backend available\" and logs the FSRU entries for future cross-check.\n\n## Scripts \u2014 what each does and when to read its source\n\n| Script | Purpose | Read source when |\n|---|---|---|\n| `pull_gem_db.py` | Wraps `gem_export_via_web.py`; pulls all-fields CSV and derives the 115-col column-index map | Schema changed; column indices look wrong; auth fails (cookies stale) |\n| `fetch_timeline.py` | Pulls the full status timeline for a UnitID from the live DB UI (export doesn't include timeline history) | UI changed; timeline parse returns nothing for a unit known to have one |\n| `normalize.py` | Canonical country / entity / capacity-unit names (module, imported by others) | Adding new country/entity; cluster matching is over- or under-merging |\n| `dedup_index.py` | Builds project-level and unit-level indexes from the GEM export | New batch type that needs a different index shape |\n| `capacity_normalize.py` | mtpa \u2194 bcm/y \u2194 m\u00b3 LNG storage conversion; range handling; per-train vs total reconciliation | New capacity unit appears in source; conversion factor disputed |\n| `status_timeline.py` | Derives current status from a timeline per the methodology's \"closest non-planned-non-FID to bottom\" rule; validates legal transitions | Methodology updates state machine; anomalous transition observed |\n| `stale_sweep.py` | Computes stale flags per `lifecycle_rules.md` (inferred shelved at 2yr, inferred cancelled at 4yr, etc.) | Methodology revises the year thresholds |\n| `entity_lookup.py` | Queries the GEM entity system to avoid duplicate entity creation | Entity search UI changed; known entity not being found |\n| `url_verifier.py` | HTTP 200 + content check + soft-error detection (paywall stubs, Cloudflare, members-only) | Verifier flags false positives/negatives; new source pattern needs handling |\n| `imo_tracker.py` | IMO \u2192 marinetraffic.org per-vessel URL (FSRU vessel lookup) | marinetraffic.org URL pattern changed; Cloudflare gating |\n| `giignl_extract.py` | Parses GIIGNL report (zip of JPEG + per-page OCR text) into a flat CSV with GEM-aligned columns | New GIIGNL edition layout changed; OCR text quality degrades |\n| `report_diff.py` | Three-way diff (matches / report-only / GEM-only / value-disagreements). Parameterized on report type so the same script serves GIIGNL and (future) IGU | Adding a new reconcilable source; match algorithm over/under-merging |\n| `fsru_sync_check.py` | Cross-check FSRU records between GEM terminals and LNG carrier project backends | Sync conventions change; reassignment detection misfires |\n| `build_review_package.py` | xlsx scaffolding \u2014 sheets, color fills, frozen panes, headers | Adding a new sheet section; changing color convention |\n| `recalc.py` | Open the xlsx, force recalc, return any formula errors | Always run before present_files |\n\nTrust the scripts by default. They're versioned scaffolding, not throwaway code. Read the source when behavior surprises you \u2014 and if you fix something, the user can copy the patched file back into project knowledge so the next batch benefits.\n\n## Output workbook structure\n\nSingle combined xlsx per batch: `/mnt/user-data/outputs/lng_terminals_batch_<YYYYMMDD>.xlsx`.\n\nSheets (empty sheets are omitted from the final workbook):\n\n| Sheet | Populated when | Contents |\n|---|---|---|\n| `README` | Always | Batch parameters, methodology rev cited, what was done, what sheets are present |\n| `updates` | Update workflow | Rows for existing units being updated, with old \u2192 new diffs and citations |\n| `new_terminals` | Discovery workflow | Newly discovered projects (project-level fields) |\n| `new_units` | Discovery or update | Unit-level data for new terminals AND new units within existing terminals (expansions, new trains) |\n| `status_timeline_additions` | Any workflow touching status | Append-only timeline entries to add to the live DB per methodology |\n| `entity_additions` | Any workflow adding owners | New immediate owners/operators/vessel-owners to create, with duplicate-check flags |\n| `giignl_diff` | Reconciliation workflow | Row-level diff against GIIGNL |\n| `giignl_to_action` | Reconciliation workflow | Findings routed to Update or Discovery (with target sheet noted) |\n| `fsru_sync` | Any batch touching FSRUs | Cross-check matches / mismatches / reassignments |\n| `monitor_list` | Discovery workflow | Candidates that don't meet \"sufficient information to add\" threshold |\n| `stale_sweep` | Triage or update | Stale-flag output from `stale_sweep.py` |\n| `country_notes_contributions` | Any batch developing new country knowledge | Drafted additions to GEM's country-resource Google doc, for user to copy over manually |\n| `qa_review` | Always | Per-cell citation log, conflicts, defects, verification log, negative-result log |\n\n## Color conventions (cells in `updates`, `new_units`, `giignl_diff`)\n\nPorted from the carrier project, with one addition:\n\n- **Green** \u2014 high confidence: primary/regulatory source (FERC, DOE, EU PCI portal, national regulator, sponsor IR) OR two independent corroborating sources agreeing on the value\n- **Yellow** \u2014 entity-level confirmation but value implied, contested, or from a single non-primary source\n- **Red** \u2014 single weak source; prefer leaving the cell blank with a `qa_review` log entry\n- **Blue** (terminals-specific) \u2014 value unchanged from existing DB value but re-verified this batch (the methodology's \"no changes\" outcome, applied at cell granularity)\n\nConfidence applies per cell, not per row.\n\n## Hard requirements (these override anything below)\n\n- **Never modify the live GEM database.** Every batch produces a staging xlsx; the user applies edits manually. The agent's edit footprint is exactly zero on the production DB.\n- **Every URL passes the verification gate before going in the xlsx** \u2014 no exceptions, even URLs that worked in prior batches. URLs decay; paywalls change; soft-errors happen.\n- **Pull a fresh GEM CSV at the start of every batch** \u2014 the user (and other GEM staff) edit between batches.\n- **Re-derive the column-index map from the fresh header row** \u2014 don't hard-code offsets, the 115-col schema can drift.\n- **Never auto-apply GIIGNL or IGU values.** A reconciliation finding is a candidate for Update, not an applied edit.\n- **Project-level field changes apply to ALL unit-rows of a multi-unit project.** The export duplicates project-level fields across unit-rows; updates must too, or the next export will show inconsistencies.\n- **No orphan `[ref]` cells** \u2014 never fill a `[ref]` without a paired data value in the same cell-pair (carries over from carrier project Rule F).\n- **Status timeline updates require pulling the existing timeline first** via `fetch_timeline.py` \u2014 the export only has current status + anchor years, not the full ordered timeline.\n- **Don't create duplicate entities.** Run `entity_lookup.py` before staging any new owner/operator/parent. The methodology is emphatic \u2014 entities are shared across all GEM trackers, and duplicates create real cleanup work for the Ownership Team.\n- **Out-of-scope fields are read-only.** LH2, NH3, SyntheticLNG, RetrofitProposed, AltFuelPrelimAgreement, AltFuelCallMarketInterest, AltFuelNotes, PCINotes, PCI3-PCI6 are explicitly \"no longer updated as of 2026\" per the methodology. The build script must NEVER write to these columns.\n\n## When to escalate to the user\n\nPause and ask before proceeding when:\n\n- A whole class of GEM values looks systematically wrong (suggests a schema misunderstanding, not a research finding)\n- A methodology rule and an SOP rule conflict\n- A discovery batch surfaces more than ~5 candidate clusters in the same country (suggests systematic gap \u2014 could be a research priority signal, but worth a conversation before generating 5+ new project records)\n- The \"sufficient information to add\" threshold is genuinely ambiguous on a candidate (sponsor named but extremely vague location, or vice versa)\n- A reconciliation batch finds disagreement on more than ~10% of matched rows (suggests either a GIIGNL methodology change or a systematic GEM issue)\n- An entity that should exist in the GEM entity system isn't found \u2014 could be a search issue, or could be a real gap\n- The GIIGNL report file isn't in the expected format (zip of JPEG + OCR text) \u2014 layout change requires confirming `giignl_extract.py` still works\n- FSRU sync surfaces a reassignment that can't be cleanly resolved (vessel moved to a terminal that doesn't exist in GEM yet)\n"

The workflows are (1) update existing terminals, (2) discover new terminals, (3) reconcile against the annual GIIGNL report, and (4) triage (decide what to work on this batch). Use this skill whenever the user asks for a terminals batch, a GIIGNL diff, a stale-sweep, a discovery run, an FSRU sync check, or any work that produces or modifies the staging xlsx (lng_terminals_batch_YYYYMMDD.xlsx). Also use this skill when the user mentions \\\"the GEM database\\\", \\\"the terminals tracker\\\", \\\"GGIT\\\", \\\"GIIGNL\\\", \\\"the methodology doc\\\", a country-level sweep, an FSRU vessel-to-terminal sync, the status timeline, the entity tree, or any of the standard GEM tools (entity link, ownership tree, wiki, test database). The skill is the executable scaffolding \\u2014 the project's research rules live in GEM's published methodology doc (the \\\"LNG Terminals Manual\\\"), which is authoritative for what counts as a terminal, what the lifecycle states mean, and how units are named. The SOPs in this project are operational \\u2014 they describe how to do the work, citing the methodology rather than restating it.\\n---\\n\\n# LNG Terminals \\u2014 Backend Scaffolding\\n\\n## How this file fits in the project\\n\\nThis is project-knowledge scaffolding for an agentic research workflow that helps a GEM contractor update the Global Gas Infrastructure Tracker's LNG terminals dataset. The user has direct edit access to the live GEM database but does NOT delegate writes to the agent \\u2014 every batch produces a staging xlsx that the user reviews and applies manually.\\n\\nThe project knowledge contains:\\n\\n- **The GEM LNG Terminals Manual** (Google Doc, read into context at session start) \\u2014 the authoritative rules of what to research and how. Sometimes called \\\"the methodology doc.\\\"\\n- **Four SOPs** \\u2014 the operational rules for each workflow:\\n  - `lng_terminal_update_sop.md` \\u2014 update existing terminals (the bread-and-butter of the annual cycle); folds in [ref]-fill work\\n  - `lng_terminal_discovery_sop.md` \\u2014 find new terminals not yet in the database\\n  - `lng_terminal_reconciliation_sop.md` \\u2014 three-way diff against GIIGNL (generic body, GIIGNL-specific appendix; future IGU SOP reuses the body)\\n  - `lng_terminal_triage_sop.md` \\u2014 decide what to work on this batch\\n- **This file** \\u2014 the workflow router\\n- **6 reference docs** (`gem_db_schema.md`, `lifecycle_rules.md`, `source_roster.md`, `entity_canonical_map.md`, `unit_conventions.md`, `country_research_notes.md`, `sop_pointers.md`)\\n- **~10 Python scripts** under `scripts/` \\u2014 the tools\\n\\n### How project knowledge appears in context\\n\\nFiles in claude.ai project knowledge appear as conversation context (loaded in the `<documents>` block at the start of a chat), NOT as files mounted on the bash filesystem. The `<file_path>` tags like `/mnt/project/gem_db_schema.md` are descriptive labels \\u2014 `cat` and `cp` will not find them. Reading via the `view` tool also won't work for these files.\\n\\n**To run the scripts**, materialize them to disk first by writing the content from project context into a working directory:\\n\\n```bash\\nmkdir -p /home/claude/work\\n```\\n\\nThen for each script the workflow needs, use `create_file` (or `cat > path << 'EOF' ... EOF` in bash) to write its content from the project_files context into `/home/claude/work/<script>.py`. After that the scripts can be invoked directly (`cd /home/claude/work && python pull_gem_db.py`).\\n\\nThe reference markdown files don't need materializing \\u2014 read them directly from context whenever the workflow says \\\"see `<file>.md`\\\".\\n\\n### Two exceptions to \\\"everything is in context\\\"\\n\\nTwo artifacts are too large to live in conversation context and need to be fetched at batch start instead:\\n\\n1. **The fresh GEM database export** \\u2014 pulled via `pull_gem_db.py` at the start of every batch. The user maintains session-cookie env vars (see `gem_export_via_web.py`); the script wraps that to also derive the column-index map.\\n2. **The GIIGNL report** \\u2014 when present in the project files (e.g. `/mnt/project/GIIGNL2026AnnualReport*.pdf`), it arrives as a zip of per-page JPEG images + per-page OCR text + a manifest, NOT as a parseable PDF. `giignl_extract.py` reads the OCR text files. Confirm the file shape with `file <path>` before assuming `.pdf` means PDF.\\n\\n## Read the methodology + relevant SOPs first\\n\\nThe methodology doc is authoritative. The SOPs are operational. Before any batch:\\n\\n1. Confirm the methodology doc is in context (it's a long Google Doc \\u2014 if it's not visible, ask the user to re-share). Note its \\\"Last updated\\\" line.\\n2. View the SOPs relevant to the workflow being run (one to three of them, depending on batch type).\\n3. Check `sop_pointers.md` for a quick rule lookup map.\\n4. If an SOP cites a methodology section that no longer exists or has changed, flag to the user before proceeding \\u2014 the methodology is what GEM staff will review your edits against, so the SOPs must stay aligned.\\n\\n## Workflow router\\n\\n### Update existing terminals (most common)\\n\\nTrigger phrases: \\\"update terminals in [country/region]\\\", \\\"refresh the [country] entries\\\", \\\"fill blank refs for terminals X to Y\\\", \\\"annual update for [country]\\\", \\\"check what's stale in [country]\\\", \\\"go through [country] terminals\\\".\\n\\nWorkflow (assuming scripts have been copied to a working directory per the section above):\\n\\n1. `python pull_gem_db.py` \\u2192 fresh CSV at `/home/claude/gem_export.csv`, prints derived column-index map. **Re-derive on every run** \\u2014 the schema can drift between GEM database revisions.\\n2. Confirm batch scope per Update SOP \\u00a72 (which terminals/countries, depth of update, whether [ref]-fill is in scope, whether status updates are in scope).\\n3. `python dedup_index.py` \\u2192 builds project/unit indexes per Update SOP \\u00a73.\\n4. For each terminal in scope:\\n   a. Pull the unit-level timeline from the live DB (`python fetch_timeline.py <UnitID>`) if any status changes are anticipated \\u2014 the export does NOT contain timeline history, only anchor years and current status.\\n   b. Source-search per Update SOP \\u00a74 \\u2014 using `source_roster.md` for tier selection and `country_research_notes.md` for country-specific tips.\\n   c. Apply lifecycle state machine per `lifecycle_rules.md` \\u2014 especially the planned-vs-actual sub-status logic and the \\\"closest non-planned-non-FID status to bottom\\\" rule for deriving current status.\\n   d. For [ref]-fill: identify blank `[ref]` columns paired with **filled** data values (the equivalent of carrier-project Rule F \\u2014 no orphan citations).\\n5. `python url_verifier.py <url> <expected1> <expected2> ...` on every URL before it goes in the xlsx. Or import as a module \\u2014 see the script's docstring.\\n6. `python capacity_normalize.py` on any capacity changes \\u2014 mtpa/bcm/y/m\\u00b3 conversions, range handling per methodology (\\\"record max in spreadsheet, range in wiki Background\\\").\\n7. `python entity_lookup.py \\\"<owner name>\\\" \\\"<country>\\\"` before staging any new owner/operator \\u2014 the methodology is emphatic about not creating duplicate entities.\\n8. **If any FSRU terminal is touched**: `python fsru_sync_check.py` \\u2014 see \\\"FSRU sync rule\\\" below.\\n9. `python build_review_package.py --mode update --batch-id <YYYYMMDD>` \\u2192 `/mnt/user-data/outputs/lng_terminals_batch_<YYYYMMDD>.xlsx`.\\n10. `python recalc.py /mnt/user-data/outputs/lng_terminals_batch_<YYYYMMDD>.xlsx` \\u2192 confirm zero formula errors.\\n11. `present_files`.\\n\\n### Discover new terminals\\n\\nTrigger phrases: \\\"find new terminals in [country/region]\\\", \\\"discovery run\\\", \\\"what's missing from GEM in [region]\\\", \\\"catch-up sweep for [country]\\\", \\\"any new proposals in [region]\\\".\\n\\nWorkflow:\\n\\n1. Confirm parameters per Discovery SOP \\u00a72 (region/country scope, gap window if any, whether to include early-stage proposals that may not meet the \\\"sufficient information to add\\\" threshold from the methodology FAQ).\\n2. `python pull_gem_db.py` \\u2192 fresh CSV; `python dedup_index.py` \\u2192 indexes used for matching candidates against existing records.\\n3. **Country-level regulatory sweep** \\u2014 Discovery SOP \\u00a74 lists per-country regulators (FERC/DOE for US, EU PCI portal + national TSOs for Europe, METI/JOGMEC for Japan, MOTIE for Korea, CNPC/Sinopec/CNOOC IR for China, etc.). Use `country_research_notes.md` to seed the search and contribute findings back.\\n4. **Trade press sweep** \\u2014 per Discovery SOP \\u00a75, using `source_roster.md`. LNG Prime, Reuters, S&P Global Commodity Insights, Argus, Upstream are the workhorses.\\n5. **Sponsor IR sweep** \\u2014 for known LNG developers (Cheniere, Venture Global, TotalEnergies, Sempra, Adnoc Gas, QatarEnergy, Petronas, NLNG, NextDecade, etc.) \\u2014 per Discovery SOP \\u00a76 and `entity_canonical_map.md`.\\n6. For each candidate: apply the \\\"sufficient information to add\\\" threshold from the methodology FAQ (sponsor identified + approximate location + concrete step taken). Candidates that don't meet the threshold go in a `monitor_list` sheet, not `new_terminals`.\\n7. `python url_verifier.py` on all URLs; `python entity_lookup.py` on every new owner/operator/parent.\\n8. **If any candidate is an FSRU**: `python fsru_sync_check.py` against both the GEM terminals and (if available) the LNG carrier project's backend.\\n9. `python build_review_package.py --mode discovery --batch-id <YYYYMMDD>` \\u2192 staging xlsx.\\n10. `python recalc.py`, then `present_files`.\\n\\n### Reconcile against GIIGNL (annual, triggered by report release)\\n\\nTrigger phrases: \\\"reconcile against GIIGNL\\\", \\\"GIIGNL diff\\\", \\\"compare GEM to the new GIIGNL\\\", \\\"process the [year] GIIGNL report\\\".\\n\\nWorkflow:\\n\\n1. Confirm the GIIGNL report is in project files. `file <path>` to confirm format (the 2026 report came as a zip of JPEG + OCR text per page, NOT a parseable PDF). Note the edition year.\\n2. Confirm scope per Reconciliation SOP \\u00a72 (which GIIGNL tables \\u2014 terminal-list, capacity-by-country, country-summary; which lifecycle states to include).\\n3. `python pull_gem_db.py` \\u2192 fresh CSV.\\n4. `python giignl_extract.py /mnt/project/GIIGNL*.pdf --output /home/claude/giignl_normalized.csv` \\u2192 flat CSV with GEM-aligned column names per Reconciliation SOP \\u00a73 (Appendix A for GIIGNL-specific table parsing).\\n5. `python report_diff.py --gem /home/claude/gem_export.csv --report /home/claude/giignl_normalized.csv --output /home/claude/giignl_diff.json` \\u2192 three-way diff (matches, GIIGNL-only, GEM-only, value-disagreements).\\n6. Route findings per Reconciliation SOP \\u00a74:\\n   - GIIGNL-only \\u2192 Discovery workflow (verify candidate is real and in-scope before adding)\\n   - GEM-only \\u2192 log in `giignl_to_action` sheet, usually no action (GIIGNL has known gaps per the methodology FAQ)\\n   - Value-disagreement \\u2192 Update workflow (GIIGNL is one source in a conflict, NOT automatically authoritative \\u2014 the methodology FAQ says a more specific or current source takes priority)\\n   - Match \\u2192 confidence bump on the GEM record\\n7. **DO NOT auto-apply GIIGNL values to the GEM record.** Every value-disagreement requires resolution through the Update workflow's normal source-search and confidence-labeling process.\\n8. `python build_review_package.py --mode reconciliation --report giignl --year <YEAR>` \\u2192 staging xlsx with `giignl_diff` and `giignl_to_action` sheets in addition to the standard sheets.\\n9. `python recalc.py`, then `present_files`.\\n\\n(A future IGU reconciliation SOP will reuse this workflow body with `igu_extract.py` and `--report igu`.)\\n\\n### Triage (decide what to work on this batch)\\n\\nTrigger phrases: \\\"what should we work on this quarter\\\", \\\"what's stale\\\", \\\"plan the [Q1/Q2/Q3/Q4] batch\\\", \\\"where are the gaps\\\", \\\"what hasn't been touched in a while\\\".\\n\\nWorkflow:\\n\\n1. `python pull_gem_db.py` \\u2192 fresh CSV.\\n2. `python stale_sweep.py` \\u2192 for each terminal/unit, compute LastUpdated age and lifecycle-rule-driven flags:\\n   - Proposed/Construction units with LastUpdated > 12 months \\u2192 due for refresh\\n   - Proposed units with no updates > 2 years \\u2192 candidates for inferred shelved (per methodology)\\n   - Shelved units with no updates > 4 years \\u2192 candidates for inferred cancelled (per methodology)\\n   - Operating units with LastUpdated > 18 months \\u2192 due for refresh (lower priority than active development)\\n3. Pull triage inputs per Triage SOP \\u00a73:\\n   - Stale-sweep results (above)\\n   - Recent news scan (last quarter) for activity in countries that haven't been touched recently\\n   - GIIGNL reconciliation backlog (any unprocessed findings from a prior reconciliation batch)\\n   - User priorities (existing GEM team commitments, upcoming publications)\\n   - Whether a fresh GIIGNL/IGU report has dropped since the last reconciliation\\n4. Produce a triage memo (markdown, not xlsx) with recommended batch composition. The user decides scope before any Update or Discovery batch starts.\\n\\n## FSRU sync rule (cross-project)\\n\\nFSRUs are tracked in both the GEM terminals tracker and (if the user is also running it) the LNG carrier project. Each project owns its own fields:\\n\\n| Field type | Owned by | Examples |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| Vessel identity & technical specs | Carriers | IMO, builder, hull, m\\u00b3 LNG capacity, propulsion, delivery year, vessel owner, vessel operator |\\n| Terminal identity & operations | Terminals | Country, port, terminal name, sendout capacity (mtpa/bcm), terminal operator, lifecycle status, location, sponsor |\\n| Linking fields (both records must agree) | Sync rule | Vessel name, IMO |\\n\\n**Sync rule mechanics:**\\n\\n1. When a terminals batch adds or updates an FSRU terminal, the FloatingVesselName + (IMO if known) go in the staging xlsx with a sync-touchpoint flag.\\n2. When a carriers batch updates an FSRU vessel that's deployed, the terminal name + country go in the carrier xlsx with the same flag.\\n3. `fsru_sync_check.py` diffs both backends on (IMO \\u2194 terminal name) pairs and surfaces mismatches. Mismatches go in a `fsru_sync` sheet of whichever xlsx is the current deliverable.\\n4. **Vessel reassignment** (FSRU moves from terminal A to terminal B) is a real and observed pattern \\u2014 at least one terminal in the export has three FSRUs in sequence. The script handles it by modeling: terminal A's prior FSRU gets an \\\"Idled\\\" or \\\"Retired\\\" status timeline entry on the unit-row; terminal B (or a new unit on terminal A) gets the new FSRU. The carrier record's deployment field updates correspondingly.\\n\\nEdge cases:\\n- **FSU / FRU** (floating storage only / floating regas only) \\u2014 same rule applies.\\n- **Deepwater Port LNG terminals** (offshore but not floating) \\u2014 terminals only, no vessel record, no sync needed. The script skips them.\\n\\nIf the user isn't running the carrier project, `fsru_sync_check.py` short-circuits to \\\"skipped \\u2014 no carrier backend available\\\" and logs the FSRU entries for future cross-check.\\n\\n## Scripts \\u2014 what each does and when to read its source\\n\\n| Script | Purpose | Read source when |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| `pull_gem_db.py` | Wraps `gem_export_via_web.py`; pulls all-fields CSV and derives the 115-col column-index map | Schema changed; column indices look wrong; auth fails (cookies stale) |\\n| `fetch_timeline.py` | Pulls the full status timeline for a UnitID from the live DB UI (export doesn't include timeline history) | UI changed; timeline parse returns nothing for a unit known to have one |\\n| `normalize.py` | Canonical country / entity / capacity-unit names (module, imported by others) | Adding new country/entity; cluster matching is over- or under-merging |\\n| `dedup_index.py` | Builds project-level and unit-level indexes from the GEM export | New batch type that needs a different index shape |\\n| `capacity_normalize.py` | mtpa \\u2194 bcm/y \\u2194 m\\u00b3 LNG storage conversion; range handling; per-train vs total reconciliation | New capacity unit appears in source; conversion factor disputed |\\n| `status_timeline.py` | Derives current status from a timeline per the methodology's \\\"closest non-planned-non-FID to bottom\\\" rule; validates legal transitions | Methodology updates state machine; anomalous transition observed |\\n| `stale_sweep.py` | Computes stale flags per `lifecycle_rules.md` (inferred shelved at 2yr, inferred cancelled at 4yr, etc.) | Methodology revises the year thresholds |\\n| `entity_lookup.py` | Queries the GEM entity system to avoid duplicate entity creation | Entity search UI changed; known entity not being found |\\n| `url_verifier.py` | HTTP 200 + content check + soft-error detection (paywall stubs, Cloudflare, members-only) | Verifier flags false positives/negatives; new source pattern needs handling |\\n| `imo_tracker.py` | IMO \\u2192 marinetraffic.org per-vessel URL (FSRU vessel lookup) | marinetraffic.org URL pattern changed; Cloudflare gating |\\n| `giignl_extract.py` | Parses GIIGNL report (zip of JPEG + per-page OCR text) into a flat CSV with GEM-aligned columns | New GIIGNL edition layout changed; OCR text quality degrades |\\n| `report_diff.py` | Three-way diff (matches / report-only / GEM-only / value-disagreements). Parameterized on report type so the same script serves GIIGNL and (future) IGU | Adding a new reconcilable source; match algorithm over/under-merging |\\n| `fsru_sync_check.py` | Cross-check FSRU records between GEM terminals and LNG carrier project backends | Sync conventions change; reassignment detection misfires |\\n| `build_review_package.py` | xlsx scaffolding \\u2014 sheets, color fills, frozen panes, headers | Adding a new sheet section; changing color convention |\\n| `recalc.py` | Open the xlsx, force recalc, return any formula errors | Always run before present_files |\\n\\nTrust the scripts by default. They're versioned scaffolding, not throwaway code. Read the source when behavior surprises you \\u2014 and if you fix something, the user can copy the patched file back into project knowledge so the next batch benefits.\\n\\n## Output workbook       "description": "Draft gem_db_schema.md based on empirical analysis of the 115-col export",
      "file_text": "# GEM Database Schema (LNG Terminals)\n\nReference for the GEM project-database all-fields LNG export. Derived empirically from the 2026-05-26 export (1,263 unit-rows across 859 terminals, 115 columns).\n\nThe authoritative schema source is the live database. This doc captures what the **CSV export** looks like, which is the entry point for all SOPs.\n\n## Pull command\n\n```bash\npython pull_gem_db.py\n```\n\nWraps `gem_export_via_web.py` (uploaded by the user). Requires `GEM_PROJECT_DB_SESSIONID` and `GEM_PROJECT_DB_CSRFTOKEN` env vars set from the user's browser session \u2014 cookies expire periodically, re-export when auth fails. Output at `/home/claude/gem_export.csv` with a sibling `/home/claude/gem_export.colmap.json` containing the derived column-index map.\n\n## Row structure\n\n- **One row per unit.** A multi-unit terminal has one row per unit, with project-level fields duplicated across all unit-rows.\n- **TerminalID** identifies the project (e.g. `T100000130274`).\n- **UnitID** identifies the unit (e.g. `G100002027401`).\n- Unit ordering in the export is not stable batch-to-batch \u2014 re-derive `(TerminalID, UnitName)` keys on every batch.\n\nDistribution of units per terminal (May 2026 export):\n\n| Units | Count |\n|---:|---:|\n| 1 | 645 terminals |\n| 2 | 127 |\n| 3 | 46 |\n| 4 | 20 |\n| 5 | 10 |\n| 6\u201313 | 11 |\n\nAbout 75% of terminals are single-unit; 25% are multi-unit with a long tail. Multi-unit projects matter disproportionately because they're usually larger and more complex export terminals.\n\n## Status timeline is NOT in the export\n\nThis is the single most important schema fact and the methodology doc doesn't make it obvious.\n\nThe export contains:\n- The **current** `Status` and `Substatus`\n- A flat set of **anchor years** (`ProposalYear`, `ConstructionYear`, `OriginalPlannedStartYear`, `LatestPlannedStartYear`, `ActualStartYear`, `ActualStartYear2`, `ActualStartYear3`, `ShelvedYear`, `CancelledYear`, `StopYear`, `PlannedStopYear`, `FIDYear`)\n\nThe export does NOT contain:\n- The ordered status timeline with all historical entries\n- Per-entry notes\n- Part-of-year information (month/quarter/half)\n- Data-entry timestamps for individual entries\n\n**Implication:** any batch that adds or modifies a status timeline entry must pull the existing timeline from the live DB first, via `fetch_timeline.py <UnitID>`. Otherwise, you risk:\n- Appending a duplicate entry that already exists\n- Re-ordering entries unintentionally (the methodology says the timeline is append-only except for genuine error corrections)\n- Losing context that the methodology requires preserving\n\nSee `lifecycle_rules.md` for the rules that derive current status from a timeline.\n\n## Field classification: project-level vs unit-level vs mixed\n\nThe methodology doc treats some fields as \"project-level\" and others as \"unit-level,\" but empirically several fields the manual classifies as project-level vary across units in practice. This matters for the build script: writing a \"project-level\" update to only one unit-row produces an inconsistent next-export.\n\nEmpirical analysis: for each multi-unit terminal (214 of them in the May 2026 export), count what percentage have the same value across all unit-rows. \u226595% = treat as project-level; \u226430% = treat as unit-level; everything in between is mixed.\n\n### Definitely project-level (apply to all unit-rows on edit)\n\nIdentity, location, classification, totals, opposition/CCS flags, and the entire set of \"no longer updated\" fields:\n\n```\nTerminalID, Wiki, TerminalName, Country/Area, Region, SubRegion,\nPrefecture/District, State/Province, Latitude, Longitude, Accuracy,\nLocation, Location [ref],\nOtherNames, LocalNames, Language,\nResearcherNotesProject,\nFuel, ImportExportOnly,\nOffshore, Floating, FloatingVesselName, FloatingVesselName [ref],\nVesselOwner, VesselOwner [ref], VesselParent, VesselOperator, VesselOperator [ref],\nAssociatedTerminals, AssociatedTerminals [ref],\nSource, Source [ref],\nPowerPlantsSupplied, PowerPlantsSupplied [ref],\nCaptiveGasPower, CaptiveGasPower [ref],\nPipelines, Pipelines [ref],\nTotImportLNGTerminalCapacityinMtpa, TotImportLNGTerminalCapacityinBcm/y,\nTotExportLNGTerminalCapacityinMtpa, TotExportLNGTerminalCapacityinBcm/y,\nTotKnownTerminalCostsUSD, TotTerminalCost [ref],\nOpposition, ESJNotes, Defeated, CCS, CCSNotes,\nPCINotes, PCI3, PCI4, PCI5, PCI6,\nLH2, NH3, SyntheticLNG, RetrofitProposed,\nAltFuelPrelimAgreement, AltFuelCallMarketInterest\n```\n\nThe \"Tot\u2026\" totals appear identical across all unit-rows because they're project-wide rollups computed by the GEM backend. **Don't write to these directly** \u2014 they'll be recomputed from unit-level capacity changes.\n\n### Definitely unit-level (apply only to the targeted unit-row)\n\n```\nUnitID, UnitName, Capacity, CapacityinMtpa, CapacityinBcm/y, StartDate [ref]\n```\n\nPlus the timeline-related fields (see \"mixed\" below) which are usually unit-level for multi-phase projects.\n\n### Mixed / context-dependent (the build script must decide per case)\n\nThese are nominally project-level per the manual but vary across unit-rows in real data. Common cause: phases or trains added at different times with different owners, costs, or status histories. The build script should:\n- Read the existing value across all unit-rows of the target project\n- If currently consistent \u2192 apply the change to all unit-rows\n- If currently inconsistent \u2192 apply the change only to the targeted unit-row, flag in `qa_review` for human review\n\n```\nFacilityType, FacilityType [ref]            (91% consistent \u2014 almost always project-level)\nStatus, Substatus, Status [ref]             (47% / 59% / 31% \u2014 clearly unit-level in multi-phase projects)\nResearcher, LastUpdated                     (per-unit by design \u2014 different researchers touch different units)\nResearcherNotesUnit                         (per-unit by design)\nOwner, Owner [ref]                          (82% / 85% \u2014 usually project-level, JV/phase differences exist)\nParent, ParentHQCountry, Parent GEM Entity ID  (85% \u2014 same as Owner)\nCapacityUnits, Capacity [ref]               (82% / 91% \u2014 usually consistent within a project)\nProposalYear, ProposalMonth, ProposalDate [ref]    (53% / 66% / 45% \u2014 different phases proposed at different times)\nConstructionYear, ConstructionMonth, ConstructionDate [ref]   (54% / 66% / 55%)\nOriginalPlannedStartYear, LatestPlannedStartYear   (43% / 43%)\nActualStartYear, ActualStartMonth, ActualStartYear2, ActualStartYear3   (47% / 73% / 97% / \u2014)\nShelvedYear, ShelvedYear [ref], CancelledYear, CancelledYear [ref]   (~88-94%)\nStopYear, StopYear [ref], PlannedStopYear   (83% / 86% / 98%)\nShelvedCancelledStatusType                  (86%)\nCost, CostUnits, CostYear, CostUSD, CostEuro, Cost [ref]   (45-92%)\nFIDStatus, FIDYear, FIDYear [ref]           (81-83%)\nFinancing, Financing [ref]                  (89% / 95%)\nTempFacility                                (99% \u2014 almost always project-level)\n```\n\n`ActualStartYear2` is interesting: 97% consistent suggests it's almost always blank or duplicated, used rarely for unit-specific corrections.\n\n## All 115 columns\n\nIndexed in export order. The \"Klass\" column indicates classification per the analysis above: **P** = project-level, **U** = unit-level, **M** = mixed/context-dependent. The \"Notes\" column flags read-only and out-of-scope fields.\n\n| Idx | Column | Klass | Notes |\n|---:|:---|:---:|:---|\n| 0 | TerminalID | P | Read-only (DB-assigned). `T100000NNNNNN` format. |\n| 1 | UnitID | U | Read-only (DB-assigned). `G100002NNNNNN` format. |\n| 2 | Wiki | P | URL to `gem.wiki/<TerminalName>`. Updated automatically. |\n| 3 | TerminalName | P | See methodology naming conventions. |\n| 4 | UnitName | U | `--` for default; phase / train / expansion name otherwise. |\n| 5 | FacilityType | M | Enum: `import`, `export`. |\n| 6 | FacilityType [ref] | M | |\n| 7 | Fuel | P | Enum: `LNG`, `Oil`, `NGL`, `NH3`, `LH2`, `eLNG`, `Oil+NGL`, `Oil+Fuels`. **Filter to `LNG` for standard work.** |\n| 8 | Status | M | Enum: `proposed`, `construction`, `operating`, `idled`, `mothballed`, `retired`, `shelved`, `cancelled`. |\n| 9 | Substatus | M | Enum: `actual`, `confirmed`, `inferred 2 y`, `inferred 4 y`. Values that don't appear in this catalog should be treated as suspect \u2014 flag in `qa_review` rather than auto-accept.\n\n### Status\n\n`proposed` (290) \u00b7 `construction` (103) \u00b7 `operating` (414) \u00b7 `idled` (10) \u00b7 `mothballed` (16) \u00b7 `retired` (28) \u00b7 `shelved` (98) \u00b7 `cancelled` (303)\n\n(Plus 1 blank row.)\n\n### Substatus (by Status)\n\n- `proposed`: blank (287), `actual` (3)\n- `construction`: `actual` (103)\n- `operating`: `actual` (414)\n- `idled`: `actual` (10)\n- `mothballed`: `actual` (16)\n- `retired`: `actual` (28)\n- `shelved`: `inferred 2 y` (73), `confirmed` (25)\n- `cancelled`: `inferred 4 y` (175), `confirmed` (125), `actual` (3)\n\nThe methodology describes \"actual\" and \"planned\" as sub-statuses, but the export never shows `planned` \u2014 likely because the export only emits the current status, and planned-status entries live only in the timeline. `planned` will appear in timeline data fetched via `fetch_timeline.py`.\n\nThe `inferred 2 y` / `inferred 4 y` values encode the year-threshold rule (2 years for inferred shelved, 4 years for inferred cancelled) directly into the substatus string. `stale_sweep.py` uses these.\n\n### CapacityUnits\n\nFor LNG terminals (Fuel = `LNG`): **use `mtpa` (preferred) or `bcm/y`.**\n\nFull enum seen: `mtpa` \u00b7 `bcm/y` \u00b7 `bpd` \u00b7 `bcf/d` \u00b7 `MMcf/d` \u00b7 `gal/day` \u00b7 `tpa` \u00b7 `MWh/d` \u00b7 `TJ/d`\n\nNon-LNG units (`bpd`, `bcf/d`, `MMcf/d`, etc.) appear on the 51 non-LNG rows (oil, NGL, NH3, LH2, eLNG). If a new value is needed for an LNG terminal, the methodology says to flag Rob/Baird rather than invent a unit.\n\n### FacilityType\n\n`import` (753) \u00b7 `export` (509)\n\n### Fuel\n\nFor standard work: filter to `LNG` (1,212 rows). Other values exist but are out of scope: `Oil` (35), `NGL` (5), `NH3` (6), `LH2` (2), `eLNG` (1), `Oil+NGL` (1), `Oil+Fuels` (1).\n\n### FIDStatus\n\nBlank (1,056) \u00b7 `Pre-FID` (111) \u00b7 `FID` (96)\n\nPer methodology FAQ: only set when there's explicit reporting. Historical \"pre-FID by default\" entries were cleaned in the 2025 cycle.\n\n### ShelvedCancelledStatusType\n\nBlank (842) \u00b7 `inferred` (262) \u00b7 `confirmed` (159)\n\nDenormalized \u2014 duplicates Substatus information. Both should be kept in sync.\n\n### Accuracy\n\n`exact` (594) \u00b7 `approximate` (639)\n\n### Country/Area\n\nFree text but stable. Use ISO country names where possible. Top 15 countries (US, China, Japan, Canada, Australia, Russia, Indonesia, India, Vietnam, Brazil, Nigeria, Mexico, Papua New Guinea, Italy, South Korea) cover ~60% of all units.\n\n### Boolean fields\n\nEncoded as `True` or blank (not `False`). The boolean columns are:\n\n```\nOffshore, Floating, ImportExportOnly, CaptiveGasPower, TempFacility (enum-bool),\nOpposition, Defeated, LH2, NH3, SyntheticLNG, RetrofitProposed,\nAltFuelPrelimAgreement, AltFuelCallMarketInterest, CCS\n```\n\nTo set false, write the empty string, not the literal `False`.\n\n## ID and URL formats\n\n- **TerminalID**: `T100000NNNNNN` (e.g. `T100000130274`)\n- **UnitID**: `G100002NNNNNN` (e.g. `G100002027401`)\n- **Wiki**: `https://www.gem.wiki/<TerminalName_with_underscores>` \u2014 matches the TerminalName per methodology. Updated automatically when TerminalName changes.\n\nThe IDs are assigned by the GEM database backend. Never invent or modify them.\n\n## [ref] columns \u2014 fill priorities\n\n24 [ref] columns paired with data columns. Blank-percentage indicates fill priority (high-blank with high-populated paired data = good [ref]-fill targets).\n\n| [ref] column | % blank | Fill priority |\n|---|---:|---|\n| CaptiveGasPower [ref] | 99.7% | Low \u2014 paired field is essentially unpopulated |\n| TotTerminalCost [ref] | 100% | Skip \u2014 paired field is a computed rollup |\n| AssociatedTerminals [ref] | 95.0% | Low \u2014 paired field also sparse |\n| VesselOperator [ref] | 94.8% | Med \u2014 relevant for FSRU/FLNG only |\n| VesselOwner [ref] | 94.7% | Med \u2014 relevant for FSRU/FLNG only |\n| ShelvedYear [ref] | 93.4% | Med \u2014 relevant when shelved status confirmed |\n| FloatingVesselName [ref] | 92.2% | Med \u2014 FSRU/FLNG only |\n| Financing [ref] | 92.0% | Med \u2014 financing data sparse to begin with |\n| CancelledYear [ref] | 90.5% | Med |\n| Pipelines [ref] | 89.6% | Low |\n| Source [ref] | 89.1% | Low \u2014 refers to gas field source, sparsely populated |\n| PowerPlantsSupplied [ref] |
