\u2014 Start year is densely populated |\n| Status [ref] | 24.4% | **High** \u2014 Status is universal |\n| Owner [ref] | 8.6% | Med \u2014 already mostly populated |\n| Location [ref] | 9.7% | Med \u2014 already mostly populated |\n| FacilityType [ref] | 9.6% | Med \u2014 already mostly populated |\n\n**[ref]-fill targets in order of expected yield: Capacity, ConstructionDate, ProposalDate, Operator, Cost, StartDate, Status.**\n\n## Schema drift detection\n\n`pull_gem_db.py` derives the column-index map from the header row on every pull. If a known column doesn't appear, the script flags it. The expected-column list lives in `pull_gem_db.py`'s `EXPECTED_COLUMNS` dict \u2014 update it when GEM adds or renames a column.\n\nIndicators of meaningful schema drift:\n- New column appears that's not in `EXPECTED_COLUMNS` \u2192 review whether it's a new in-scope field or a backend-only addition\n- A column expected by `EXPECTED_COLUMNS` disappears \u2192 likely renamed; check the live DB edit UI\n- A column's value distribution shifts dramatically (e.g. `Substatus` gains a new enum value) \u2192 may indicate the methodology has changed\n\nBefore running a batch after detected drift, view the live DB unit edit page for one or two units to confirm the schema is what you expect, and update `EXPECTED_COLUMNS` plus this schema doc.\n",

      "json_block": "{\"language\": \"markdown\", \"code\": \"# GEM Database Schema (LNG Terminals)\\n\\nReference for the GEM project-database all-fields LNG export. Derived empirically from the 2026-05-26 export (1,263 unit-rows across 859 terminals, 115 columns).\\n\\nThe authoritative schema source is the live database. This doc captures what the **CSV export** looks like, which is the entry point for all SOPs.\\n\\n## Pull command\\n\\n```bash\\npython pull_gem_db.py\\n```\\n\\nWraps `gem_export_via_web.py` (uploaded by the user). Requires `GEM_PROJECT_DB_SESSIONID` and `GEM_PROJECT_DB_CSRFTOKEN` env vars set from the user's browser session \\u2014 cookies expire periodically, re-export when auth fails. Output at `/home/claude/gem_export.csv` with a sibling `/home/claude/gem_export.colmap.json` containing the derived column-index map.\\n\\n## Row structure\\n\\n- **One row per unit.** A multi-unit terminal has one row per unit, with project-level fields duplicated across all unit-rows.\\n- **TerminalID** identifies the project (e.g. `T100000130274`).\\n- **UnitID** identifies the unit (e.g. `G100002027401`).\\n- Unit ordering in the export is not stable batch-to-batch \\u2014 re-derive `(TerminalID, UnitName)` keys on every batch.\\n\\nDistribution of units per terminal (May 2026 export):\\n\\n| Units | Count |\\n|---:|---:|\\n| 1 | 645 terminals |\\n| 2 | 127 |\\n| 3 | 46 |\\n| 4 | 20 |\\n| 5 | 10 |\\n| 6\\u201313 | 11 |\\n\\nAbout 75% of terminals are single-unit; 25% are multi-unit with a long tail. Multi-unit projects matter disproportionately because they're usually larger and more complex export terminals.\\n\\n## Status timeline is NOT in the export\\n\\nThis is the single most important schema fact and the methodology doc doesn't make it obvious.\\n\\nThe export contains:\\n- The **current** `Status` and `Substatus`\\n- A flat set of **anchor years** (`ProposalYear`, `ConstructionYear`, `OriginalPlannedStartYear`, `LatestPlannedStartYear`, `ActualStartYear`, `ActualStartYear2`, `ActualStartYear3`, `ShelvedYear`, `CancelledYear`, `StopYear`, `PlannedStopYear`, `FIDYear`)\\n\\nThe export does NOT contain:\\n- The ordered status timeline with all historical entries\\n- Per-entry notes\\n- Part-of-year information (month/quarter/half)\\n- Data-entry timestamps for individual entries\\n\\n**Implication:** any batch that adds or modifies a status timeline entry must pull the existing timeline from the live DB first, via `fetch_timeline.py <UnitID>`. Otherwise, you risk:\\n- Appending a duplicate entry that already exists\\n- Re-ordering entries unintentionally (the methodology says the timeline is append-only except for genuine error corrections)\\n- Losing context that the methodology requires preserving\\n\\nSee `lifecycle_rules.md` for the rules that derive current status from a timeline.\\n\\n## Field classification: project-level vs unit-level vs mixed\\n\\nThe methodology doc treats some fields as \\\"project-level\\\" and others as \\\"unit-level,\\\" but empirically several fields the manual classifies as project-level vary across units in practice. This matters for the build script: writing a \\\"project-level\\\" update to only one unit-row produces an inconsistent next-export.\\n\\nEmpirical analysis: for each multi-unit terminal (214 of them in the May 2026 export), count what percentage have the same value across all unit-rows. \\u226595% = treat as project-level; \\u226430% = treat as unit-level; everything in between is mixed.\\n\\n### Definitely project-level (apply to all unit-rows on edit)\\n\\nIdentity, location, classification, totals, opposition/CCS flags, and the entire set of \\\"no longer updated\\\" fields:\\n\\n```\\nTerminalID, Wiki, TerminalName, Country/Area, Region, SubRegion,\\nPrefecture/District, State/Province, Latitude, Longitude, Accuracy,\\nLocation, Location [ref],\\nOtherNames, LocalNames, Language,\\nResearcherNotesProject,\\nFuel, ImportExportOnly,\\nOffshore, Floating, FloatingVesselName, FloatingVesselName [ref],\\nVesselOwner, VesselOwner [ref], VesselParent, VesselOperator, VesselOperator [ref],\\nAssociatedTerminals, AssociatedTerminals [ref],\\nSource, Source [ref],\\nPowerPlantsSupplied, PowerPlantsSupplied [ref],\\nCaptiveGasPower, CaptiveGasPower [ref],\\nPipelines, Pipelines [ref],\\nTotImportLNGTerminalCapacityinMtpa, TotImportLNGTerminalCapacityinBcm/y,\\nTotExportLNGTerminalCapacityinMtpa, TotExportLNGTerminalCapacityinBcm/y,\\nTotKnownTerminalCostsUSD, TotTerminalCost [ref],\\nOpposition, ESJNotes, Defeated, CCS, CCSNotes,\\nPCINotes, PCI3, PCI4, PCI5, PCI6,\\nLH2, NH3, SyntheticLNG, RetrofitProposed,\\nAltFuelPrelimAgreement, AltFuelCallMarketInterest\\n```\\n\\nThe \\\"Tot\\u2026\\\" totals appear identical across all unit-rows because they're project-wide rollups computed by the GEM backend. **Don't write to these directly** \\u2014 they'll be recomputed from unit-level capacity changes.\\n\\n### Definitely unit-level (apply only to the targeted unit-row)\\n\\n```\\nUnitID, UnitName, Capacity, CapacityinMtpa, CapacityinBcm/y, StartDate [ref]\\n```\\n\\nPlus the timeline-related fields (see \\\"mixed\\\" below) which are usually unit-level for multi-phase projects.\\n\\n### Mixed / context-dependent (the build script must decide per case)\\n\\nThese are nominally project-level per the manual but vary across unit-rows in real data. Common cause: phases or trains added at different times with different owners, costs, or status histories. The build script should:\\n- Read the existing value across all unit-rows of the target project\\n- If currently consistent \\u2192 apply the change to all unit-rows\\n- If currently inconsistent \\u2192 apply the change only to the targeted unit-row, flag in `qa_review` for human review\\n\\n```\\nFacilityType, FacilityType [ref]            (91% consistent \\u2014 almost always project-level)\\nStatus, Substatus, Status [ref]             (47% / 59% / 31% \\u2014 clearly unit-level in multi-phase projects)\\nResearcher, LastUpdated                     (per-unit by design \\u2014 different researchers touch different units)\\nResearcherNotesUnit                         (per-unit by design)\\nOwner, Owner [ref]                          (82% / 85% \\u2014 usually project-level, JV/phase differences exist)\\nParent, ParentHQCountry, Parent GEM Entity ID  (85% \\u2014 same as Owner)\\nCapacityUnits, Capacity [ref]               (82% / 91% \\u2014 usually consistent within a project)\\nProposalYear, ProposalMonth, ProposalDate [ref]    (53% / 66% / 45% \\u2014 different phases proposed at different times)\\nConstructionYear, ConstructionMonth, ConstructionDate [ref]   (54% / 66% / 55%)\\nOriginalPlannedStartYear, LatestPlannedStartYear   (43% / 43%)\\nActualStartYear, ActualStartMonth, ActualStartYear2, ActualStartYear3   (47% / 73% / 97% / \\u2014)\\nShelvedYear, ShelvedYear [ref], CancelledYear, CancelledYear [ref]   (~88-94%)\\nStopYear, StopYear [ref], PlannedStopYear   (83% / 86% / 98%)\\nShelvedCancelledStatusType duplicated, used rarely for unit-specific corrections.\\n\\n## All 115 columns\\n\\nIndexed in export order. The \\\"Klass\\\" column indicates classification per the analysis above: **P** = project-level, **U** = unit-level, **M** = mixed/context-dependent. Values that don't appear in this catalog should be treated as suspect \\u2014 flag in `qa_review` rather than auto-accept.\\n\\n### Status\\n\\n`proposed` (290) \\u00b7 `construction` (103) \\u00b7 `operating` (414) \\u00b7 `idled` (10) \\u00b7 `mothballed` (16) \\u00b7 `retired` (28) \\u00b7 `shelved` (98) \\u00b7 `cancelled` (303)\\n\\n(Plus 1 blank row.)\\n\\n### Substatus (by Status)\\n\\n- `proposed`: blank (287), `actual` (3)\\n- `construction`: `actual` (103)\\n- `operating`: `actual` (414)\\n- `idled`: `actual` (10)\\n- `mothballed`: `actual` (16)\\n- `retired`: `actual` (28)\\n- `shelved`: `inferred 2 y` (73), `confirmed` (25)\\n- `cancelled`: `inferred 4 y` (175), `confirmed` (125), `actual` (3)\\n\\nThe methodology describes \\\"actual\\\" and \\\"planned\\\" as sub-statuses, but the export never shows `planned` \\u2014 likely because the export only emits the current status, and planned-status entries live only in the timeline. `planned` will appear in timeline data fetched via `fetch_timeline.py`.\\n\\nThe `inferred 2 y` / `inferred 4 y` values encode the year-threshold rule (2 years for inferred shelved, 4 years for inferred cancelled) directly into the substatus string. `stale_sweep.py` uses these.\\n\\n### CapacityUnits\\n\\nFor LNG terminals (Fuel = `LNG`): **use `mtpa` (preferred) or `bcm/y`.**\\n\\nFull enum seen: `mtpa` \\u00b7 `bcm/y` \\u00b7 `bpd` \\u00b7 `bcf/d` \\u00b7 `MMcf/d` \\u00b7 `gal/day` \\u00b7 `tpa` \\u00b7 `MWh/d` \\u00b7 `TJ/d`\\n\\nNon-LNG units (`bpd`, `bcf/d`, `MMcf/d`, etc.) appear on the 51 non-LNG rows (oil, NGL, NH3, LH2, eLNG). If a new value is needed for an LNG terminal, the methodology says to flag Rob/Baird rather than invent a unit.\\n\\n### FacilityType\\n\\n`import` (753) \\u00b7 `export` (509)\\n\\n### Fuel\\n\\nFor standard work: filter to `LNG` (1,212 rows). Other values exist but are out of scope: `Oil` (35), `NGL` (5), `NH3` (6), `LH2` (2), `eLNG` (1), `Oil+NGL` (1), `Oil+Fuels` (1).\\n\\n### FIDStatus\\n\\nBlank (1,056) \\u00b7 `Pre-FID` (111) \\u00b7 `FID` (96)\\n\\nPer methodology FAQ: only set when there's explicit reporting. Historical \\\"pre-FID by default\\\" entries were cleaned in the 2025 cycle.\\n\\n### ShelvedCancelledStatusType\\n\\nBlank (842) \\u00b7 `inferred` (262) \\u00b7 `confirmed` (159)\\n\\nDenormalized \\u2014 duplicates Substatus information. Both should be kept in sync.\\n\\n### Accuracy\\n\\n`exact` (594) \\u00b7 `approximate` (639)\\n\\n### Country/Area\\n\\nFree text but stable. Use ISO country names where possible. Top 15 countries (US, China, Japan, Canada, Australia, Russia, Indonesia, India, Vietnam, Brazil, Nigeria, Mexico, Papua New Guinea, Italy, South Korea) cover ~60% of all units.\\n\\n### Boolean fields\\n\\nEncoded as `True` or blank (not `False`). The boolean columns are:\\n\\n```\\nOffshore, Floating, ImportExportOnly, CaptiveGasPower, TempFacility (enum-bool),\\nOpposition, Defeated, LH2, NH3, SyntheticLNG, RetrofitProposed,\\nAltFuelPrelimAgreement, AltFuelCallMarketInterest, CCS\\n```\\n\\nTo set false, write the empty string, not the literal `False`.\\n\\n## ID and URL formats\\n\\n- **TerminalID**: `T100000NNNNNN` (e.g. `T100000130274`)\\n- **UnitID**: `G100002NNNNNN` (e.g. `G100002027401`)\\n- **Wiki**: `https://www.gem.wiki/<TerminalName_with_underscores>` \\u2014 matches the TerminalName per methodology. Updated automatically when TerminalName changes.\\n\\nThe IDs are assigned by the GEM database backend. Never invent or modify them.\\n\\n## [ref] columns \\u2014 fill priorities\\n\\n24 [ref] columns paired with data columns. of expected yield: Capacity, ConstructionDate, ProposalDate, Operator, Cost, StartDate, Status.**\\n\\n## Schema drift detection\\n\\n`pull_gem_db.py` derives the column-index map from the header row on every pull. If a known column doesn't appear, the script flags it. The expected-column list lives in `pull_gem_db.py`'s `EXPECTED_COLUMNS` dict \\u2014 update it when GEM adds or renames a column.\\n\\nIndicators of meaningful schema drift:\\n- New column appears that's not in `EXPECTED_COLUMNS` \\u2192 review whether it's a new in-scope field or a backend-only addition\\n- A column expected by `EXPECTED_COLUMNS` disappears \\u2192 likely renamed; check the live DB edit UI\\n- A column's value distribution shifts dramatically (e.g. `Substatus` gains a new enum value) \\u2192 may indicate the methodology has changed\\n\\nBefore running a batch after detected drift, view the live DB unit edit page for one or two units to confirm the schema is what you expect, and update `EXPECTED_COLUMNS` plus this schema doc.\\n\", \"filename\": \"/home/claude/work/gem_db_schema.md\"}"

    "input": {
      "description": "Draft lifecycle_rules.md \u2014 the status state machine and timeline derivation rules",
      "file_text": "# Lifecycle Rules \u2014 Status Timeline State Machine\n\nThe rules for how a GEM LNG terminal unit moves between lifecycle states, how the timeline is constructed and read, and how current status is derived from a timeline. This file is operational scaffolding; the methodology doc is the authoritative source. Where this file and the methodology disagree, the methodology wins and this file gets updated.\n\n## The eight statuses\n\nPer the methodology, every LNG unit has exactly one current status drawn from this set:\n\n| Status | Meaning | Substatus options |\n|---|---|---|\n| `proposed` | Announced or in pre-construction development | (blank), `actual` (rare) |\n| `construction` | Site prep or active building underway | `actual` |\n| `operating` | Commissioned or in commercial operation | `actual` |\n| `idled` | Operated once, now sitting unused (typically short-term) | `actual` |\n| `mothballed` | Formally taken offline, not yet retired | `actual` |\n| `retired` | Permanently taken out of operation | `actual` |\n| `shelved` | Sponsor publicly paused, OR no updates for 2-4 years | `confirmed`, `inferred 2 y` |\n| `cancelled` | Sponsor publicly cancelled, OR no updates for 4+ years | `confirmed`, `inferred 4 y`, `actual` (rare) |\n\n**`FID` is not a status.** It's a milestone that lives in the timeline as a separate entry type with its own substatus (`actual` or `planned`).\n\n### Substatus semantics\n\nSubstatus has two distinct meanings depending on Status:\n\n1. **Active statuses** (`construction`, `operating`, `idled`, `mothballed`, `retired`) plus `FID`: `actual` vs `planned`. The export only ever emits `actual` because it shows current status; `planned` entries live in the timeline.\n2. **Dormancy statuses** (`shelved`, `cancelled`): `confirmed` vs `inferred 2 y` / `inferred 4 y`. Confirmed = the sponsor announced the pause/cancellation. Inferred = no updates for the threshold period.\n\n`proposed` has no substatus (blank); the rare `proposed` + `actual` cases are likely data-entry artifacts and should be flagged in `qa_review`.\n\n## The timeline model\n\nA unit's status timeline is an **ordered list of entries**, each with:\n\n- `status` \u2014 one of the eight statuses, or `FID`\n- `sub_status` \u2014 `actual` / `planned` / `confirmed` / `inferred 2 y` / `inferred 4 y` / blank\n- `year` \u2014 4-digit year\n- `part_of_year` \u2014 month, quarter, half, or blank\n- `notes` \u2014 free text, optional\n- (hidden) `data_entry_timestamp` \u2014 when the entry was added\n\n**The timeline is append-only.** New developments add new entries; they do NOT modify or delete prior entries. The only exception per the methodology FAQ is correcting genuine errors in past entries.\n\n**Ordering is by stage of development**, not by `data_entry_timestamp`. Researchers can drag-and-drop to re-order. New planned entries usually go after their corresponding actual milestone; new actuals appended to the bottom.\n\n### Why ordering matters\n\nThe current status of a unit is derived as: **the status closest to the bottom of the timeline, excluding entries with substatus `planned` and excluding `FID` entries.**\n\nA worked example from the methodology:\n\n```\nProposed (2023)\nConstruction (planned, 2025)\nOperating (planned, 2026)\nConstruction (actual, 2025)\nFID (actual, 2025)\nOperating (planned, 2027)\n```\n\nCurrent status = `construction` (the only non-planned non-FID entry below the proposal). Future revisions (e.g. operation actually starts in 2027) append a new `Operating (actual, 2027)` entry at the bottom, which then becomes the current status.\n\n## Anchor years vs timeline (the export gap)\n\n**The CSV export does NOT contain the timeline.** It contains:\n\n- The current status and substatus (one each, current value)\n- Eleven \"anchor year\" columns that flatten the most important year values:\n  - `ProposalYear`, `ProposalMonth` \u2014 earliest proposed entry's year\n  - `ConstructionYear`, `ConstructionMonth` \u2014 first construction (actual) entry's year\n  - `OriginalPlannedStartYear` \u2014 first operating (planned) entry's year\n  - `LatestPlannedStartYear` \u2014 most recent operating (planned) entry's year\n  - `ActualStartYear`, `ActualStartMonth` \u2014 first operating (actual) entry's year\n  - `ActualStartYear2`, `ActualStartYear3` \u2014 used for restarts after idling (rare)\n  - `ShelvedYear` \u2014 shelved entry's year\n  - `CancelledYear` \u2014 cancelled entry's year\n  - `StopYear` \u2014 when operation stopped (any of idled, mothballed, retired); `PlannedStopYear` for planned\n  - `FIDYear` \u2014 FID entry's year (`actual` or `planned`, see ambiguity note below)\n\n**Implication for all SOPs:** any status timeline change requires pulling the existing timeline first with `fetch_timeline.py <UnitID>`. The export alone cannot tell you:\n- Whether a status transition was previously recorded as planned\n- The order of entries\n- Per-entry notes\n- The data-entry timestamps\n\nWorking blind from the export risks duplicate entries, incorrect ordering, and lost methodology-required context.\n\n## Legal state transitions\n\nThe methodology doesn't explicitly enumerate legal transitions, but reading the status definitions in order yields the following graph. The build script and `status_timeline.py` use this for validation.\n\n```\nproposed \u2500\u252c\u2500\u2192 construction \u2500\u2192 operating \u2500\u252c\u2500\u2192 idled \u2500\u252c\u2500\u2192 operating  (restart)\n          \u2502                               \u2502          \u251c\u2500\u2192 mothballed\n          \u2502                               \u2502          \u2514\u2500\u2192 retired\n          \u251c\u2500\u2192 shelved \u2500\u2192 cancelled        \u251c\u2500\u2192 mothballed \u2500\u2192 retired\n          \u2514\u2500\u2192 cancelled                   \u2514\u2500\u2192 retired\n                                          \u2502\n                                          (very rarely: \u2192 shelved or cancelled\n                                           if a project is abandoned mid-operation;\n                                           see \"Edge cases\" below)\n\nproposed \u2190\u2500 (no transition from any other state to proposed under normal rules;\n             see \"Dead-and-revived\" edge case below)\n```\n\n### Strict transitions\n\n- `proposed` can transition to: `construction`, `shelved`, `cancelled`\n- `construction` can transition to: `operating`, `shelved` (rare \u2014 methodology: \"shelved if entered construction but never went operating\")\n- `operating` can transition to: `idled`, `mothballed`, `retired`\n- `idled` can transition to: `operating`, `mothballed`, `retired`\n- `mothballed` can transition to: `operating` (rare), `retired`\n- `retired` is terminal (no outbound transitions)\n- `shelved` can transition to: `cancelled` (either confirmed or inferred), `construction` (rare revival), `operating` (very rare)\n- `cancelled` is normally terminal, but see \"Dead-and-revived\" below\n\n### Forbidden transitions (flag in `qa_review`)\n\n- Any transition INTO `proposed` from another active state \u2014 proposed projects that revive are usually a new unit (see \"Dead-and-revived\")\n- `retired` \u2192 anything (retirement is permanent per the methodology)\n- Any direct `construction` \u2192 `retired` skipping `operating`\n- Any direct `operating` \u2192 `cancelled` (operating projects that stop get `idled`/`mothballed`/`retired`, not `cancelled`)\n\n## Anchor year invariants\n\nYear values must be consistent with each other and with the current status. The build script enforces these on write; `stale_sweep.py` flags violations on read.\n\nFor any unit:\n\n- `ProposalYear \u2264 ConstructionYear \u2264 ActualStartYear` when all three are populated\n- `ConstructionYear \u2264 LatestPlannedStartYear` when both are populated\n- `ActualStartYear \u2264 StopYear` when both are populated\n- `OriginalPlannedStartYear \u2264 LatestPlannedStartYear` (the latest planned should not be earlier than the original)\n- `ShelvedYear \u2264 CancelledYear` when both are populated (a project shelved before cancellation)\n\nBy current status:\n\n- **`proposed`**: `ProposalYear` should be populated. `ConstructionYear`, `ActualStartYear`, `ShelvedYear`, `CancelledYear`, `StopYear` should be blank.\n- **`construction`**: `ProposalYear` and `ConstructionYear` should be populated. `ActualStartYear`, `ShelvedYear`, `CancelledYear`, `StopYear` should be blank.\n- **`operating`**: `ActualStartYear` should be populated. `ShelvedYear`, `CancelledYear`, `StopYear` should be blank.\n- **`idled` / `mothballed` / `retired`**: `ActualStartYear` and `StopYear` should be populated. `ShelvedYear`, `CancelledYear` should be blank.\n- **`shelved`**: `ShelvedYear` should be populated. `CancelledYear`, `StopYear` should be blank (unless the project was operating before being shelved, which is rare).\n- **`cancelled`**: `CancelledYear` should be populated.\n\n### Reality check: invariants are violated in the existing data\n\nThe May 2026 export reveals that \"should be populated\" is aspirational, not enforced:\n\n- 28 `operating` units have no `ActualStartYear`\n- 48 `proposed` units have no `ProposalYear`\n- 29 `cancelled` units have no `CancelledYear`\n- 10 `shelved` units have no `ShelvedYear`\n- 3 `construction` units have no `ConstructionYear`\n\nThese are not bugs in the database \u2014 they're historical records where the anchor year wasn't captured during data entry. **Treat invariant violations as `qa_review` flags, not as hard errors that block a batch.** Backfilling a missing anchor year is a legitimate update.\n\n### FIDStatus / FIDYear ambiguity\n\n`FIDStatus=Pre-FID` with `FIDYear` populated appears 87 times in the export. The methodology says FIDYear should be set only with explicit reporting of an actual FID, so `Pre-FID` + populated `FIDYear` is ambiguous. Most likely meaning: \"year of expected/planned FID.\" When updating these units:\n\n- If the sponsor has since taken FID, update to `FIDStatus=FID` with the actual year\n- If the planned FID year has passed without FID, leave the FIDStatus alone but flag in `qa_review` \u2014 a project that missed its planned FID is a candidate for stale-sweep\n- Never *set* a `Pre-FID` + `FIDYear` combination on a new entry; it's only acceptable as a legacy state\n\n## Dormancy thresholds (the stale-sweep rules)\n\nPer the methodology:\n\n- A `proposed`, `construction`, `idled`, or `mothballed` unit with no project updates for **2 years** \u2192 candidate for `inferred shelved`\n- A `shelved` (`confirmed` or `inferred 2 y`) unit with no project updates for **2 more years** (4 years total since last activity) \u2192 candidate for `inferred cancelled`\n\nThe \"no updates\" clock starts from the most recent of: the last status timeline entry's year, or the LastUpdated field on the unit (whichever is more recent and trustworthy). `stale_sweep.py` uses `LastUpdated` as the primary signal because it's mechanically tractable.\n\n### Adding an inferred entry\n\nWhen `stale_sweep.py` flags a unit:\n\n1. Pull the existing timeline with `fetch_timeline.py`\n2. Confirm via research that there really are no recent updates (sometimes a unit is stale because of researcher capacity, not because the project is dormant \u2014 a quick news search resolves this)\n3. If genuinely dormant, append a new timeline entry:\n   - Status: `shelved` or `cancelled`\n   - Substatus: `inferred 2 y` or `inferred 4 y`\n   - Year: the current year (the year the inference is being made)\n   - Notes: a brief explanation including the \"last known activity\" date\n   - Datasource: per the methodology FAQ, the datasource for `inferred shelved` and the subsequent `inferred cancelled` can be the same source \u2014 the one originally cited for the latest active-status entry\n\n### Shelved \u2192 Cancelled escalation\n\nThe methodology FAQ specifically permits: a unit confirmed `shelved` with no updates for 2+ more years can be labeled `confirmed cancelled` (not `inferred`) using the same source. This is a deliberate departure from the literal \"inferred from time\" rule \u2014 the project is treated as confirmed cancelled because the prior confirmed-shelved status carries forward the sponsor intent.\n\n## Edge cases\n\n### Dead-and-revived proposal\n\nA previously cancelled or shelved proposal re-emerges. Per the methodology FAQ:\n\n- **Same fundamental proposal** (same sponsor, same site, same approximate design): re-use the existing unit. Add a new `proposed` entry to the timeline. Do NOT delete the prior cancelled/shelved entries.\n- **Significantly different proposal** (different sponsor, different design, even if same site): create a new unit. The old unit stays cancelled.\n\nThis is one of the few cases where `proposed` is a valid transition destination in the timeline (though only as a new entry appended to a timeline that may already contain a later `cancelled`).\n\n### Project shelved during construction\n\nThe methodology explicitly notes: \"A project is also shelved if it has entered construction but never formally goes into operation.\" So `construction` \u2192 `shelved` is legal even though it's unusual. Example given: Nord Stream 2 (a pipeline, not LNG, but illustrative).\n\n### Project with multiple operating start dates\n\nSome units restart after a period of idling \u2014 captured in `ActualStartYear2` and `ActualStartYear3`. Only 3 units use `ActualStartYear2` and 0 use `ActualStartYear3` in the current export, so this is rare but real. The timeline gets a new `operating (actual, YYYY)` entry; the `ActualStartYear2` field gets updated; `StopYear` should remain populated from the prior stop.\n\n### FID without project status change\n\nTaking FID does not change the unit's Status \u2014 a unit can be `construction` and have `FIDStatus=FID` with `FIDYear` set, but Status stays `construction` (or whatever it was). FID is recorded as a separate timeline entry but doesn't affect status derivation.\n\n### Multi-unit project with units at different statuses\n\nEach unit has its own status timeline. A project may have:\n- Train 1: `operating`\n- Train 2: `construction`\n- Train 3: `proposed`\n- Train 4: `cancelled`\n\nThis is normal. The project-level rollups (`TotImportLNGTerminalCapacityinMtpa` etc.) summarize operating capacity differently from total proposed-or-greater capacity \u2014 the build script doesn't compute these (they're read-only DB-side), but staging xlsx outputs should make per-unit status differences visible in the `updates` sheet.\n\n### Operating unit that's part of a permanent-replacement scheme\n\nPer the methodology, the `TempFacility` field marks units as `interim` or `permanent replacement`. Lifecycle handling:\n- The interim FSRU usually goes through `operating` \u2192 `idled` \u2192 `retired` as the permanent terminal commissions\n- The permanent terminal follows the normal `proposed` \u2192 `construction` \u2192 `operating` arc\n- Both units share an `AssociatedTerminals` link; the FSRU sync rule may apply if the interim is an FSRU vessel\n\n## How the build script uses these rules\n\nEvery status change staged to the xlsx goes through `status_timeline.py`, which validates:\n\n1. The proposed new entry is a legal transition from the prior current status\n2. Anchor year invariants will not be violated after the entry is applied\n3. If substatus is `inferred 2 y` or `inferred 4 y`, the timeline genuinely supports the inference (no recent active entries)\n4. If status is `cancelled` and substatus is `confirmed` via the shelved\u2192cancelled escalation, the prior `shelved` entry exists in the timeline\n\nFailures \u2192 the entry is staged with a warning in `qa_review`, but not blocked. Human review at xlsx-application time makes the final call. The script is a guardrail, not a gate.\n\n## Quick-reference card\n\nFor day-of-batch consultation without re-reading this whole file:\n\n| If you're doing... | Read this section |\n|---|---|\n| Adding a new proposed unit | \"The eight statuses\" + \"Anchor year invariants\" \u2192 proposed row |\n| Confirming a status change (e.g. proposed \u2192 construction) | \"Legal state transitions\" |\n| Adding an inferred shelved/cancelled | \"Dormancy thresholds\" |\n| Resolving a dead-and-revived case | \"Edge cases\" \u2192 first bullet |\n| FID milestone update | \"Substatus semantics\" + \"FIDStatus/FIDYear ambiguity\" |\n| FSRU vessel swap-out on a terminal | \"Edge cases\" \u2192 permanent-replacement scheme + the FSRU sync rule in SKILL.md |\n| Multi-unit project with mixed statuses | \"Edge cases\" \u2192 multi-unit |\n",

      "json_block": "{\"language\": \"markdown\", \"code\": \"# Lifecycle Rules \\u2014 Status Timeline State Machine\\n\\nThe rules for how a GEM LNG terminal unit moves between lifecycle states, how the timeline is constructed and read, and how current status is derived from a timeline. This file is operational scaffolding; the methodology doc is the authoritative source. Where this file and the methodology disagree, the methodology wins and this file gets updated.\\n\\n## The eight statuses\\n\\nPer the methodology, every LNG unit has exactly one current status drawn from this set:\\n\\n| Status | Meaning | Substatus options |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| `proposed` | Announced or in pre-construction development | (blank), `actual` (rare) |\\n| `construction` | Site prep or active building underway | `actual` |\\n| `operating` | Commissioned or in commercial operation | `actual` |\\n| `idled` | Operated once, now sitting unused (typically short-term) | `actual` |\\n| `mothballed` | Formally taken offline, not yet retired | `actual` |\\n| `retired` | Permanently taken out of operation | `actual` |\\n| `shelved` | Sponsor publicly paused, OR no updates for 2-4 years | `confirmed`, `inferred 2 y` |\\n| `cancelled` | Sponsor publicly cancelled, OR no updates for 4+ years | `confirmed`, `inferred 4 y`, `actual` (rare) |\\n\\n**`FID` is not a status.** It's a milestone that lives in the timeline as a separate entry type with its own substatus (`actual` or `planned`).\\n\\n### Substatus semantics\\n\\nSubstatus has two distinct meanings depending on Status:\\n\\n1. **Active statuses** (`construction`, `operating`, `idled`, `mothballed`, `retired`) plus `FID`: `actual` vs `planned`. The export only ever emits `actual` because it shows current status; `planned` entries live in the timeline.\\n2. **Dormancy statuses** (`shelved`, `cancelled`): `confirmed` vs `inferred 2 y` / `inferred 4 y`. Confirmed = the sponsor announced the pause/cancellation. Inferred = no updates for the threshold period.\\n\\n`proposed` has no substatus (blank); the rare `proposed` + `actual` cases are likely data-entry artifacts and should be flagged in `qa_review`.\\n\\n## The timeline model\\n\\nA unit's status timeline is an **ordered list of entries**, each with:\\n\\n- `status` \\u2014 one of the eight statuses, or `FID`\\n- `sub_status` \\u2014 `actual` / `planned` / `confirmed` / `inferred 2 y` / `inferred 4 y` / blank\\n- `year` \\u2014 4-digit year\\n- `part_of_year` \\u2014 month, quarter, half, or blank\\n- `notes` \\u2014 free text, optional\\n- (hidden) `data_entry_timestamp` \\u2014 when the entry was added\\n\\n**The timeline is append-only.** New developments add new entries; they do NOT modify or delete prior entries. The only exception per the methodology FAQ is correcting genuine errors in past entries.\\n\\n**Ordering is by stage of development**, not by `data_entry_timestamp`. Researchers can drag-and-drop to re-order. New planned entries usually go after their corresponding actual milestone; new actuals appended to the bottom.\\n\\n### Why ordering matters\\n\\nThe current status of a unit is derived as: **the status closest to the bottom of the timeline, excluding entries with substatus `planned` and excluding `FID` entries.**\\n\\nA worked example from the methodology:\\n\\n```\\nProposed (2023)\\nConstruction (planned, 2025)\\nOperating (planned, 2026)\\nConstruction (actual, 2025)\\nFID (actual, 2025)\\nOperating (planned, 2027)\\n```\\n\\nCurrent status = `construction` (the only non-planned non-FID entry below the proposal). Future revisions (e.g. operation actually starts in 2027) append a new `Operating (actual, 2027)` entry at the bottom, which then becomes the current status.\\n\\n## Anchor years vs timeline (the export gap)\\n\\n**The CSV export does NOT contain the timeline.** It contains:\\n\\n- The current status and substatus (one each, current value)\\n- Eleven \\\"anchor year\\\" columns that flatten the most important year values:\\n  - `ProposalYear`, `ProposalMonth` \\u2014 earliest proposed entry's year\\n  - `ConstructionYear`, `ConstructionMonth` \\u2014 first construction (actual) entry's year\\n  - `OriginalPlannedStartYear` \\u2014 first operating (planned) entry's year\\n  - `LatestPlannedStartYear` \\u2014 most recent operating (planned) entry's year\\n  - `ActualStartYear`, `ActualStartMonth` \\u2014 first operating (actual) entry's year\\n  - `ActualStartYear2`, `ActualStartYear3` \\u2014 used for restarts after idling (rare)\\n  - `ShelvedYear` \\u2014 shelved entry's year\\n  - `CancelledYear` \\u2014 cancelled entry's year\\n  - `StopYear` \\u2014 when operation stopped (any of idled, mothballed, retired); `PlannedStopYear` for planned\\n  - `FIDYear` \\u2014 FID entry's year (`actual` or `planned`, see ambiguity note below)\\n\\n**Implication for all SOPs:** any status timeline change requires pulling the existing timeline first with `fetch_timeline.py <UnitID>`. The export alone cannot tell you:\\n- Whether a status transition was previously recorded as planned\\n- The order of entries\\n- Per-entry notes\\n- The data-entry timestamps\\n\\nWorking blind from the export risks duplicate entries, incorrect ordering, and lost methodology-required context.\\n\\n## Legal state transitions\\n\\nThe methodology doesn't explicitly enumerate legal transitions, but reading the status definitions in order yields the following graph. The build script and `status_timeline.py` use this for validation.\\n\\n```\\nproposed \\u2500\\u252c\\u2500\\u2192 construction \\u2500\\u2192 operating \\u2500\\u252c\\u2500\\u2192 idled \\u2500\\u252c\\u2500\\u2192 operating  (restart)\\n          \\u2502                               \\u2502          \\u251c\\u2500\\u2192 mothballed\\n          \\u2502                               \\u2502          \\u2514\\u2500\\u2192 retired\\n          \\u251c\\u2500\\u2192 shelved \\u2500\\u2192 cancelled        \\u251c\\u2500\\u2192 mothballed \\u2500\\u2192 retired\\n          \\u2514\\u2500\\u2192 cancelled                   \\u2514\\u2500\\u2192 retired\\n                                          \\u2502\\n                                          (very rarely: \\u2192 shelved or cancelled\\n                                           if a project is abandoned mid-operation;\\n                                           see \\\"Edge cases\\\" below)\\n\\nproposed \\u2190\\u2500 (no transition from any other state to proposed under normal rules;\\n             see \\\"Dead-and-revived\\\" edge case below)\\n```\\n\\n### Strict transitions\\n\\n- `proposed` can transition to: `construction`, `shelved`, `cancelled`\\n- `construction` can transition to: `operating`, `shelved` (rare \\u2014 methodology: \\\"shelved if entered construction but never went operating\\\")\\n- `operating` can transition to: `idled`, `mothballed`, `retired`\\n- `idled` can transition to: `operating`, `mothballed`, `retired`\\n- `mothballed` can transition to: `operating` (rare), `retired`\\n- `retired` is terminal (no outbound transitions)\\n- `shelved` can transition to: `cancelled` (either confirmed or inferred), `construction` (rare revival), `operating` (very rare)\\n- `cancelled` is normally terminal, but see \\\"Dead-and-revived\\\" below\\n\\n### Forbidden transitions (flag in `qa_review`)\\n\\n- Any transition INTO `proposed` from another active state \\u2014 proposed projects that revive are usually a new unit (see \\\"Dead-and-revived\\\")\\n- `retired` \\u2192 anything (retirement is permanent per the methodology)\\n- Any direct `construction` \\u2192 `retired` skipping `operating`\\n- Any direct `operating` \\u2192 `cancelled` (operating projects that stop get `idled`/`mothballed`/`retired`, not `cancelled`)\\n\\n## Anchor year invariants\\n\\nYear values must be consistent with each other and with the current status. The build script enforces these on write; `stale_sweep.py` flags violations on read.\\n\\nFor any unit:\\n\\n- `ProposalYear \\u2264 ConstructionYear \\u2264 ActualStartYear` when all three are populated\\n- `ConstructionYear \\u2264 LatestPlannedStartYear` when both are populated\\n- `ActualStartYear \\u2264 StopYear` when both are populated\\n- `OriginalPlannedStartYear \\u2264 LatestPlannedStartYear` (the latest planned should not be earlier than the original)\\n- `ShelvedYear \\u2264 CancelledYear` when both are populated (a project shelved before cancellation)\\n\\nBy current status:\\n\\n- **`proposed`**: `ProposalYear` should be populated. `ConstructionYear`, `ActualStartYear`, `ShelvedYear`, `CancelledYear`, `StopYear` should be blank.\\n- **`construction`**: `ProposalYear` and `ConstructionYear` should be populated. `ActualStartYear`, `ShelvedYear`, `CancelledYear`, `StopYear` should be blank.\\n- **`operating`**: `ActualStartYear` should be populated. `ShelvedYear`, `CancelledYear`, `StopYear` should be blank.\\n- **`idled` / `mothballed` / `retired`**: `ActualStartYear` and `StopYear` should be populated. `ShelvedYear`, `CancelledYear` should be blank.\\n- **`shelved`**: `ShelvedYear` should be populated. `CancelledYear`, `StopYear` should be blank (unless the project was operating before being shelved, which is rare).\\n- **`cancelled`**: `CancelledYear` should be populated.\\n\\n### Reality check: invariants are violated in the existing data\\n\\nThe May 2026 export reveals that \\\"should be populated\\\" is aspirational, not Key things worth your attention before I move on to the reconciliation SOP:\n\n**The transition graph** is my reconstruction from the methodology \u2014 it's not explicitly stated in the manual, but it's implied by the status definitions and the FAQ. The forbidden transitions list in particular is my inference, not a quote. Worth checking my read:\n\n- `proposed` is normally never a destination state (revivals get new units, except for same-fundamental-proposal cases)\n- `retired` is terminal\n- `operating` \u2192 `cancelled` is forbidden \u2014 operating projects that stop become `idled`/`mothballed`/`retired`, not `cancelled` (since `cancelled` is for proposals that never reach operation)\n- Direct `construction` \u2192 `retired` skipping `operating` is forbidden\n\nIf GEM treats any of these differently, the rules file needs to know.\n\n**The substatus semantics** \u2014 substatus means two completely different things depending on Status (active/planned for build-stage statuses, confirmed/inferred for dormancy statuses). I made this explicit because it's confusing in the manual and it'll affect how `status_timeline.py` reads/validates entries.\n\n**The anchor year invariants** are framed as \"should be\" not \"must be\" because the existing data violates them frequently \u2014 and as the analysis showed, those violations are usually historical incompleteness, not bugs. The rules treat them as `qa_review` flags rather than blocking errors. If you'd rather treat them as hard errors (forcing backfill before a status update can land), let me know.\n\n**The \"build script is a guardrail not a gate\" framing** at the bottom \u2014 this matches the carrier project's philosophy: validation surfaces issues to the human reviewer rather than blocking. Since the user applies all edits manually anyway, the script doesn't need veto power. The xlsx review step is the actual gate.\n\n**One thing I deliberately didn't include**: a script for *automatically* converting old-style \"presumed\" status entries (mentioned in the manual as having been renamed to \"inferred\") into the new form. The manual says these should have been cleaned up in the 2025 cycle, so it's plausibly a non-issue. If you encounter \"presumed\" entries in the live DB during a batch, the SOP should treat it as a data-quality finding and propose the rename, but the build script shouldn't auto-apply.\n\nProceed to `lng_terminal_reconciliation_sop.md`?",

This wave of new supply should pro\\u0002gressively ease structural constraints and mitigate the \\r\\nlong-term impact of current disruptions.\\r\\nHowever, greater capacity does not necessarily trans\\u0002late into a simpler market. The LNG sector is becoming \\r\\nmore selective. Buyers are increasingly differentiating \\r\\nbetween supply sources based not only on cost, but \\r\\nalso on reliability, including political considerations and \\r\\nthe security of maritime routes, as well as flexibility and \\r\\nenvironmental performance. Contracting strategies are \\r\\nevolving accordingly, with greater emphasis on portfolio \\r\\noptimization and responsiveness.\\r\\nRegulation, particularly in Europe, is also becoming a \\r\\ndefining factor of market dynamics. Measures ranging \\r\\nfrom methane regulations to due diligence requirements \\r\\nare reshaping access to the European market with vi\\u0002sible effects: higher costs, reduced flexibility and rising \\r\\nuncertainty for suppliers. U.S. authorities, including En\\u0002ergy Secretary Chris Wright, have warned against the \\r\\nextraterritorial reach of European regulations on LNG \\r\\nimports. More broadly, the evolving transatlantic re\\u0002lationship reflects a shift toward a more transactional \\r\\nenergy framework, in which political bargains, including \\r\\nthe $750 billion energy commitment agreed between \\r\\nPresident Trump and the European Commission, now \\r\\ndirectly influence LNG market dynamics. \\r\\nEurope itself is showing signs of recalibration. De\\u0002lays, adjustments and increasing reliance on flexibility \\r\\nmechanisms across key climate policies point to a gra\\u0002dual retreat from the initial ambition of the Green Deal. \\r\\nThe growing visibility of carbon costs, now directly im\\u0002pacting households and industry, has brought the issue \\r\\nof \u201cgreenflation\u201d to the forefront of political and econo\\u0002mic debate.\\r\\nRecent events have further exposed the limits of an \\r\\nenergy system relying heavily on intermittent electricity \\r\\ngeneration without sufficient dispatchable capacity. The \\r\\nIberian blackout and the rebound in gas-fired power \\r\\ngeneration have illustrated a simple reality: resilience \\r\\nstill depends on flexible and reliable energy sources. \\r\\nIn this context, LNG continues to provide flexibility, \\r\\ndispatchability and global connectivity, attributes that \\r\\nremain indispensable in an energy system increasingly \\r\\ndefined by intermittency, fragmentation and uncertainty.\\r\\nThe Hormuz crisis has also shown the cost of dis\\u0002ruption. When LNG is constrained or made unaffordable, \\r\\nthe result is not necessarily faster decarbonization, but, \\r\\nin some cases, gas-to-coal switching. If LNG were to be \\r\\nseen as overregulated, insecure or commercially disad\\u0002vantaged, its contribution to the energy transition could \\r\\nbe weakened, not because of a lack of relevance, but \\r\\nbecause of policy-driven or geopolitical distortions.\\r\\nLooking ahead to 2030, the LNG market will be larger, \\r\\nmore interconnected and more flexible, but also more de\\u0002manding. Increased supply will not eliminate competition; \\r\\nit will redefine it. In a better-supplied market, advantage \\r\\nwill accrue to projects and portfolios that combine cost \\r\\ncompetitiveness with execution reliability, commercial \\r\\nagility and credible environmental performance.\\r\\nLNG will remain at the heart of geopolitical and \\r\\neconomic considerations. Its capital intensity and the \\r\\nconcentration of resources ensure that it will continue \\r\\nto play a strategic role in energy security debates. The \\r\\ncurrent crisis is a reminder that the path toward a more \\r\\nbalanced market is unlikely to be linear.\\r\\nYet the broader direction is clear. The LNG industry \\r\\nis not retreating; it is evolving. Once again, a surplus of \\r\\ncapacity has been overtaken by events. Once again, the \\r\\nmarket is adapting.       "description": "Draft the reconciliation SOP \u2014 generic body + GIIGNL-specific appendix",
      "file_text": "# LNG Terminals Reconciliation SOP\n\nLast revised: 2026-05 (rev 1, initial draft)\n\nOperational rules for reconciling the GEM LNG terminals database against an authoritative annual report \u2014 primarily GIIGNL, with the same workflow body intended to serve a future IGU reconciliation SOP. This SOP describes how to do the diff cleanly; the *fixes* go through the Update or Discovery workflows. Reconciliation surfaces work; it does not perform it.\n\nThe methodology doc (LNG Terminals Manual) is authoritative for the underlying research rules. This SOP is operational.\n\n## \u00a71 When to run this SOP\n\nTrigger conditions:\n- A new GIIGNL Annual Report has been published (typically June, covering the prior calendar year) and added to the project files\n- The user explicitly requests a reconciliation batch\n- Triage SOP \u00a73 flags \"unprocessed GIIGNL reconciliation\" as a backlog item\n\nDo NOT run reconciliation:\n- More than once against the same report edition (it's an annual workflow, not recurring)\n- Against partial or draft GIIGNL releases \u2014 wait for the published edition\n- As a substitute for Update or Discovery batches \u2014 its outputs are inputs to those, not replacements\n\n## \u00a72 Confirm parameters at batch start\n\nBefore any tool runs, confirm with the user:\n\n1. **Which report edition** \u2014 typically the year on the cover (e.g. \"GIIGNL 2026 Annual Report\" covers calendar year 2025 trade data)\n2. **Which GIIGNL sections** are in scope. Default: both the liquefaction table (operating + recently-commissioned export terminals) and the regasification table (operating + recently-commissioned import terminals). Country narratives are also in scope as a secondary source for proposed/construction projects that may inform Discovery routing.\n3. **Which GEM lifecycle states to compare against** \u2014 default: GIIGNL is operating-only, so the reconciliation primarily matches against GEM `operating`, `idled`, `mothballed`, `retired` rows (GIIGNL keeps recently-retired entries for one report cycle). GEM `construction` rows may match GIIGNL narrative mentions, but the value-level diff only meaningfully applies to operating capacity.\n4. **Whether to include the country-summary tables** (per-country totals) as a sanity check on GEM's project-level rollups. Default: yes.\n\nThese parameters get written into the staging xlsx README sheet.\n\n## \u00a73 Workflow\n\n### \u00a73.1 Setup\n\n1. Verify the GIIGNL report file is in project files at `/mnt/project/GIIGNL*.pdf` (or wherever the user placed it).\n2. `file <path>` to confirm format. The 2026 GIIGNL came as a zip of per-page JPEG + OCR text files + manifest.json, NOT as a parseable PDF. If the format differs, the extractor may need adjustment.\n3. Materialize scripts to working directory per the SKILL.md instructions:\n   - `pull_gem_db.py`, `normalize.py`, `dedup_index.py`\n   - `giignl_extract.py`, `report_diff.py`, `url_verifier.py`\n   - `build_review_package.py`, `recalc.py`\n4. `python pull_gem_db.py` \u2192 fresh GEM CSV at `/home/claude/gem_export.csv`. **Mandatory** per the [ref]-fill SOP discipline \u2014 the database changes between batches.\n\n### \u00a73.2 Extract GIIGNL into structured form\n\n`python giignl_extract.py /mnt/project/GIIGNL*.pdf --output /home/claude/giignl_normalized.csv`\n\nThe extractor produces a flat CSV with GEM-aligned column names so the diff is column-comparable. See Appendix A for the per-table extraction rules.\n\n**The extractor is vision-assisted, not pure regex.** GIIGNL tables have column structure that's lost in text-only OCR (the per-page `.txt` files have rows wrapped unpredictably). The extractor uses the per-page JPEG images plus the OCR text as a confirmation channel. Output rows include a `_source_page` column for traceability.\n\nVerify the extraction before proceeding:\n- Total liquefaction MTPA in the extracted CSV should match the GIIGNL Key Figures page (524 MTPA in 2026 edition)\n- Total regasification MTPA should match Key Figures (1,247 MTPA in 2026 edition)\n- Per-country subtotals (where GIIGNL displays them) should match the sum of country rows\n- If totals don't match within 2%, suspect missing rows from OCR/parsing \u2014 investigate before continuing\n\n### \u00a73.3 Normalize both sides\n\n`python normalize.py` is imported as a module by `report_diff.py`. Both the GEM CSV and the GIIGNL CSV go through:\n- Country name normalization (ISO names, common variants)\n- Owner/operator entity normalization (per `entity_canonical_map.md`)\n- Capacity unit normalization (everything \u2192 mtpa)\n- Terminal name normalization (strip \"LNG Terminal\", \"FSRU\", \"FLNG\" suffixes; handle \"T1\"/\"Train 1\" variants)\n\nThe normalized values are used for matching ONLY; the unnormalized values are preserved in the diff output for human readability.\n\n### \u00a73.4 Run the diff\n\n`python report_diff.py --gem /home/claude/gem_export.csv --report /home/claude/giignl_normalized.csv --output /home/claude/giignl_diff.json`\n\nThe script produces a four-way classification per (country, normalized-terminal-name) pair:\n\n| Classification | Meaning | Default route |\n|---|---|---|\n| **Match \u2014 values agree** | Both have the entity, values align within tolerance | Confidence bump only; no edit needed |\n| **Match \u2014 values disagree** | Both have the entity, one or more fields differ | \u2192 Update workflow |\n| **GIIGNL-only** | GIIGNL has it, GEM doesn't | \u2192 Discovery workflow |\n| **GEM-only** | GEM has it, GIIGNL doesn't | \u2192 log only (usually expected, see \u00a73.7) |\n\nThe script also produces a fifth category for human resolution:\n\n| Classification | Meaning | Default route |\n|---|---|---|\n| **Ambiguous match** | Multiple GEM rows could match one GIIGNL row, or vice versa | Manual review in `giignl_diff` sheet |\n\n### \u00a73.5 Matching algorithm\n\nTwo-pass match:\n\n**Pass 1: exact match on (normalized country, normalized terminal name).** Highest confidence. Direct hit.\n\n**Pass 2: fuzzy match within country** for unmatched GIIGNL rows. For each unmatched GIIGNL row, score every GEM row in the same country by:\n- Token-set similarity of terminal name (e.g. \"Arzew GL3Z\" vs \"Arzew LNG Terminal\" \u2192 high overlap on \"Arzew\")\n- Owner-entity overlap (any common entity \u2192 bonus)\n- Capacity proximity (within 30% of nominal MTPA \u2192 bonus)\n- Start-year proximity (within 2 years \u2192 bonus)\n- FSRU vessel name match (when both rows are FSRUs) \u2192 strong bonus\n\nScores above a threshold get a \"probable match\" classification; below threshold = no match. Ambiguous when two GEM rows score within 10% of each other against the same GIIGNL row.\n\n**Matching is at the project level, not the unit level**, because GIIGNL aggregates per-site and GEM splits into units. A GIIGNL row like \"Arzew GL3Z, 4.7 MTPA, 1 train\" matches a GEM project that may have one or more units; the diff records the GIIGNL-side numbers against the *project total* from GEM's per-unit rollup. If the GEM project's per-unit breakdown doesn't sum to the GIIGNL number, that itself is a `value-disagreement`.\n\n### \u00a73.6 Disagreement classification rules\n\nValue disagreements get classified by field type, since each field has its own default cause-of-disagreement:\n\n**Capacity disagreements** \u2014 most common. Usual causes:\n- Unit conversion error in either source (GIIGNL is always MTPA for these tables)\n- Per-train vs total reconciliation issue (GEM has 6 units of 3.3 MTPA = 19.8 MTPA project total; GIIGNL shows 22.2 MTPA \u2014 investigate the difference)\n- Expansion or debottlenecking captured by one source but not the other\n- One source quoting nameplate, the other quoting actual achieved capacity (methodology says use nameplate)\n\n**Start-year disagreements** \u2014 usual causes:\n- Planned vs actual confusion\n- Different definition of \"operating\" (commissioning cargo vs commercial operations \u2014 see methodology FAQ on Calcasieu Pass)\n- Multi-train projects with staggered starts being averaged\n\n**Owner disagreements** \u2014 usual causes:\n- Immediate owner vs ultimate parent\n- Stale data in one source after a recent ownership change\n- JV percentages cited differently (GIIGNL often shows percentages; GEM stores immediate owner separately from parent)\n\n**Status disagreements** \u2014 usual causes:\n- GIIGNL drops shelved/cancelled projects entirely; if GEM has the project as proposed and GIIGNL doesn't list it, that's GEM-only (expected), not a status disagreement\n- GIIGNL lists a project that GEM has as `cancelled` \u2192 strong signal GEM is wrong; check if the project was revived\n\nEach disagreement goes into `giignl_diff` sheet with a `disagreement_category` column drawn from the above. The Update workflow uses the category to pick its source-search strategy.\n\n### \u00a73.7 Routing GEM-only findings\n\nGEM-only is the most common classification and usually requires no action \u2014 GIIGNL has known gaps:\n- GIIGNL doesn't comprehensively cover small-scale or non-member-country terminals\n- GIIGNL drops projects below a coverage threshold\n- GIIGNL only covers operating; GEM tracks proposed/construction/shelved/cancelled\n\n**Flag for review** when GEM-only is suspicious:\n- GEM `operating` status in a GIIGNL-member country that GIIGNL doesn't list \u2014 possibly a GEM error (project was actually cancelled or never operated)\n- GEM project listed in a country where GIIGNL's country-summary total wouldn't accommodate it (e.g. GEM has a 5 MTPA terminal in a country GIIGNL reports as 8 MTPA total when GEM's other terminals already sum to 8)\n- GEM `operating` with `LastUpdated > 18 months` and not in GIIGNL \u2014 possibly stale data that should move to `mothballed`/`retired`\n\nThese get routed to `giignl_to_action` sheet with `route: review` (not directly to Update) \u2014 the conclusion may be \"GEM is correct, GIIGNL gap\" rather than an actionable edit.\n\n### \u00a73.8 No auto-application of GIIGNL values\n\n**Hard rule.** A value disagreement is a *candidate* for update, not an applied edit. Every disagreement goes through the Update workflow's normal source-search and confidence-labeling process. The methodology FAQ is explicit: \"if we find a more specific or current source on a terminal that conflicts with the report, that source/data should take priority.\"\n\nThe reconciliation batch's xlsx output includes:\n- `giignl_diff` sheet \u2014 every diff finding with full context (both sides' values, classification, category)\n- `giignl_to_action` sheet \u2014 findings that route to Update or Discovery, with target action noted\n\nThe Update / Discovery batches that consume these findings cite GIIGNL as ONE source among others, with the same source-tier treatment as other annual industry reports. Per `source_roster.md`, GIIGNL is Tier 1 but not authoritative \u2014 sponsor IR or primary regulatory filings take priority.\n\n### \u00a73.9 URL verification\n\nAny URLs included in the staging xlsx (e.g. for GIIGNL-only findings where the agent has pre-searched for confirming sources) must pass `url_verifier.py` per the standard rules. The GIIGNL document itself is NOT a URL-citable source for individual rows \u2014 there's no per-row URL into a paginated PDF. Cite GIIGNL by edition year and table name in a separate `report_citation` column, not as a URL.\n\n### \u00a73.10 Build the staging package\n\n`python build_review_package.py --mode reconciliation --report giignl --year <YEAR> --batch-id <YYYYMMDD>`\n\nProduces `/mnt/user-data/outputs/lng_terminals_batch_<YYYYMMDD>.xlsx` with the standard sheets plus two reconciliation-specific sheets:\n\n- `giignl_diff` \u2014 full diff output, color-coded per cell (green = match, yellow = ambiguous, red = disagreement, blue = GEM-only-expected, no fill = GIIGNL-only-needs-discovery)\n- `giignl_to_action` \u2014 actionable findings with proposed routing (Update vs Discovery vs Review)\n\nEmpty sheets are omitted per SKILL.md convention.\n\n`python recalc.py /mnt/user-data/outputs/lng_terminals_batch_<YYYYMMDD>.xlsx` \u2192 zero formula errors.\n\n`present_files`.\n\n### \u00a73.11 Errata log\n\nWhen reconciliation finds GIIGNL clearly wrong (e.g. capacity figure that contradicts the operator's own filings), record in `country_notes_contributions` sheet under \"GIIGNL errata observed\". Over multiple years this builds a useful record of GIIGNL's failure modes (which countries it covers poorly, which kinds of fields it gets wrong) that informs future reconciliations.\n\n## \u00a74 Confidence labels (reconciliation-specific)\n\nStandard color scheme from SKILL.md applies, with reconciliation-specific cell semantics:\n\n- **Green** \u2014 Match with values agreeing within tolerance. Confidence bump on the GEM record; no edit needed.\n- **Yellow** \u2014 Match but values disagree, OR ambiguous match. Requires Update workflow follow-up.\n- **Red** \u2014 Disagreement where GIIGNL contradicts GEM on a primary field (status, capacity) and the disagreement looks substantive. Requires Update workflow follow-up and probably new source research.\n- **Blue** \u2014 GEM-only finding that's expected (GIIGNL gap, not a GEM error). No action needed; re-verified by absence.\n\nGIIGNL-only findings get no color fill \u2014 they're not GEM cells, they're new candidates.\n\n## \u00a75 Edge cases and gotchas\n\n### \u00a75.1 GIIGNL's geographic scope \u2260 GEM's\n\nGIIGNL is import/export-focused and largely member-driven. Some terminals never appear in GIIGNL even though they exist (small-scale, non-member countries, certain Russian terminals post-sanctions). The country-resource doc and `country_research_notes.md` should track known GIIGNL coverage gaps.\n\n### \u00a75.2 FSRU vessel reassignments\n\nGIIGNL reports the FSRU vessel currently at each terminal. If a terminal swapped FSRUs since the last GIIGNL, the diff will show the FSRU vessel name disagreement. This is real signal \u2014 route to Update workflow with the FSRU sync rule (SKILL.md) for cross-check against the carrier project.\n\nGIIGNL sometimes shows a recently-departed FSRU at its old terminal because GIIGNL is published months after year-end. Don't immediately treat as \"GIIGNL is wrong\" \u2014 check whether GEM's record has the swap-out documented.\n\n### \u00a75.3 Multi-terminal sites\n\nSome sites host multiple terminals (e.g. one country's main LNG hub). GIIGNL may aggregate or split differently from GEM. The matching algorithm's \"ambiguous match\" classification catches this \u2014 it requires manual resolution before any action.\n\n### \u00a75.4 Operating-but-not-yet-in-GIIGNL\n\nGIIGNL covers operating terminals through the report year. A terminal that started up in early calendar year covered by the report should appear; one that started in late Q4 of that year often doesn't. If a recently-started GEM `operating` terminal isn't in GIIGNL, check the GEM `ActualStartYear` \u2014 if Q4 or later, expect it in next year's GIIGNL.\n\n### \u00a75.5 Floating storage units (FSU/FRU) not in liquefaction or regasification tables\n\nFSU and FRU vessels are non-standard. GIIGNL handling varies. Check the terminal narrative sections for mentions rather than expecting tabular rows.\n\n### \u00a75.6 The capacity numbers in GIIGNL's narrative don't always match its own tables\n\nGIIGNL's country narratives sometimes cite a different capacity number than the GIIGNL tabular row for the same terminal. When this happens, prefer the tabular value for the diff (it's the structured source) and log the narrative discrepancy as a GIIGNL errata.\n\n## \u00a76 Pause-and-ask triggers\n\nStop and consult the user before proceeding when:\n\n- More than ~10% of matched rows have value disagreements \u2192 systematic issue (GIIGNL methodology change, GEM schema misunderstanding, or extractor bug). Don't auto-route 100+ Update batches; review the pattern first.\n- The extractor produces totals that diverge from GIIGNL's Key Figures by more than 2% \u2192 likely missing rows. Don't proceed with an incomplete diff.\n- GIIGNL-only findings exceed ~30 candidates \u2192 may indicate a GEM coverage gap for a whole region, worth scoping a Discovery batch around it rather than treating as 30 individual discoveries.\n- The GIIGNL report file is in an unexpected format (not the zip-of-images structure) \u2192 extractor needs adjustment before proceeding.\n- A country shows GIIGNL country-summary totals that diverge dramatically from the sum of GEM operating capacity for that country \u2192 could be a country definition mismatch (e.g. one source includes a disputed territory) or a real coverage gap.\n\n---\n\n## Appendix A \u2014 GIIGNL-specific extraction rules\n\nThese are the rules that `giignl_extract.py` implements. They're documented here because they evolve with each GIIGNL edition.\n\n### A.1 Source format (2026 edition)\n\nThe 2026 GIIGNL Annual Report file is named `.pdf` but is actually a zip archive containing:\n- 80 JPEG page images (`1.jpeg` through `80.jpeg`)\n- 80 OCR text files (`1.txt` through `80.txt`)\n- `manifest.json` with per-page metadata\n\nOCR text quality is decent for prose, structurally messy for tables (column boundaries lost, rows wrap). The extractor uses both:\n- OCR text as primary source for narrative pages\n- JPEG images via vision processing for tabular pages, with OCR text as a confirmation channel\n\n### A.2 Page sections (2026 edition)\n\n| Pages | Section | Use |\n|---|---|---|\n| 1-3 | Cover, profile, editorial | Skip |\n| 4-7 | Key figures, narrative overview | Use Key Figures totals as extraction sanity check |\n| 8-27 | Trade dynamics narrative | Skip for diff; informational |\n| 28-31 | Liquefaction narrative | Use country sections as secondary signal for Discovery routing |\n| 32-37 | **Liquefaction tables** | Primary extraction source for export terminal diff |\n| 48-52 | Regasification narrative | Use country sections as secondary signal |\n| 53-62 | **Regasification tables** | Primary extraction source for import terminal diff |\n| 64-77 | Contracts, shipping, member info | Skip for diff |\n\nPage numbers may shift between editions \u2014 always re-derive section boundaries from the report's TOC or by content-pattern detection.\n\n### A.3 Liquefaction table schema\n\nColumns observed in 2026:\n1. Country (with subtotal MTPA shown for multi-project countries)\n2. Project name (e.g. \"Arzew GL3Z\", \"NLNG T1\", \"Idku T2\")\n3. Nominal capacity (MTPA, decimal)\n4. Number of trains (integer, typically 1 per row since rows are per-train)\n5. Number of tanks (integer)\n6. Total storage capacity (liq m\u00b3)\n7. Owner(s) \u2014 free text with percentages, e.g. \"Sonatrach\" or \"ENI 50%, EGAS 40%, EGPC 10%\"\n8. Operator\n9. MT-LT Buyer(s) \u2014 comma-separated entities\n10. Start date \u2014 year only\n\nExtractor produces normalized CSV with columns:\n- `_giignl_section` = \"liquefaction\"\n- `_source_page` (integer)\n- `country` (raw)\n- `country_normalized` (per normalize.py)\n- `project` (raw)\n- `project_normalized` (lowercased, \"T1\"/\"Train 1\" unified)\n- `facility_type` = \"export\"\n- `capacity_mtpa` (float)\n- `n_trains` (int)\n- `n_tanks` (int)\n- `storage_m3` (int)\n- `owners_raw` (text)\n- `owners_parsed` (list of {entity, pct})\n- `operator` (text)\n- `buyers_raw` (text)\n- `buyers_parsed` (list of entities)\n- `start_year` (int)\n\n### A.4 Regasification table schema\n\nColumns observed in 2026:\n1. Market (country)\n2. Site (with FSRU vessel name appended when applicable, e.g. \"Escobar / Excelerate Expedient (FSRU)\")\n3. Concept (\"Onshore\" or \"Offshore\")\n4. Number of tanks\n5. Total capacity (liq m\u00b3)\n6. Number of vaporizers (may be N/A for FSRUs)\n7. Nominal capacity (MTPA, decimal)\n8. Owner \u2014 free text, often split into \"Owner: X / Charterer: Y\" for FSRUs\n9. Operator \u2014 free text, often split for FSRUs as \"FSRU: X / Terminal: Y\"\n10. Third Party Access (Yes/No/dash)\n11. Additional Services offered (text or dash)\n12. Start-up date \u2014 year only\n\nExtractor produces normalized CSV with columns:\n- `_giignl_section` = \"regasification\"\n- `_source_page`\n- `country` (raw and normalized)\n- `site` (raw)\n- `site_normalized`\n- `facility_type` = \"import\"\n- `is_floating` (bool, derived from \"FSRU\" or \"FLNG\" in site/concept)\n- `vessel_name` (when floating, extracted from site text)\n- `concept` = \"onshore\" | \"offshore\"\n- `capacity_mtpa` (float)\n- `n_tanks`, `storage_m3`, `n_vaporizers`\n- `owners_raw`, `owners_parsed`\n- `charterer` (when FSRU)\n- `operator_raw`, `operator_parsed`\n- `terminal_operator` (when FSRU has separate terminal operator)\n- `tpa` (bool \u2014 Third Party Access)\n- `additional_services` (text)\n- `start_year` (int)\n\n### A.5 Country subtotal rows\n\nGIIGNL inserts subtotal labels for some countries (e.g. \"Algeria 25.3 MTPA\"). The extractor:\n- Detects subtotal rows by pattern: country name + capacity + \"MTPA\" without other fields\n- Uses subtotals as a sanity check (sum of per-project rows in that country should match)\n- Does NOT produce an output row for subtotals (they're metadata)\n\n### A.6 OCR artifact handling\n\nThe 2026 OCR shows these consistent artifacts:\n- `\\u0002` characters appearing as soft-hyphen breaks within words (e.g. `Mids\\u0002cale` for \"Midscale\")\n- Line breaks (`\\r\\n`) inserted mid-cell, especially in long owner descriptions\n- Numbers occasionally split across lines (`125,\\n000` for \"125,000\")\n- Capacity unit suffixes (\"MTPA\") rendered inconsistently\n\nThe extractor's text-cleanup pass:\n1. Strip `\\u0002` characters\n2. Re-join wrapped numeric values\n3. Normalize whitespace\n4. Re-attach orphaned units to preceding numbers\n\n### A.7 What to add for IGU (future)\n\nIGU's World LNG Report has different table layouts but the same conceptual content.
