      "json_block": "{\"language\": \"markdown\", \"code\": \"# LNG Terminals Reconciliation SOP\\n\\nLast revised: 2026-05 (rev 1, initial draft)\\n\\nOperational rules for reconciling the GEM LNG terminals database against an authoritative annual report \\u2014 primarily GIIGNL, with the same workflow body intended to serve a future IGU reconciliation SOP. This SOP describes how to do the diff cleanly; the *fixes* go through the Update or Discovery workflows. Reconciliation surfaces work; it does not perform it.\\n\\nThe methodology doc (LNG Terminals Manual) is authoritative for the underlying research rules. This SOP is operational.\\n\\n## \\u00a71 When to run this SOP\\n\\nTrigger conditions:\\n- A new GIIGNL Annual Report has been published (typically June, covering the prior calendar year) and added to the project files\\n- The user explicitly requests a reconciliation batch\\n- Triage SOP \\u00a73 flags \\\"unprocessed GIIGNL reconciliation\\\" as a backlog item\\n\\nDo NOT run reconciliation:\\n- More than once against the same report edition (it's an annual workflow, not recurring)\\n- Against partial or draft GIIGNL releases \\u2014 wait for the published edition\\n- As a substitute for Update or Discovery batches \\u2014 its outputs are inputs to those, not replacements\\n\\n## \\u00a72 Confirm parameters at batch start\\n\\nBefore any tool runs, confirm with the user:\\n\\n1. **Which report edition** \\u2014 typically the year on the cover (e.g. \\\"GIIGNL 2026 Annual Report\\\" covers calendar year 2025 trade data)\\n2. **Which GIIGNL sections** are in scope. Default: both the liquefaction table (operating + recently-commissioned export terminals) and the regasification table (operating + recently-commissioned import terminals). Country narratives are also in scope as a secondary source for proposed/construction projects that may inform Discovery routing.\\n3. **Which GEM lifecycle states to compare against** \\u2014 default: GIIGNL is operating-only, so the reconciliation primarily matches against GEM `operating`, `idled`, `mothballed`, `retired` rows (GIIGNL keeps recently-retired entries for one report cycle). GEM `construction` rows may match GIIGNL narrative mentions, but the value-level diff only meaningfully applies to operating capacity.\\n4. **Whether to include the country-summary tables** (per-country totals) as a sanity check on GEM's project-level rollups. Default: yes.\\n\\nThese parameters get written into the staging xlsx README sheet.\\n\\n## \\u00a73 Workflow\\n\\n### \\u00a73.1 Setup\\n\\n1. Verify the GIIGNL report file is in project files at `/mnt/project/GIIGNL*.pdf` (or wherever the user placed it).\\n2. `file <path>` to confirm format. The 2026 GIIGNL came as a zip of per-page JPEG + OCR text files + manifest.json, NOT as a parseable PDF. If the format differs, the extractor may need adjustment.\\n3. Materialize scripts to working directory per the SKILL.md instructions:\\n   - `pull_gem_db.py`, `normalize.py`, `dedup_index.py`\\n   - `giignl_extract.py`, `report_diff.py`, `url_verifier.py`\\n   - `build_review_package.py`, `recalc.py`\\n4. `python pull_gem_db.py` \\u2192 fresh GEM CSV at `/home/claude/gem_export.csv`. **Mandatory** per the [ref]-fill SOP discipline \\u2014 the database changes between batches.\\n\\n### \\u00a73.2 Extract GIIGNL into structured form\\n\\n`python giignl_extract.py /mnt/project/GIIGNL*.pdf --output /home/claude/giignl_normalized.csv`\\n\\nThe extractor produces a flat CSV with GEM-aligned column names so the diff is column-comparable. See Appendix A for the per-table extraction rules.\\n\\n**The extractor is vision-assisted, not pure regex.** GIIGNL tables have column structure that's lost in text-only OCR (the per-page `.txt` files have rows wrapped unpredictably). The extractor uses the per-page JPEG images plus the OCR text as a confirmation channel. Output rows include a `_source_page` column for traceability.\\n\\nVerify the extraction before proceeding:\\n- Total liquefaction MTPA in the extracted CSV should match the GIIGNL Key Figures page (524 MTPA in 2026 edition)\\n- Total regasification MTPA should match Key Figures (1,247 MTPA in 2026 edition)\\n- Per-country subtotals (where GIIGNL displays them) should match the sum of country rows\\n- If totals don't match within 2%, suspect missing rows from OCR/parsing \\u2014 investigate before continuing\\n\\n### \\u00a73.3 Normalize both sides\\n\\n`python normalize.py` is imported as a module by `report_diff.py`. Both the GEM CSV and the GIIGNL CSV go through:\\n- Country name normalization (ISO names, common variants)\\n- Owner/operator entity normalization (per `entity_canonical_map.md`)\\n- Capacity unit normalization (everything \\u2192 mtpa)\\n- Terminal name normalization (strip \\\"LNG Terminal\\\", \\\"FSRU\\\", \\\"FLNG\\\" suffixes; handle \\\"T1\\\"/\\\"Train 1\\\" variants)\\n\\nThe normalized values are used for matching ONLY; the unnormalized values are preserved in the diff output for human readability.\\n\\n### \\u00a73.4 Run the diff\\n\\n`python report_diff.py --gem /home/claude/gem_export.csv --report /home/claude/giignl_normalized.csv --output /home/claude/giignl_diff.json`\\n\\nThe script produces a four-way classification per (country, normalized-terminal-name) pair:\\n\\n| Classification | Meaning | Default route |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| **Match \\u2014 values agree** | Both have the entity, values align within tolerance | Confidence bump only; no edit needed |\\n| **Match \\u2014 values disagree** | Both have the entity, one or more fields differ | \\u2192 Update workflow |\\n| **GIIGNL-only** | GIIGNL has it, GEM doesn't | \\u2192 Discovery workflow |\\n| **GEM-only** | GEM has it, GIIGNL doesn't | \\u2192 log only (usually expected, see \\u00a73.7) |\\n\\nThe script also produces a fifth category for human resolution:\\n\\n| Classification | Meaning | Default route |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| **Ambiguous match** | Multiple GEM rows could match one GIIGNL row, or vice versa | Manual review in `giignl_diff` sheet |\\n\\n### \\u00a73.5 Matching algorithm\\n\\nTwo-pass match:\\n\\n**Pass 1: exact match on (normalized country, normalized terminal name).** Highest confidence. Direct hit.\\n\\n**Pass 2: fuzzy match within country** for unmatched GIIGNL rows. For each unmatched GIIGNL row, score every GEM row in the same country by:\\n- Token-set similarity of terminal name (e.g. \\\"Arzew GL3Z\\\" vs \\\"Arzew LNG Terminal\\\" \\u2192 high overlap on \\\"Arzew\\\")\\n- Owner-entity overlap (any common entity \\u2192 bonus)\\n- Capacity proximity (within 30% of nominal MTPA \\u2192 bonus)\\n- Start-year proximity (within 2 years \\u2192 bonus)\\n- FSRU vessel name match (when both rows are FSRUs) \\u2192 strong bonus\\n\\nScores above a threshold get a \\\"probable match\\\" classification; below threshold = no match. Ambiguous when two GEM rows score within 10% of each other against the same GIIGNL row.\\n\\n**Matching is at the project level, not the unit level**, because GIIGNL aggregates per-site and GEM splits into units. A GIIGNL row like \\\"Arzew GL3Z, 4.7 MTPA, 1 train\\\" matches a GEM project that may have one or more units; the diff records the GIIGNL-side numbers against the *project total* from GEM's per-unit rollup. If the GEM project's per-unit breakdown doesn't sum to the GIIGNL number, that itself is a `value-disagreement`.\\n\\n### \\u00a73.6 Disagreement classification rules\\n\\nValue disagreements get classified by field type, since each field has its own default cause-of-disagreement:\\n\\n**Capacity disagreements** \\u2014 most common. Usual causes:\\n- Unit conversion error in either source (GIIGNL is always MTPA for these tables)\\n- Per-train vs total reconciliation issue (GEM has 6 units of 3.3 MTPA = 19.8 MTPA project total; GIIGNL shows 22.2 MTPA \\u2014 investigate the difference)\\n- Expansion or debottlenecking captured by one source but not the other\\n- One source quoting nameplate, the other quoting actual achieved capacity (methodology says use nameplate)\\n\\n**Start-year disagreements** \\u2014 usual causes:\\n- Planned vs actual confusion\\n- Different definition of \\\"operating\\\" (commissioning cargo vs commercial operations \\u2014 see methodology FAQ on Calcasieu Pass)\\n- Multi-train projects with staggered starts being averaged\\n\\n**Owner disagreements** \\u2014 usual causes:\\n- Immediate owner vs ultimate parent\\n- Stale data in one source after a recent ownership change\\n- JV percentages cited differently (GIIGNL often shows percentages; GEM stores immediate owner separately from parent)\\n\\n**Status disagreements** \\u2014 usual causes:\\n- GIIGNL drops shelved/cancelled projects entirely; if GEM has the project as proposed and GIIGNL doesn't list it, that's GEM-only (expected), not a status disagreement\\n- GIIGNL lists a project that GEM has as `cancelled` \\u2192 strong signal GEM is wrong; check if the project was revived\\n\\nEach disagreement goes into `giignl_diff` sheet with a `disagreement_category` column drawn from the above. The Update workflow uses the category to pick its source-search strategy.\\n\\n### \\u00a73.7 Routing GEM-only findings\\n\\nGEM-only is the most common classification and usually requires no action \\u2014 GIIGNL has known gaps:\\n- GIIGNL doesn't comprehensively cover small-scale or non-member-country terminals\\n- GIIGNL drops projects below a coverage threshold\\n- GIIGNL only covers operating; GEM tracks proposed/construction/shelved/cancelled\\n\\n**Flag for review** when GEM-only is suspicious:\\n- GEM `operating` status in a GIIGNL-member country that GIIGNL doesn't list \\u2014 possibly a GEM error (project was actually cancelled or never operated)\\n- GEM project listed in a country where GIIGNL's country-summary total wouldn't accommodate it (e.g. GEM has a 5 MTPA terminal in a country GIIGNL reports as 8 MTPA total when GEM's other terminals already sum to 8)\\n- GEM `operating` with `LastUpdated > 18 months` and not in GIIGNL \\u2014 possibly stale data that should move to `mothballed`/`retired`\\n\\nThese get routed to `giignl_to_action` sheet with `route: review` (not directly to Update) \\u2014 the conclusion may be \\\"GEM is correct, GIIGNL gap\\\" rather than an actionable edit.\\n\\n### \\u00a73.8 No auto-application of GIIGNL values\\n\\n**Hard rule.** A value disagreement is a *candidate* for update, not an applied edit. Every disagreement goes through the Update workflow's normal source-search and confidence-labeling process. The methodology FAQ is explicit: \\\"if we find a more specific or current source on a terminal that conflicts with the report, that source/data should take priority.\\\"\\n\\nThe reconciliation batch's xlsx output includes:\\n- `giignl_diff` sheet \\u2014 every diff finding with full context (both sides' values, classification, category)\\n- `giignl_to_action` sheet \\u2014 findings that route to Update or Discovery, with target action noted\\n\\nThe Update / Discovery batches that consume these findings cite GIIGNL as ONE source among others, with the same source-tier treatment as other annual industry reports. Per `source_roster.md`, GIIGNL is Tier 1 but not authoritative \\u2014 sponsor IR or primary regulatory filings take priority.\\n\\n### \\u00a73.9 URL verification\\n\\nAny URLs included in the staging xlsx (e.g. for GIIGNL-only findings where the agent has pre-searched for confirming sources) must pass `url_verifier.py` per the standard rules. The GIIGNL document itself is NOT a URL-citable source for individual rows \\u2014 there's no per-row URL into a paginated PDF. Cite GIIGNL by edition year and table name in a separate `report_citation` column, not as a URL.\\n\\n### \\u00a73.10 Build the staging package\\n\\n`python build_review_package.py --mode reconciliation --report giignl --year <YEAR> --batch-id <YYYYMMDD>`\\n\\nProduces `/mnt/user-data/outputs/lng_terminals_batch_<YYYYMMDD>.xlsx` with the standard sheets plus two reconciliation-specific sheets:\\n\\n- `giignl_diff` \\u2014 full diff output, color-coded per cell (green = match, yellow = ambiguous, red = disagreement, blue = GEM-only-expected, no fill = GIIGNL-only-needs-discovery)\\n- `giignl_to_action` \\u2014 actionable findings with proposed routing (Update vs Discovery vs Review)\\n\\nEmpty sheets are omitted per SKILL.md convention.\\n\\n`python recalc.py /mnt/user-data/outputs/lng_terminals_batch_<YYYYMMDD>.xlsx` \\u2192 zero formula errors.\\n\\n`present_files`.\\n\\n### \\u00a73.11 Errata log\\n\\nWhen reconciliation finds GIIGNL clearly wrong (e.g. capacity figure that contradicts the operator's own filings), record in `country_notes_contributions` sheet under \\\"GIIGNL errata observed\\\". Over multiple years this builds a useful record of GIIGNL's failure modes (which countries it covers poorly, which kinds of fields it gets wrong) that informs future reconciliations.\\n\\n## \\u00a74 Confidence labels (reconciliation-specific)\\n\\nStandard color scheme from SKILL.md applies, with reconciliation-specific cell semantics:\\n\\n- **Green** \\u2014 Match with values agreeing within tolerance. Confidence bump on the GEM record; no edit needed.\\n- **Yellow** \\u2014 Match but values disagree, OR ambiguous match. Requires Update workflow follow-up.\\n- **Red** \\u2014 Disagreement where GIIGNL contradicts GEM on a primary field (status, capacity) and the disagreement looks substantive. Requires Update workflow follow-up and probably new source research.\\n- **Blue** \\u2014 GEM-only finding that's expected (GIIGNL gap, not a GEM error). No action needed; re-verified by absence.\\n\\nGIIGNL-only findings get no color fill \\u2014 they're not GEM cells, they're new candidates.\\n\\n## \\u00a75 Edge cases and gotchas\\n\\n### \\u00a75.1 GIIGNL's geographic scope \\u2260 GEM's\\n\\nGIIGNL is import/export-focused and largely member-driven. Some terminals never appear in GIIGNL even though they exist (small-scale, non-member countries, certain Russian terminals post-sanctions). The country-resource doc and `country_research_notes.md` should track known GIIGNL coverage gaps.\\n\\n### \\u00a75.2 FSRU vessel reassignments\\n\\nGIIGNL reports the FSRU vessel currently at each terminal. If a terminal swapped FSRUs since the last GIIGNL, the diff will show the FSRU vessel name disagreement. This is real signal \\u2014 route to Update workflow with the FSRU sync rule (SKILL.md) for cross-check against the carrier project.\\n\\nGIIGNL sometimes shows a recently-departed FSRU at its old terminal because GIIGNL is published months after year-end. Don't immediately treat as \\\"GIIGNL is wrong\\\" \\u2014 check whether GEM's record has the swap-out documented.\\n\\n### \\u00a75.3 Multi-terminal sites\\n\\nSome sites host multiple terminals (e.g. one country's main LNG hub). GIIGNL may aggregate or split differently from GEM. The matching algorithm's \\\"ambiguous match\\\" classification catches this \\u2014 it requires manual resolution before any action.\\n\\n### \\u00a75.4 Operating-but-not-yet-in-GIIGNL\\n\\nGIIGNL covers operating terminals through the report year. A terminal that started up in early calendar year covered by the report should appear; one that started in late Q4 of that year often doesn't. If a recently-started GEM `operating` terminal isn't in GIIGNL, check the GEM `ActualStartYear` \\u2014 if Q4 or later, expect it in next year's GIIGNL.\\n\\n### \\u00a75.5 Floating storage units (FSU/FRU) not in liquefaction or regasification tables\\n\\nFSU and FRU vessels are non-standard. GIIGNL handling varies. Check the terminal narrative sections for mentions rather than expecting tabular rows.\\n\\n### \\u00a75.6 The capacity numbers in GIIGNL's narrative don't always match its own tables\\n\\nGIIGNL's country narratives sometimes cite a different capacity number than the GIIGNL tabular row for the same terminal. When this happens, prefer the tabular value for the diff (it's the structured source) and log the narrative discrepancy as a GIIGNL errata.\\n\\n## \\u00a76 Pause-and-ask triggers\\n\\nStop and consult the user before proceeding when:\\n\\n- More than ~10% of matched rows have value disagreements \\u2192 systematic issue (GIIGNL methodology change, GEM schema misunderstanding, or extractor bug). Don't auto-route 100+ Update batches; review the pattern first.\\n- The extractor produces totals that diverge from GIIGNL's Key Figures by more than 2% \\u2192 likely missing rows. Don't proceed with an incomplete diff.\\n- GIIGNL-only findings exceed ~30 candidates \\u2192 may indicate a GEM coverage gap for a whole region, worth scoping a Discovery batch around it rather than treating as 30 individual discoveries.\\n- The GIIGNL report file is in an unexpected format (not the zip-of-images structure) \\u2192 extractor needs adjustment before proceeding.\\n- A country shows GIIGNL country-summary totals that diverge dramatically from the sum of GEM operating capacity for that country \\u2192 could be a country definition mismatch (e.g. one source includes a disputed territory) or a real coverage gap.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Appendix A \\u2014 GIIGNL-specific extraction rules\\n\\nThese are the rules that `giignl_extract.py` implements. They're documented here because they evolve with each GIIGNL edition.\\n\\n### A.1 Source format (2026 edition)\\n\\nThe 2026 GIIGNL Annual Report file is named `.pdf` but is actually a zip archive containing:\\n- 80 JPEG page images (`1.jpeg` through `80.jpeg`)\\n- 80 OCR text files (`1.txt` through `80.txt`)\\n- `manifest.json` with per-page metadata\\n\\nOCR text quality is decent for prose, structurally messy for tables (column boundaries lost, rows wrap). The extractor uses both:\\n- OCR text as primary source for narrative pages\\n- JPEG images via vision processing for tabular pages, with OCR text as a confirmation channel\\n\\n### A.2 Page sections (2026 edition)\\n\\n| Pages | Section | Use |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| 1-3 | Cover, profile, editorial | Skip |\\n| 4-7 | Key figures, narrative overview | Use Key Figures totals as extraction sanity check |\\n| 8-27 | Trade dynamics narrative | Skip for diff; informational |\\n| 28-31 | Liquefaction narrative | Use country sections as secondary signal for Discovery routing |\\n| 32-37 | **Liquefaction tables** | Primary extraction source for export terminal diff |\\n| 48-52 | Regasification narrative | Use country sections as secondary signal |\\n| 53-62 | **Regasification tables** | Primary extraction source for import terminal diff |\\n| 64-77 | Contracts, shipping, member info | Skip for diff |\\n\\nPage numbers may shift between editions \\u2014 always re-derive section boundaries from the report's TOC or by content-pattern detection.\\n\\n### A.3 Liquefaction table schema\\n\\nColumns observed in 2026:\\n1. Country (with subtotal MTPA shown for multi-project countries)\\n2. Project name (e.g. \\\"Arzew GL3Z\\\", \\\"NLNG T1\\\", \\\"Idku T2\\\")\\n3. Nominal capacity (MTPA, decimal)\\n4. Number of trains (integer, typically 1 per row since rows are per-train)\\n5. Number of tanks (integer)\\n6. Total storage capacity (liq m\\u00b3)\\n7. Owner(s) \\u2014 free text with percentages, e.g. \\\"Sonatrach\\\" or \\\"ENI 50%, EGAS 40%, EGPC 10%\\\"\\n8. Operator\\n9. MT-LT Buyer(s) \\u2014 comma-separated entities\\n10. Start date \\u2014 year only\\n\\nExtractor produces normalized CSV with columns:\\n- `_giignl_section` = \\\"liquefaction\\\"\\n- `_source_page` (integer)\\n- `country` (raw)\\n- `country_normalized` (per normalize.py)\\n- `project` (raw)\\n- `project_normalized` (lowercased, \\\"T1\\\"/\\\"Train 1\\\" unified)\\n- `facility_type` = \\\"export\\\"\\n- `capacity_mtpa` (float)\\n- `n_trains` (int)\\n- `n_tanks` (int)\\n- `storage_m3` (int)\\n- `owners_raw` (text)\\n- `owners_parsed` (list of {entity, pct})\\n- `operator` (text)\\n- `buyers_raw` (text)\\n- `buyers_parsed` (list of entities)\\n- `start_year` (int)\\n\\n### A.4 Regasification table schema\\n\\nColumns observed in 2026:\\n1. Market (country)\\n2. Site (with FSRU vessel name appended when applicable, e.g. \\\"Escobar / Excelerate Expedient (FSRU)\\\")\\n3. Concept (\\\"Onshore\\\" or \\\"Offshore\\\")\\n4. Number of tanks\\n5. Total capacity (liq m\\u00b3)\\n6. Number of vaporizers (may be N/A for FSRUs)\\n7. Nominal capacity (MTPA, decimal)\\n8. Owner \\u2014 free text, often split into \\\"Owner: X / Charterer: Y\\\" for FSRUs\\n9. Operator \\u2014 free text, often split for FSRUs as \\\"FSRU: X / Terminal: Y\\\"\\n10. Third Party Access (Yes/No/dash)\\n11. Additional Services offered (text or dash)\\n12. Start-up date \\u2014 year only\\n\\nExtractor produces normalized CSV with columns:\\n- `_giignl_section` = \\\"regasification\\\"\\n- `_source_page`\\n- `country` (raw and normalized)\\n- `site` (raw)\\n- `site_normalized`\\n- `facility_type` = \\\"import\\\"\\n- `is_floating` (bool, derived from \\\"FSRU\\\" or \\\"FLNG\\\" in site/concept)\\n- `vessel_name` (when floating, extracted from site text)\\n- `concept` = \\\"onshore\\\" | \\\"offshore\\\"\\n- `capacity_mtpa` (float)\\n- `n_tanks`, `storage_m3`, `n_vaporizers`\\n- `owners_raw`, `owners_parsed`\\n- `charterer` (when FSRU)\\n- `operator_raw`, `operator_parsed`\\n- `terminal_operator` (when FSRU has separate terminal operator)\\n- `tpa` (bool \\u2014 Third Party Access)\\n- `additional_services` (text)\\n- `start_year` (int)\\n\\n### A.5 Country subtotal rows\\n\\nGIIGNL inserts subtotal labels for some countries (e.g. \\\"Algeria 25.3 MTPA\\\"). The extractor:\\n- Detects subtotal rows by pattern: country name + capacity + \\\"MTPA\\\" without other fields\\n- Uses subtotals as a sanity check (sum of per-project rows in that country should match)\\n- Does NOT produce an output row for subtotals (they're metadata)\\n\\n### A.6 OCR artifact handling\\n\\nThe 2026 OCR shows these consistent artifacts:\\n- `\\\\u0002` characters appearing as soft-hyphen breaks within words (e.g. `Mids\\\\u0002cale` for \\\"Midscale\\\")\\n- Line breaks (`\\\\r\\\\n`) inserted mid-cell, especially in long owner descriptions\\n- Numbers occasionally split across lines (`125,\\\\n000` for \\\"125,000\\\")\\n- Capacity unit suffixes (\\\"MTPA\\\") rendered inconsistently\\n\\nThe extractor's text-cleanup pass:\\n1. Strip `\\\\u0002` characters\\n2. Re-join wrapped numeric values\\n3. Normalize whitespace\\n4. Re-attach orphaned units to preceding numbers\\n\\n### A.7 What to add for IGU (future)\\n\\nIGU's World LNG Report has different table layouts but the same conceptual content. The shared `report_diff.py` body works unchanged; only `igu_extract.py` differs from `giignl_extract.py`. Likely IGU-specific changes:\\n- Different section page ranges\\n- IGU often uses bcm/y as primary unit (convert via `capacity_normalize.py`)\\n- IGU's \\\"operating capacity\\\" definitions may differ from GIIGNL \\u2014 document in the IGU SOP appendix\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Quick-reference card\\n\\n| Step | Command |\\n|---|---|\\n| Pull GEM | `python pull_gem_db.py` |\\n| Extract GIIGNL | `python giignl_extract.py /mnt/project/GIIGNL*.pdf --output /home/claude/giignl_normalized.csv` |\\n| Verify extraction totals | Compare against GIIGNL Key Figures (524 MTPA liq / 1,247 MTPA regas for 2026 edition) |\\n| Run diff | `python report_diff.py --gem ... --report ... --output /home/claude/giignl_diff.json` |\\n| Verify URLs (for any pre-searched corroborating sources) | `python url_verifier.py <url> <expected...>` |\\n| Build staging xlsx | `python build_review_package.py --mode reconciliation --report giignl --year <YEAR>` |\\n| Sanity check | `python recalc.py <xlsx>` |\\n| Present | `present_files` |\\n\", \"filename\": \"/home/claude/work/lng_terminal_reconciliation_sop.md\"}"

Key things informed by looking at the actual GIIGNL content:\n\n**The structure that emerged from looking at real pages:**\n- GIIGNL data lives in two main table blocks (liquefaction p32-37, regasification p54-62) with country narratives between them\n- OCR is text-perfect for prose but structurally lossy for tables \u2014 column boundaries don't survive\n- The extraction needs to be **vision-assisted** (use the JPEG images via vision processing) with OCR text as a confirmation channel, not pure regex\n- Country subtotals and Key Figures totals provide built-in sanity checks for extraction completeness\n- FSRU info is embedded inline in regasification site names (e.g. \"Escobar / Excelerate Expedient (FSRU)\") \u2014 needs special parsing\n\n**Three things I'm flagging in this SOP that you should explicitly approve or push back on:**\n\n1. **GIIGNL is matched at the project level, not unit level.** GIIGNL aggregates per-site, GEM splits into units. So a 6-unit NLNG project in GEM matches one \"NLNG\" row in GIIGNL. The diff rolls GEM up to project totals for comparison. If the GEM per-unit breakdown doesn't sum to the GIIGNL number, *that* becomes a value-disagreement. This feels right but it does mean unit-level disagreements (where GEM's Train 1 is 3.3 MTPA and GIIGNL has it at 3.5 MTPA) can get washed out by the rollup.\n\n2. **No URL citation for GIIGNL rows.** The 80-page PDF has no per-row URLs, so the SOP says to cite as \"edition year + table name\" in a `report_citation` column rather than trying to URL-cite. The build script handles this differently from URL citations. If GEM expects URL-style citations even for report sources, the convention needs to change.\n\n3. **The \"GEM-only is usually expected\" default.** I'm treating GEM-only as the default benign outcome (because GEM covers proposed/construction/shelved/cancelled while GIIGNL only covers operating). Suspicious cases get flagged for review, but most GEM-only findings produce no work. If GEM staff would rather see all GEM-only findings actively reviewed, the default should flip.\n\n**One thing I want to be explicit about:** the `giignl_extract.py` script I described uses vision processing on the page JPEGs. That's an LLM call per page, which is slower and more expensive than pure regex but reliable. For 80 pages this is fine; for a future much larger report it might matter. I'll write the script that way unless you'd prefer a different approach.\n\nNext file in the queue is `lng_terminal_update_sop.md`. Proceed?",

      "description": "Draft the Update SOP \u2014 the bread-and-butter workflow for existing terminals",
      "file_text": "# LNG Terminals Update SOP\n\nLast revised: 2026-05 (rev 1, initial draft)\n\nOperational rules for updating existing terminals in the GEM LNG terminals database. This is the bread-and-butter workflow of the annual cycle: refreshing data on terminals already in the database, adding new timeline entries, filling blank `[ref]` citations, and processing stale-sweep flags.\n\nThe methodology doc (LNG Terminals Manual) is authoritative for the underlying research rules. This SOP is operational \u2014 describes how to execute the work, citing the methodology rather than restating it.\n\n## \u00a71 When to run this SOP\n\nTrigger conditions:\n- Triage SOP has selected a country/region for update this batch\n- A reconciliation batch produced `giignl_to_action` findings routed to Update\n- The user explicitly requests an update batch (\"refresh the Japan terminals\", \"fill blank Capacity refs for the EU rows\")\n- Stale-sweep flagged units passing dormancy thresholds (inferred shelved at 2y, inferred cancelled at 4y)\n- A specific news event triggers a known-needed update (a recent FID announcement, a confirmed shelving, a vessel reassignment)\n\n## \u00a72 Confirm parameters at batch start\n\nBefore any tool runs, confirm:\n\n1. **Scope** \u2014 which terminals are in scope. Options:\n   - A country or set of countries (e.g. \"all Japan terminals\")\n   - A status filter (e.g. \"all `proposed` units globally with `LastUpdated > 12 months`\")\n   - A list of specific UnitIDs (from reconciliation routing or user-supplied)\n   - A field focus (e.g. \"all blank `Capacity [ref]` paired with populated Capacity\")\n2. **Sub-type focus** \u2014 which of the four update sub-types is primary for this batch (see \u00a73). Many batches mix them, but understanding the primary type guides time allocation.\n3. **Depth** \u2014 light refresh (verify current data, fill blank refs) vs deep refresh (re-research from sources, propose value changes). Light is faster, lower-risk, appropriate for `operating` units in stable markets. Deep is needed when triage signals a country has been neglected or when a major development is suspected.\n4. **Whether timeline pulls are anticipated** \u2014 any status change requires `fetch_timeline.py` per unit. If many status changes are expected (e.g. processing a backlog of confirmed shelvings), allocate batch time accordingly \u2014 this is the slowest part of the workflow.\n5. **FSRU handling** \u2014 if scope includes FSRU terminals, the FSRU sync rule applies (SKILL.md). Cross-check against the carrier project backend at batch end.\n\nThese parameters get written into the staging xlsx README sheet.\n\n## \u00a73 The four update sub-types\n\nMost batches mix these, but it helps to understand each as a distinct recipe.\n\n### \u00a73.1 [ref]-fill (carrier-project parallel)\n\nDirect port of the carrier [ref]-fill workflow. For each row in scope:\n- Identify `[ref]` columns that are blank AND have populated paired data values\n- Source-search for URLs that contain the value verbatim\n- Apply the URL verification gate (\u00a77)\n- Stage the fill with appropriate confidence color\n\nPriority columns by yield (from `gem_db_schema.md`):\n1. `Capacity [ref]` \u2014 86% blank, paired with `CapacityinMtpa` which is densely populated\n2. `ConstructionDate [ref]` \u2014 78% blank, paired with `ConstructionYear`\n3. `ProposalDate [ref]` \u2014 49% blank, paired with `ProposalYear`\n4. `Operator [ref]` \u2014 66% blank, paired with `Operator`\n5. `Cost [ref]` \u2014 88% blank, paired with `Cost`\n6. `StartDate [ref]` \u2014 32% blank, paired with `ActualStartYear`\n7. `Status [ref]` \u2014 24% blank, paired with `Status`\n\n**Rule F (no orphan citations) applies** \u2014 never fill a `[ref]` without a paired data value in the same row. The methodology FAQ confirms: a citation must support a specific data point.\n\n### \u00a73.2 Status / timeline updates\n\nAdding a new timeline entry, changing current status, or correcting a prior entry. **The most rule-bound sub-type** \u2014 `lifecycle_rules.md` governs end-to-end.\n\nWorkflow:\n1. `python fetch_timeline.py <UnitID>` \u2014 pull the existing timeline from the live DB (mandatory; the export doesn't contain it)\n2. Verify the proposed change is a legal state transition (`lifecycle_rules.md` \"Legal state transitions\")\n3. If adding a planned entry, locate the correct insertion point (typically after the most recent matching actual)\n4. If adding an actual entry, append to the bottom of the timeline\n5. Backfill the corresponding anchor year column if it's blank (e.g. confirming construction start \u2192 populate `ConstructionYear` if blank)\n6. Backfill the paired `[ref]` column for the anchor year\n7. Stage in `status_timeline_additions` sheet AND update the unit row in `updates` sheet\n\nSpecial cases per `lifecycle_rules.md`:\n- **Inferred shelved/cancelled additions** \u2014 substatus `inferred 2 y` or `inferred 4 y`; datasource can re-use the source for the latest active entry per methodology FAQ\n- **Shelved \u2192 cancelled escalation** \u2014 substatus `confirmed` (not `inferred`) per methodology FAQ; same datasource as the prior shelved entry\n- **Dead-and-revived** \u2014 same unit (new `proposed` entry) if same fundamental proposal; new unit if significantly different\n- **FID milestone** \u2014 separate timeline entry with substatus `actual` or `planned`; does NOT change unit Status\n\n### \u00a73.3 Value updates (capacity, cost, ownership, etc.)\n\nMost source-search-intensive sub-type. Adding or changing data values where the change isn't a status transition. Common cases:\n\n- **Capacity revision** \u2014 debottlenecking, expansion of a single train, restatement of nameplate. Use `capacity_normalize.py` for any unit conversion. Per methodology, range values store the max in the spreadsheet with the range in the wiki Background section.\n- **Cost addition or update** \u2014 new cost figure published, or year-stamp + currency conversion to USD/EUR. Methodology requires `CostYear` to be the publication year of the source for FX conversion purposes.\n- **Ownership change** \u2014 new operator, equity stake change, JV restructuring. Run `entity_lookup.py` for every new entity name; if creating a new entity, add to `entity_additions` sheet.\n- **FSRU vessel change** \u2014 vessel swap-out at an FSRU terminal. Triggers FSRU sync rule (SKILL.md). The prior vessel typically gets a status timeline entry on its associated terminal row (idled/retired); the new vessel gets entered on the receiving terminal row.\n- **Location refinement** \u2014 coordinates becoming more precise (e.g. from `approximate` to `exact`). Always update `Accuracy` along with lat/lng.\n\nFor each value update:\n- Source-search per \u00a74\n- URL-verify per \u00a77\n- Apply confidence color per \u00a76\n- Stage in `updates` sheet\n\n### \u00a73.4 Stale-driven sweeps\n\nProcessing `stale_sweep.py` output. Mechanical compared to the others \u2014 the rule is in `lifecycle_rules.md`, the work is mostly verification + entry.\n\nFor each flagged unit:\n1. Quick news search to confirm genuine dormancy (sometimes units are stale because of researcher capacity, not because the project is dormant)\n2. If genuinely dormant, follow the \u00a73.2 timeline-update workflow with substatus `inferred 2 y` or `inferred 4 y`\n3. If active development is found, the result is a regular value/status update (\u00a73.2 or \u00a73.3), and the stale flag is incidentally cleared by virtue of `LastUpdated` becoming current\n\nBatches that are dominated by stale-sweep tend to be high-throughput, low-research-depth.\n\n## \u00a74 Source-search strategy by field\n\nDifferent fields have different best-source-tiers. Use `source_roster.md` for the full ranked list; this is the field-specific quick reference.\n\n| Field | Best primary | Best corroborator | Caution |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Status (sponsor announcement) | Sponsor IR / press release | Reuters, Bloomberg, S&P Global | Trade press sometimes leads sponsor IR by hours-days |\n| Capacity (nameplate) | Sponsor IR + project filings (FERC/DOE/EU PCI) | GIIGNL annual report, sponsor presentations | Operational capacity \u2260 nameplate; methodology says use nameplate |\n| Construction start | Sponsor PR + ground-breaking news | Trade press, regulator approval dates | \"Site prep\" vs \"active construction\" is fuzzy \u2014 see methodology |\n| FID | Sponsor IR (definitive) | S&P Global, Reuters | \"Pre-FID with funding lined up\" \u2260 FID; methodology says only mark FID with explicit announcement |\n| Cost | Sponsor IR + regulatory filings (FERC, EU PCI portal) | Trade press estimates | Always record `CostYear` = publication year of source; FX conversion needs this |\n| Ownership | Sponsor IR + regulatory filings + entity registries | Trade press, recent annual reports | Immediate owner vs ultimate parent \u2014 keep distinct per schema |\n| Operator | Sponsor IR + regulatory filings | Trade press | Sometimes Owner \u2260 Operator for FSRUs |\n| Location coordinates | Regulator approval docs (FERC, EU PCI), satellite imagery | Sponsor maps | Wiki coordinates are sometimes stale; verify against satellite |\n| FSRU vessel name | Marine traffic services (marinetraffic.org, vesselfinder), sponsor PR | Trade press | Vessel reassignments happen mid-year; check timeline carefully |\n| FSRU vessel IMO | Marine traffic services | Class society registries (DNV, ABS, LR, KR, ClassNK) | FSRU sync rule cross-check |\n| Pipelines / PowerPlantsSupplied | Operator IR, regulatory filings | Trade press, country regulator | Often missing from primary sources; secondary sources fill gaps |\n| CCS | Sponsor sustainability reports, sponsor PR | Trade press | New priority for 2026; data is sparse |\n\nFor country-specific sources, consult `country_research_notes.md`. Contribute findings back to that file as part of the batch.\n\n## \u00a75 Cluster coherence (Rule E from the carrier project, adapted)\n\nWhen a single URL is used as the citation for multiple `[ref]` cells across a project (or across multiple units within a project), the URL must be **cluster-coherent**: it must verifiably reference the project AND contain the specific values being cited.\n\nA URL that mentions \"Sabine Pass\" and \"23 MTPA\" supports citing capacity for Sabine Pass. It does NOT support citing capacity for the adjacent Cameron LNG terminal, even if the article briefly mentions Cameron.\n\nFor multi-unit projects:\n- A project-level URL (covering all units) is fine for project-level fields\n- A unit-specific URL (covering only Train 3, say) is only valid for that unit's data\n- The build script should track which URLs cite which units to catch over-attribution\n\nThis is operationally identical to Rule E from the carrier [ref]-fill SOP, and `url_verifier.py` enforces it via the expected-content check.\n\n## \u00a76 Confidence labeling\n\nPer SKILL.md, the color scheme is:\n\n- **Green** \u2014 High confidence: primary/regulatory source (sponsor IR, FERC, DOE, EU PCI portal, national regulator) OR two independent corroborating Tier 1 sources agreeing on the value\n- **Yellow** \u2014 Entity-level confirmation but value implied, contested, or from a single non-primary source\n- **Red** \u2014 Single weak source. **Prefer leaving the cell blank** and logging in `qa_review` rather than staging red. Per the carrier project convention, red is a signal that work is needed, not that the work is done.\n- **Blue** \u2014 Value unchanged from existing DB value but re-verified this batch. The \"no changes\" outcome at cell granularity.\n\nConfidence applies per cell, not per row. A row might have a green Status update, a yellow Capacity revision, and blue confirmations on Owner and Location.\n\n### \u00a76.1 GIIGNL and IGU as sources\n\nGIIGNL and IGU are Tier 1 but not authoritative. Per the methodology FAQ: \"if we find a more specific or current source on a terminal that conflicts with the report, that source/data should take priority.\" A value supported by GIIGNL alone is yellow; supported by GIIGNL + a sponsor IR confirmation is green.\n\n### \u00a76.2 The blue convention specifically\n\nBlue is more important for terminals than for carriers. The methodology has a \"no changes\" outcome in the Record of Full Updates field, and many terminal updates are confirmations rather than changes. Using blue to mark \"checked, no change\" makes the staging xlsx review faster: the reviewer can scan for non-blue cells (where actual work happened) rather than reading every row.\n\nA cell is colored blue when:\n- The agent searched for current information\n- The current sources confirm the existing DB value\n- The `[ref]` is already populated (or got populated in this batch)\n- The unit's `LastUpdated` will be bumped to the batch date\n\nIf the agent searched but did NOT find a confirming source, the cell stays uncolored \u2014 that's a research gap, not a confirmation.\n\n## \u00a77 URL verification gate (mandatory)\n\nEvery URL staged in the xlsx must pass `url_verifier.py` before the batch is presented. No exceptions, even for URLs that worked in prior batches \u2014 URLs decay, paywalls change, soft-errors happen.\n\n```bash\npython url_verifier.py <url> <expected_string_1> <expected_string_2> ...\n```\n\nThe verifier checks:\n1. HTTP 200 (not 4xx/5xx)\n2. Not a soft-error page (title doesn't contain \"404\", \"429\", \"Just a moment\" (Cloudflare), etc.)\n3. Body contains every `expected_string` (case-insensitive)\n\n`expected_string` arguments should include the **terminal name**, the **value being cited**, and ideally the **owner or country** for cluster coherence per \u00a75. Examples:\n- For a capacity citation: `<url> \"Sabine Pass\" \"23 MTPA\"`\n- For a status update: `<url> \"Cameron LNG\" \"construction\" \"Train 4\"`\n- For an ownership change: `<url> \"Plaquemines\" \"Venture Global\" \"Excelerate\"`\n\nVerification failures result in the URL being dropped from the citation. If the cell would be left blank as a result, the build script flags it in `qa_review` for human attention.\n\n### \u00a77.1 Specific source patterns and soft errors\n\nCommon soft-error patterns the verifier catches:\n- **Paywalled sources** (Reuters, S&P Global, Wall Street Journal): often return 200 with a stub body that says \"Subscribe to read more\" \u2014 the verifier catches this if the `expected_string` includes the value (which won't be in the stub)\n- **Cloudflare interstitials** (Riviera Maritime, sometimes LNG Prime): \"Just a moment...\" page with 200 status \u2014 caught by title check\n- **GIIGNL members-only links**: redirect to login with 200 \u2014 caught by absence of expected content\n- **Government archive pages** (regulator FOI archives, EU PCI portal): URL structure changes between portal redesigns; older URLs may 404 silently or redirect to a search page\n\nWhen the verifier flags a paywall stub for a Tier 1 source like Reuters, the workaround is to find an alternative source (often Reuters' free wire copy on a syndicated site) rather than to cite the paywall.\n\n### \u00a77.2 Pre-existing URL re-verification\n\nBefore staging any update that touches a row with existing `[ref]` URLs in unchanged cells, **re-verify the existing URLs** (whether or not the batch is editing them). This is the equivalent of the carrier project's \u00a73.8a 404 sweep. Rationale: a row that's getting a blue \"re-verified\" treatment on some cells should have its other citations confirmed too, since the reviewer will assume the row was checked in its entirety.\n\nExisting URLs that fail re-verification go in `qa_review` with proposed action: either find a replacement URL or blank the `[ref]` cell (and the paired data if Rule F requires it).\n\n## \u00a78 Entity discipline\n\nPer the methodology, GEM's entity system is shared across all trackers. Creating a duplicate entity is real cleanup work for the Ownership Team. Before staging any new Owner, Parent, Operator, VesselOwner, VesselParent, or VesselOperator:\n\n1. `python entity_lookup.py \"<entity name>\" \"<country>\"` \u2014 searches the existing entity DB\n2. If a match is found, use its existing entity ID (the schema's `Parent GEM Entity ID` column)\n3. If no match is found, add to `entity_additions` sheet with the lookup attempts logged\n4. The user reviews `entity_additions` before applying the batch; they create the new entity via the GEM UI and link it\n\nFor entity *name* variants (e.g. \"TotalEnergies\" vs \"Total Energies\" vs \"Total\"):\n- `entity_canonical_map.md` maps known variants to canonical names\n- New variants encountered in a batch get added to that file\n- The build script uses the canonical name when staging, with the original-as-found preserved in a `qa_review` log entry\n\n## \u00a79 Project-level vs unit-level edits\n\nPer `gem_db_schema.md`, fields fall into three classes: project-level (apply to all unit-rows), unit-level (apply only to the target unit-row), and mixed/context-dependent (decide per case).\n\nThe build script enforces:\n- **Project-level field edits** are applied to every unit-row of the project automatically. The staging xlsx shows the edit on one representative row in `updates` with a note \"project-level: applies to N unit-rows\".\n- **Unit-level field edits** are applied only to the targeted UnitID.\n- **Mixed-class field edits** trigger a read-before-write: the script checks current consistency across unit-rows.\n  - If currently consistent \u2192 apply to all unit-rows\n  - If currently inconsistent \u2192 apply only to the targeted unit-row and flag in `qa_review` for human review\n\nFor Owner specifically (one of the most common mixed-class fields), the inconsistency check should distinguish JV-structure cases (where different units genuinely have different owners, e.g. a project where Phase 2 added a new equity partner) from data-entry cases (where one unit's Owner is stale or wrong). Use the timeline + datasource dates to triage.\n\n## \u00a710 Out-of-scope fields (read-only)\n\nPer the methodology and `gem_db_schema.md`, these fields are **never written** by the build script:\n\n**Computed / rollup columns** (DB regenerates from underlying data):\n- `CapacityinMtpa`, `CapacityinBcm/y`\n- `TotImportLNGTerminalCapacityinMtpa`, `TotImportLNGTerminalCapacityinBcm/y`\n- `TotExportLNGTerminalCapacityinMtpa`, `TotExportLNGTerminalCapacityinBcm/y`\n- `CostUSD`, `CostEuro`\n- `TotKnownTerminalCostsUSD`, `TotTerminalCost [ref]`\n- `TerminalID`, `UnitID`, `Wiki`\n\n**Out-of-scope per methodology** (no longer updated as of 2026):\n- `PCINotes`, `PCI3`, `PCI4`, `PCI5`, `PCI6`\n- `LH2`, `NH3`, `SyntheticLNG`, `RetrofitProposed`\n- `AltFuelPrelimAgreement`, `AltFuelCallMarketInterest`\n\nIf a batch would otherwise want to write one of these (e.g. a source confirms a planned LH2 retrofit), record the finding in `qa_review` with a note that the field is out-of-scope \u2014 don't stage the edit.\n\n## \u00a711 Workflow (linear)\n\nPutting it together, a standard update batch looks like:\n\n1. **Confirm parameters** (\u00a72)\n2. **Materialize scripts** per SKILL.md\n3. `python pull_gem_db.py` \u2192 fresh CSV, column-index map. **Mandatory every batch.**\n4. `python dedup_index.py` \u2192 project + unit indexes\n5. `python stale_sweep.py` if the batch includes stale-driven work\n6. **For each unit in scope:**\n   a. Pull existing timeline with `fetch_timeline.py` if any status changes anticipated\n   b. Source-search per \u00a74 using `source_roster.md` and `country_research_notes.md`\n   c. Apply lifecycle rules from `lifecycle_rules.md`\n   d. Identify [ref]-fill targets per \u00a73.1\n   e. Identify value updates per \u00a73.3\n   f. Resolve any cluster-coherence questions per \u00a75\n7. `python url_verifier.py` on every staged URL (\u00a77)\n8. `python url_verifier.py` re-check on pre-existing URLs in touched rows (\u00a77.2)\n9. `python entity_lookup.py` for every new entity reference (\u00a78)\n10. `python capacity_normalize.py` for any capacity edits with unit conversion\n11. **If batch touches any FSRU terminal:** `python fsru_sync_check.py` (SKILL.md FSRU sync rule)\n12. `python build_review_package.py --mode update --batch-id <YYYYMMDD>` \u2192 staging xlsx\n13. `python recalc.py` \u2192 confirm zero formula errors\n14. `present_files`\n\n## \u00a712 Hard rules (these override anything below)\n\n- **Never modify the live GEM database.** Outputs are always staging xlsx for human review.\n- **Every URL passes the \u00a77 verification gate** \u2014 no exceptions.\n- **Pull a fresh GEM CSV at the start of every batch** (\u00a711.3).\n- **Re-derive the column-index map** from the fresh header row.\n- **No orphan `[ref]` cells** \u2014 never fill a `[ref]` without a paired data value (Rule F from the carrier project, methodology FAQ).\n- **Status timeline edits require pulling the existing timeline first** via `fetch_timeline.py` (\u00a73.2).\n- **Don't create duplicate entities** \u2014 run `entity_lookup.py` before staging any new owner/operator/parent (\u00a78).\n- **Out-of-scope fields are read-only** (\u00a710).\n- **Project-level field changes apply to ALL unit-rows of a multi-unit project** (\u00a79).\n- **Cluster coherence on every URL** \u2014 a URL must verifiably reference the project AND contain the value being cited (\u00a75).\n- **Never auto-apply values from GIIGNL or IGU** \u2014 they're Tier 1 sources but not authoritative (\u00a76.1). Methodology FAQ is explicit.\n- **FSRU edits trigger sync check** (\u00a711.11).\n\n## \u00a713 Pause-and-ask triggers\n\nStop and consult the user when:\n\n- A whole class of GEM values looks systematically wrong (suggests methodology misunderstanding or schema drift, not a research finding)\n- Source corroboration is too thin to support even yellow for a key field, even after Tier 1 + Tier 2 sources searched\n- A status change is proposed but the existing timeline shows the same transition was already entered (possible duplicate, possible legitimate restart)\n- A capacity update would change the project total by more than 20% (possible debottlenecking \u2014 but also possible source error)\n- An ownership update would change the controlling parent (possible acquisition \u2014 verify with regulatory filings before staging)\n- The FSRU sync check surfaces a reassignment that doesn't have a matching event on the carrier side\n- A unit's existing URLs all fail re-verification and no replacement sources are found (suggests the project may no longer be active)\n- An `entity_lookup` returns no match for an entity name that obviously should exist (suggests a search issue or a genuine gap requiring user judgment)\n\n---\n\n## Quick-reference card\n\n| Sub-type | Primary action | Required scripts |\n|---|---|---|\n| [ref]-fill | Fill blank refs paired with data | `url_verifier.py`, `build_review_package.py` |\n| Status / timeline | Add timeline entry, change Status | `fetch_timeline.py`, `status_timeline.py`, `build_review_package.py` |\n| Value update | Add/change data values | `url_verifier.py`, `entity_lookup.py`, `capacity_normalize.py` (if applicable), `build_review_package.py` |\n| Stale sweep | Process inferred shelved/cancelled | `stale_sweep.py`, `fetch_timeline.py`, `build_review_package.py` |\n\n| Color | Meaning | When to use |\n|---|---|---|\n| Green | Primary source or 2+ corroborating Tier 1 | Default for sponsor IR, regulator filings |\n| Yellow | Single non-primary, or value implied | GIIGNL alone, single trade press article |\n| Red | Single weak source | Prefer blank; log in qa_review |\n| Blue | Re-verified,       "json_block": "{\"language\": \"markdown\", \"code\": \"# LNG Terminals Update SOP\\n\\nLast revised: 2026-05 (rev 1, initial draft)\\n\\nOperational rules for updating existing terminals in the GEM LNG terminals database. This is the bread-and-butter workflow of the annual cycle: refreshing data on terminals already in the database, adding new timeline entries, filling blank `[ref]` citations, and processing stale-sweep flags.\\n\\nThe methodology doc (LNG Terminals Manual) is authoritative for the underlying research rules. This SOP is operational \\u2014 describes how to execute the work, citing the methodology rather than restating it.\\n\\n## \\u00a71 When to run this SOP\\n\\nTrigger conditions:\\n- Triage SOP has selected a country/region for update this batch\\n- A reconciliation batch produced `giignl_to_action` findings routed to Update\\n- The user explicitly requests an update batch (\\\"refresh the Japan terminals\\\", \\\"fill blank Capacity refs for the EU rows\\\")\\n- Stale-sweep flagged units passing dormancy thresholds (inferred shelved at 2y, inferred cancelled at 4y)\\n- A specific news event triggers a known-needed update (a recent FID announcement, a confirmed shelving, a vessel reassignment)\\n\\n## \\u00a72 Confirm parameters at batch start\\n\\nBefore any tool runs, confirm:\\n\\n1. **Scope** \\u2014 which terminals are in scope. Options:\\n   - A country or set of countries (e.g. \\\"all Japan terminals\\\")\\n   - A status filter (e.g. \\\"all `proposed` units globally with `LastUpdated > 12 months`\\\")\\n   - A list of specific UnitIDs (from reconciliation routing or user-supplied)\\n   - A field focus (e.g. \\\"all blank `Capacity [ref]` paired with populated Capacity\\\")\\n2. **Sub-type focus** \\u2014 which of the four update sub-types is primary for this batch (see \\u00a73). Many batches mix them, but understanding the primary type guides time allocation.\\n3. **Depth** \\u2014 light refresh (verify current data, fill blank refs) vs deep refresh (re-research from sources, propose value changes). Light is faster, lower-risk, appropriate for `operating` units in stable markets. Deep is needed when triage signals a country has been neglected or when a major development is suspected.\\n4. **Whether timeline pulls are anticipated** \\u2014 any status change requires `fetch_timeline.py` per unit. If many status changes are expected (e.g. processing a backlog of confirmed shelvings), allocate batch time accordingly \\u2014 this is the slowest part of the workflow.\\n5. **FSRU handling** \\u2014 if scope includes FSRU terminals, the FSRU sync rule applies (SKILL.md). Cross-check against the carrier project backend at batch end.\\n\\nThese parameters get written into the staging xlsx README sheet.\\n\\n## \\u00a73 The four update sub-types\\n\\nMost batches mix these, but it helps to understand each as a distinct recipe.\\n\\n### \\u00a73.1 [ref]-fill (carrier-project parallel)\\n\\nDirect port of the carrier [ref]-fill workflow. For each row in scope:\\n- Identify `[ref]` columns that are blank AND have populated paired data values\\n- Source-search for URLs that contain the value verbatim\\n- Apply the URL verification gate (\\u00a77)\\n- Stage the fill with appropriate confidence color\\n\\nPriority columns by yield (from `gem_db_schema.md`):\\n1. `Capacity [ref]` \\u2014 86% blank, paired with `CapacityinMtpa` which is densely populated\\n2. `ConstructionDate [ref]` \\u2014 78% blank, paired with `ConstructionYear`\\n3. `ProposalDate [ref]` \\u2014 49% blank, paired with `ProposalYear`\\n4. `Operator [ref]` \\u2014 66% blank, paired with `Operator`\\n5. `Cost [ref]` \\u2014 88% blank, paired with `Cost`\\n6. `StartDate [ref]` \\u2014 32% blank, paired with `ActualStartYear`\\n7. `Status [ref]` \\u2014 24% blank, paired with `Status`\\n\\n**Rule F (no orphan citations) applies** \\u2014 never fill a `[ref]` without a paired data value in the same row. The methodology FAQ confirms: a citation must support a specific data point.\\n\\n### \\u00a73.2 Status / timeline updates\\n\\nAdding a new timeline entry, changing current status, or correcting a prior entry. **The most rule-bound sub-type** \\u2014 `lifecycle_rules.md` governs end-to-end.\\n\\nWorkflow:\\n1. `python fetch_timeline.py <UnitID>` \\u2014 pull the existing timeline from the live DB (mandatory; the export doesn't contain it)\\n2. Verify the proposed change is a legal state transition (`lifecycle_rules.md` \\\"Legal state transitions\\\")\\n3. If adding a planned entry, locate the correct insertion point (typically after the most recent matching actual)\\n4. If adding an actual entry, append to the bottom of the timeline\\n5. Backfill the corresponding anchor year column if it's blank (e.g. confirming construction start \\u2192 populate `ConstructionYear` if blank)\\n6. Backfill the paired `[ref]` column for the anchor year\\n7. Stage in `status_timeline_additions` sheet AND update the unit row in `updates` sheet\\n\\nSpecial cases per `lifecycle_rules.md`:\\n- **Inferred shelved/cancelled additions** \\u2014 substatus `inferred 2 y` or `inferred 4 y`; datasource can re-use the source for the latest active entry per methodology FAQ\\n- **Shelved \\u2192 cancelled escalation** \\u2014 substatus `confirmed` (not `inferred`) per methodology FAQ; same datasource as the prior shelved entry\\n- **Dead-and-revived** \\u2014 same unit (new `proposed` entry) if same fundamental proposal; new unit if significantly different\\n- **FID milestone** \\u2014 separate timeline entry with substatus `actual` or `planned`; does NOT change unit Status\\n\\n### \\u00a73.3 Value updates (capacity, cost, ownership, etc.)\\n\\nMost source-search-intensive sub-type. Adding or changing data values where the change isn't a status transition. Common cases:\\n\\n- **Capacity revision** \\u2014 debottlenecking, expansion of a single train, restatement of nameplate. Use `capacity_normalize.py` for any unit conversion. Per methodology, range values store the max in the spreadsheet with the range in the wiki Background section.\\n- **Cost addition or update** \\u2014 new cost figure published, or year-stamp + currency conversion to USD/EUR. Methodology requires `CostYear` to be the publication year of the source for FX conversion purposes.\\n- **Ownership change** \\u2014 new operator, equity stake change, JV restructuring. Run `entity_lookup.py` for every new entity name; if creating a new entity, add to `entity_additions` sheet.\\n- **FSRU vessel change** \\u2014 vessel swap-out at an FSRU terminal. Triggers FSRU sync rule (SKILL.md). The prior vessel typically gets a status timeline entry on its associated terminal row (idled/retired); the new vessel gets entered on the receiving terminal row.\\n- **Location refinement** \\u2014 coordinates becoming more precise (e.g. from `approximate` to `exact`). Always update `Accuracy` along with lat/lng.\\n\\nFor each value update:\\n- Source-search per \\u00a74\\n- URL-verify per \\u00a77\\n- Apply confidence color per \\u00a76\\n- Stage in `updates` sheet\\n\\n### \\u00a73.4 Stale-driven sweeps\\n\\nProcessing `stale_sweep.py` output. Mechanical compared to the others \\u2014 the rule is in `lifecycle_rules.md`, the work is mostly verification + entry.\\n\\nFor each flagged unit:\\n1. Quick news search to confirm genuine dormancy (sometimes units are stale because of researcher capacity, not because the project is dormant)\\n2. If genuinely dormant, follow the \\u00a73.2 timeline-update workflow with substatus `inferred 2 y` or `inferred 4 y`\\n3. If active development is found, the result is a regular value/status update (\\u00a73.2 or \\u00a73.3), and the stale flag is incidentally cleared by virtue of `LastUpdated` becoming current\\n\\nBatches that are dominated by stale-sweep tend to be high-throughput, low-research-depth.\\n\\n## \\u00a74 Source-search strategy by field\\n\\nDifferent fields have different best-source-tiers. Use `source_roster.md` for the full ranked list; this is the field-specific quick reference.\\n\\n| Field | Best primary | Best corroborator | Caution |\\n|---|---|---|---|\\n| Status (sponsor announcement) | Sponsor IR / press release | Reuters, Bloomberg, S&P Global | Trade press sometimes leads sponsor IR by hours-days |\\n| Capacity (nameplate) | Sponsor IR + project filings (FERC/DOE/EU PCI) | GIIGNL annual report, sponsor presentations | Operational capacity \\u2260 nameplate; methodology says use nameplate |\\n| Construction start | Sponsor PR + ground-breaking news | Trade press, regulator approval dates | \\\"Site prep\\\" vs \\\"active construction\\\" is fuzzy \\u2014 see methodology |\\n| FID | Sponsor IR (definitive) | S&P Global, Reuters | \\\"Pre-FID with funding lined up\\\" \\u2260 FID; methodology says only mark FID with explicit announcement |\\n| Cost | Sponsor IR + regulatory filings (FERC, EU PCI portal) | Trade press estimates | Always record `CostYear` = publication year of source; FX conversion needs this |\\n| Ownership | Sponsor IR + regulatory filings + entity registries | Trade press, recent annual reports | Immediate owner vs ultimate parent \\u2014 keep distinct per schema |\\n| Operator | Sponsor IR + regulatory filings | Trade press | Sometimes Owner \\u2260 Operator for FSRUs |\\n| Location coordinates | Regulator approval docs (FERC, EU PCI), satellite imagery | Sponsor maps | Wiki coordinates are sometimes stale; verify against satellite |\\n| FSRU vessel name | Marine traffic services (marinetraffic.org, vesselfinder), sponsor PR | Trade press | Vessel reassignments happen mid-year; check timeline carefully |\\n| FSRU vessel IMO | Marine traffic services | Class society registries (DNV, ABS, LR, KR, ClassNK) | FSRU sync rule cross-check |\\n| Pipelines / PowerPlantsSupplied | Operator IR, regulatory filings | Trade press, country regulator | Often missing from primary sources; secondary sources fill gaps |\\n| CCS | Sponsor sustainability reports, sponsor PR | Trade press | New priority for 2026; data is sparse |\\n\\nFor country-specific sources, consult `country_research_notes.md`. Contribute findings back to that file as part of the batch.\\n\\n## \\u00a75 Cluster coherence (Rule E from the carrier project, adapted)\\n\\nWhen a single URL is used as the citation for multiple `[ref]` cells across a project (or across multiple units within a project), the URL must be **cluster-coherent**: it must verifiably reference the project AND contain the specific values being cited.\\n\\nA URL that mentions \\\"Sabine Pass\\\" and \\\"23 MTPA\\\" supports citing capacity for Sabine Pass. It does NOT support citing capacity for the adjacent Cameron LNG terminal, even if the article briefly mentions Cameron.\\n\\nFor multi-unit projects:\\n- A project-level URL (covering all units) is fine for project-level fields\\n- A unit-specific URL (covering only Train 3, say) is only valid for that unit's data\\n- The build script should track which URLs cite which units to catch over-attribution\\n\\nThis is operationally identical to Rule E from the carrier [ref]-fill SOP, and `url_verifier.py` enforces it via the expected-content check.\\n\\n## \\u00a76 Confidence labeling\\n\\nPer SKILL.md, the color scheme is:\\n\\n- **Green** \\u2014 High confidence: primary/regulatory source (sponsor IR, FERC, DOE, EU PCI portal, national regulator) OR two independent corroborating Tier 1 sources agreeing on the value\\n- **Yellow** \\u2014 Entity-level confirmation but value implied, contested, or from a single non-primary source\\n- **Red** \\u2014 Single weak source. **Prefer leaving the cell blank** and logging in `qa_review` rather than staging red. Per the carrier project convention, red is a signal that work is needed, not that the work is done.\\n- **Blue** \\u2014 Value unchanged from existing DB value but re-verified this batch. The \\\"no changes\\\" outcome at cell granularity.\\n\\nConfidence applies per cell, not per row. A row might have a green Status update, a yellow Capacity revision, and blue confirmations on Owner and Location.\\n\\n### \\u00a76.1 GIIGNL and IGU as sources\\n\\nGIIGNL and IGU are Tier 1 but not authoritative. Per the methodology FAQ: \\\"if we find a more specific or current source on a terminal that conflicts with the report, that source/data should take priority.\\\" A value supported by GIIGNL alone is yellow; supported by GIIGNL + a sponsor IR confirmation is green.\\n\\n### \\u00a76.2 The blue convention specifically\\n\\nBlue is more important for terminals than for carriers. The methodology has a \\\"no changes\\\" outcome in the Record of Full Updates field, and many terminal updates are confirmations rather than changes. Using blue to mark \\\"checked, no change\\\" makes the staging xlsx review faster: the reviewer can scan for non-blue cells (where actual work happened) rather than reading every row.\\n\\nA cell is colored blue when:\\n- The agent searched for current information\\n- The current sources confirm the existing DB value\\n- The `[ref]` is already populated (or got populated in this batch)\\n- The unit's `LastUpdated` will be bumped to the batch date\\n\\nIf the agent searched but did NOT find a confirming source, the cell stays uncolored \\u2014 that's a research gap, not a confirmation.\\n\\n## \\u00a77 URL verification gate (mandatory)\\n\\nEvery URL staged in the xlsx must pass `url_verifier.py` before the batch is presented. No exceptions, even for URLs that worked in prior batches \\u2014 URLs decay, paywalls change, soft-errors happen.\\n\\n```bash\\npython url_verifier.py <url> <expected_string_1> <expected_string_2> ...\\n```\\n\\nThe verifier checks:\\n1. HTTP 200 (not 4xx/5xx)\\n2. Not a soft-error page (title doesn't contain \\\"404\\\", \\\"429\\\", \\\"Just a moment\\\" (Cloudflare), etc.)\\n3. Body contains every `expected_string` (case-insensitive)\\n\\n`expected_string` arguments should include the **terminal name**, the **value being cited**, and ideally the **owner or country** for cluster coherence per \\u00a75. Examples:\\n- For a capacity citation: `<url> \\\"Sabine Pass\\\" \\\"23 MTPA\\\"`\\n- For a status update: `<url> \\\"Cameron LNG\\\" \\\"construction\\\" \\\"Train 4\\\"`\\n- For an ownership change: `<url> \\\"Plaquemines\\\" \\\"Venture Global\\\" \\\"Excelerate\\\"`\\n\\nVerification failures result in the URL being dropped from the citation. If the cell would be left blank as a result, the build script flags it in `qa_review` for human attention.\\n\\n### \\u00a77.1 Specific source patterns and soft errors\\n\\nCommon soft-error patterns the verifier catches:\\n- **Paywalled sources** (Reuters, S&P Global, Wall Street Journal): often return 200 with a stub body that says \\\"Subscribe to read more\\\" \\u2014 the verifier catches this if the `expected_string` includes the value (which won't be in the stub)\\n- **Cloudflare interstitials** (Riviera Maritime, sometimes LNG Prime): \\\"Just a moment...\\\" page with 200 status \\u2014 caught by title check\\n- **GIIGNL members-only links**: redirect to login with 200 \\u2014 caught by absence of expected content\\n- **Government archive pages** (regulator FOI archives, EU PCI portal): URL structure changes between portal redesigns; older URLs may 404 silently or redirect to a search page\\n\\nWhen the verifier flags a paywall stub for a Tier 1 source like Reuters, the workaround is to find an alternative source (often Reuters' free wire copy on a syndicated site) rather than to cite the paywall.\\n\\n### \\u00a77.2 Pre-existing URL re-verification\\n\\nBefore staging any update that touches a row with existing `[ref]` URLs in unchanged cells, **re-verify the existing URLs** (whether or not the batch is editing them). This is the equivalent of the carrier project's \\u00a73.8a 404 sweep. Rationale: a row that's getting a blue \\\"re-verified\\\" treatment on some cells should have its other citations confirmed too, since the reviewer will assume the row was checked in its entirety.\\n\\nExisting URLs that fail re-verification go in `qa_review` with proposed action: either find a replacement URL or blank the `[ref]` cell (and the paired data if Rule F requires it).\\n\\n## \\u00a78 Entity discipline\\n\\nPer the methodology, GEM's entity system is shared across all trackers. Creating a duplicate entity is real cleanup work for the Ownership Team. Before staging any new Owner, Parent, Operator, VesselOwner, VesselParent, or VesselOperator:\\n\\n1. `python entity_lookup.py \\\"<entity name>\\\" \\\"<country>\\\"` \\u2014 searches the existing entity DB\\n2. If a match is found, use its existing entity ID (the schema's `Parent GEM Entity ID` column)\\n3. If no match is found, add to `entity_additions` sheet with the lookup attempts logged\\n4. The user reviews `entity_additions` before applying the batch; they create the new entity via the GEM UI and link it\\n\\nFor entity *name* variants (e.g. \\\"TotalEnergies\\\" vs \\\"Total Energies\\\" vs \\\"Total\\\"):\\n- `entity_canonical_map.md` maps known variants to canonical names\\n- New variants encountered in a batch get added to that file\\n- The build script uses the canonical name when staging, with the original-as-found preserved in a `qa_review` log entry\\n\\n## \\u00a79 Project-level vs unit-level edits\\n\\nPer `gem_db_schema.md`, fields fall into three classes: project-level (apply to all unit-rows), unit-level (apply only to the target unit-row), and mixed/context-dependent (decide per case).\\n\\nThe build script enforces:\\n- **Project-level field edits** are applied to every unit-row of the project automatically. The staging xlsx shows the edit on one representative row in `updates` with a note \\\"project-level: applies to N unit-rows\\\".\\n- **Unit-level field edits** are applied only to the targeted UnitID.\\n- **Mixed-class field edits** trigger a read-before-write: the script checks current consistency across unit-rows.\\n  - If currently consistent \\u2192 apply to all unit-rows\\n  - If currently inconsistent \\u2192 apply only to the targeted unit-row and flag in `qa_review` for human review\\n\\nFor Owner specifically (one of the most common mixed-class fields), the inconsistency check should distinguish JV-structure cases (where different units genuinely have different owners, e.g. a project where Phase 2 added a new equity partner) from data-entry cases (where one unit's Owner is stale or wrong). Use the timeline + datasource dates to triage.\\n\\n## \\u00a710 Out-of-scope fields (read-only)\\n\\nPer the methodology and `gem_db_schema.md`, these fields are **never written** by the build script:\\n\\n**Computed / rollup columns** (DB regenerates from underlying data):\\n- `CapacityinMtpa`, `CapacityinBcm/y`\\n- `TotImportLNGTerminalCapacityinMtpa`, `TotImportLNGTerminalCapacityinBcm/y`\\n- `TotExportLNGTerminalCapacityinMtpa`, `TotExportLNGTerminalCapacityinBcm/y`\\n- `CostUSD`, `CostEuro`\\n- `TotKnownTerminalCostsUSD`, `TotTerminalCost [ref]`\\n- `TerminalID`, `UnitID`, `Wiki`\\n\\n**Out-of-scope per methodology** (no longer updated as of 2026):\\n- `PCINotes`, `PCI3`, `PCI4`, `PCI5`, `PCI6`\\n- `LH2`, `NH3`, `SyntheticLNG`, `RetrofitProposed`\\n- `AltFuelPrelimAgreement`, `AltFuelCallMarketInterest`\\n\\nIf a batch would otherwise want to write one of these (e.g. a source confirms a planned LH2 retrofit), record the finding in `qa_review` with a note that the field is out-of-scope \\u2014 don't stage the edit.\\n\\n## \\u00a711 Workflow (linear)\\n\\nPutting it together, a standard update batch looks like:\\n\\n1. **Confirm parameters** (\\u00a72)\\n2. **Materialize scripts** per SKILL.md\\n3. `python pull_gem_db.py` \\u2192 fresh CSV, column-index map. **Mandatory every batch.**\\n4. `python dedup_index.py` \\u2192 project + unit indexes\\n5. `python stale_sweep.py` if the batch includes stale-driven work\\n6. **For each unit in scope:**\\n   a. Pull existing timeline with `fetch_timeline.py` if any status changes anticipated\\n   b. Source-search per \\u00a74 using `source_roster.md` and `country_research_notes.md`\\n   c. Apply lifecycle rules from `lifecycle_rules.md`\\n   d. Identify [ref]-fill targets per \\u00a73.1\\n   e. Identify value updates per \\u00a73.3\\n   f. Resolve any cluster-coherence questions per \\u00a75\\n7. `python url_verifier.py` on every staged URL (\\u00a77)\\n8. `python url_verifier.py` re-check on pre-existing URLs in touched rows (\\u00a77.2)\\n9. `python entity_lookup.py` for every new entity reference (\\u00a78)\\n10. `python capacity_normalize.py` for any capacity edits with unit conversion\\n11. **If batch touches any FSRU terminal:** `python fsru_sync_check.py` (SKILL.md FSRU sync rule)\\n12. `python build_review_package.py --mode update --batch-id <YYYYMMDD>` \\u2192 staging xlsx\\n13. `python recalc.py` \\u2192 confirm zero formula errors\\n14. `present_files`\\n\\n## \\u00a712 Hard rules (these override anything below)\\n\\n- **Never modify the live GEM database.** Outputs are always staging xlsx for human review.\\n- **Every URL passes the \\u00a77 verification gate** \\u2014 no exceptions.\\n- **Pull a fresh GEM CSV at the start of every batch** (\\u00a711.3).\\n- **Re-derive the column-index map** from the fresh header row.\\n- **No orphan `[ref]` cells** \\u2014 never fill a `[ref]` without a paired data value (Rule F from the carrier project, methodology FAQ).\\n- **Status timeline edits require pulling the existing timeline first** via `fetch_timeline.py` (\\u00a73.2).\\n- **Don't create duplicate entities** \\u2014 run `entity_lookup.py` before staging any new owner/operator/parent (\\u00a78).\\n- **Out-of-scope fields are read-only** (\\u00a710).\\n- **Project-level field changes apply to ALL unit-rows of a multi-unit project** (\\u00a79).\\n- **Cluster coherence on every URL** \\u2014 a URL must verifiably reference the project AND contain the value being cited (\\u00a75).\\n- **Never auto-apply values from GIIGNL or IGU** \\u2014 they're Tier 1 sources but not authoritative (\\u00a76.1). Methodology FAQ is explicit.\\n- **FSRU edits trigger sync check** (\\u00a711.11).\\n\\n## \\u00a713 Pause-and-ask triggers\\n\\nStop and consult the user when:\\n\\n- A whole class of GEM values looks systematically wrong (suggests methodology misunderstanding or schema drift, not a research finding)\\n- Source corroboration is too thin to support even yellow for a key field, even after Tier 1 + Tier 2 sources searched\\n- A status change is proposed but the existing timeline shows the same transition was already entered (possible duplicate, possible legitimate restart)\\n- A capacity update would change the project total by more than 20% (possible debottlenecking \\u2014 but also possible source error)\\n- An ownership update would change the controlling parent (possible acquisition \\u2014 verify with regulatory filings before staging)\\n- The FSRU sync check surfaces a reassignment that doesn't have a matching event on the carrier side\\n- A unit's existing URLs all fail re-verification and no replacement sources are found (suggests the project may no longer be active)\\n- An `entity_lookup` returns no match for an entity name that obviously should exist (suggests a search issue or a genuine gap requiring user judgment)\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Quick-reference card\\n\\n| Sub-type | Primary action | Required scripts |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| [ref]-fill | Fill blank refs paired with data | `url_verifier.py`, `build_review_package.py` |\\n| Status / timeline | Add timeline entry, change Status | `fetch_timeline.py`, `status_timeline.py`, `build_review_package.py` |\\n| Value update | Add/change data values | `url_verifier.py`, `entity_lookup.py`, `capacity_normalize.py` (if applicable), `build_review_package.py` |\\n| Stale sweep | corroborating Tier 1 | Default for sponsor IR, regulator filings |\\n| Yellow | Single non-primary, or value implied | GIIGNL alone, single trade press article |\\n| Red | Single weak source | Prefer
