      "description": "Draft the Discovery SOP \u2014 finding new LNG terminals not yet in the GEM database",
      "file_text": "# LNG Terminals Discovery SOP\n\nLast revised: 2026-05 (rev 1, initial draft)\n\nOperational rules for finding LNG terminals (both import and export, all scales except bunkering) that are NOT yet in the GEM database. Discovery feeds candidate terminals into a staging xlsx for human review and addition to the live DB.\n\nThe methodology doc (LNG Terminals Manual) is authoritative for what counts as a terminal, the \"sufficient information to add\" threshold, and how new units are named. This SOP is operational \u2014 describes how to execute the discovery work, citing the methodology rather than restating it.\n\n## \u00a71 When to run this SOP\n\nTrigger conditions:\n- Triage SOP has scoped a country/region for discovery work this batch\n- A reconciliation batch produced `giignl_to_action` findings routed to Discovery (GIIGNL-only candidates)\n- The user explicitly requests a discovery run for a country, region, or sponsor\n- A specific news event suggests new project activity in a region not covered by an upcoming Update batch (a major sponsor's quarterly announcement, a country opening a new round of bids)\n- A \"catch-up sweep\" after a long period without coverage of a particular region\n\n## \u00a72 Confirm parameters at batch start\n\nDiscovery is more sensitive to scope choices than Update, because the \"what's in scope?\" question genuinely affects what candidates surface. Confirm before any tool runs:\n\n1. **Geographic scope** \u2014 country, region, or global. Global discovery is expensive; if the user requests global, push back unless triage justifies it.\n2. **Project type scope** \u2014 import, export, or both. Defaults to both per the project-wide scope (excluding bunkering).\n3. **Lifecycle stage threshold** \u2014 how early-stage to accept candidates. Options:\n   - **Tight** (default): require the methodology's \"sufficient information to add\" \u2014 sponsor identified + approximate location + concrete step taken\n   - **Permissive**: include early-rumor-stage candidates in a `monitor_list` sheet for future tracking\n   - **Operating-only**: only accept candidates already commissioned (rare \u2014 usually combined with reconciliation backlog)\n4. **Time window** \u2014 how far back to search. Defaults to \"anything not in the current GEM export, regardless of age\" but practically the highest yield is announcements from the last 12-24 months.\n5. **FSRU handling** \u2014 if scope includes import discovery in countries with FSRU activity, sync rule applies (SKILL.md).\n6. **Reconciliation-fed candidates** \u2014 if any GIIGNL-only findings from a prior reconciliation are pending, list them in scope at batch start. Discovery for these is partly pre-done (GIIGNL provided the initial lead); workflow focuses on verification and threshold testing.\n\nThese parameters get written into the staging xlsx README sheet.\n\n## \u00a73 The \"sufficient information to add\" threshold\n\nPer the methodology FAQ, a candidate qualifies for addition to GEM when all three are present:\n\n1. **Sponsor identified** \u2014 a specific company or entity (not \"consortium being formed\" or \"TBD\")\n2. **Approximate location** \u2014 at minimum, a country + region/state/port (latitude/longitude can be approximate; methodology accepts `Accuracy = approximate`)\n3. **Concrete step taken** \u2014 beyond pure verbal intent. Examples that count: MOU signed, site selected, FEED contract awarded, environmental permit applied for, public consultation initiated, regulatory pre-filing, land lease secured.\n\nCandidates that fall short go in `monitor_list` (see \u00a75) with a note on which threshold elements are missing. This is the equivalent of the Update SOP's \"yellow \u2192 leave blank\" discipline: not everything we find should result in an add.\n\n**Edge cases:**\n- **Vague sponsor** (e.g. \"a Chinese consortium\") \u2014 fails the sponsor test. Monitor list.\n- **Multiple alternative sites under consideration** (e.g. \"Site A or Site B in Vietnam\") \u2014 usually fails the location test unless one is clearly the leading candidate per recent reporting.\n- **Verbal intent only** (e.g. \"X country's energy minister said the country will build an LNG import terminal by 2030\") \u2014 fails the concrete step test. Monitor list.\n- **Genuine pre-FID with sponsor, location, FEED contract** \u2014 passes. Add as `proposed`, FID status `Pre-FID` only if explicitly reported.\n- **Project announced years ago but no apparent activity since** \u2014 passes the threshold but enters as `shelved` with substatus `inferred 2 y` or `confirmed`. The age of the most recent news drives the status, not the age of the project itself.\n\n## \u00a74 The four-ring discovery model\n\nBorrowed from the carrier project's discovery structure, adapted for terminals. The rings are searched in order; later rings catch what earlier rings miss.\n\n### \u00a74.1 Ring A \u2014 country-level regulatory sweep\n\nThe most authoritative ring. National regulators publish concrete project information (filings, permits, environmental assessments) that establishes both existence and several key data fields at once.\n\nFor each country in scope, consult:\n\n- **United States**: FERC eLibrary (`elibrary.ferc.gov`) for import/export terminals; DOE Office of Fossil Energy & Carbon Management export authorizations\n- **European Union**: PCI list portal (`energy.ec.europa.eu`); per-country TSOs (e.g. GRTgaz for France, Snam for Italy)\n- **United Kingdom**: Ofgem decisions; Planning Inspectorate (NSIP project list)\n- **Canada**: CER (Canada Energy Regulator) for export licenses; provincial environmental assessment agencies (BC EAO, etc.)\n- **Australia**: NOPSEMA for offshore; state EPA decisions; AEMO gas statement of opportunities\n- **Japan**: METI announcements; JOGMEC strategic reserve plans\n- **South Korea**: MOTIE; KOGAS IR\n- **China**: NDRC press releases; CNPC, Sinopec, CNOOC quarterly disclosures; provincial development & reform commissions for inland regas\n- **India**: MOPNG; PNGRB tariff orders (which require regulatory filings before operation)\n- **Brazil**: ANP terminal authorizations; EPE planning documents\n- **Mexico**: CRE permits; SENER strategic outlooks\n- **Russia**: Limited public regulatory data post-sanctions; check IISS, FACTS Global Energy secondary coverage\n- **Middle East / Gulf**: state oil company IR (Saudi Aramco, ADNOC Gas, QatarEnergy); ENOC for UAE\n- **Africa**: country-by-country highly variable; check IEA Africa Energy Outlook, Reuters Africa, sponsor IR\n- **Southeast Asia**: per-country, e.g. Philippines DOE, Vietnam MOIT, Indonesia ESDM\n\nThis list is not exhaustive. `country_research_notes.md` is the working memory for country-specific regulator URLs, filing patterns, and update cadences. Contribute findings back to that file.\n\n### \u00a74.2 Ring B \u2014 trade press sweep\n\nFor each country/region in scope, search trade press for new-project announcements in the time window:\n\n- **Workhorses**: LNG Prime, Reuters Energy, S&P Global Commodity Insights, Argus Media, Upstream Online, Energy Intelligence\n- **Regional specialists**: Splash247 (shipping angle), Riviera Maritime Media (technical), Hellenic Shipping News (Europe), Hydrocarbons Africa, Energy Voice (UK)\n- **Tier 1b regulatory press**: en.sedaily.com (Korean DART proxies), iMarine (Asia)\n\nSearch patterns that work:\n- `\"LNG terminal\" \"<country>\" \"announced\" \"<year>\"`\n- `\"<country>\" \"regasification\" \"MOU\"`\n- `\"FSRU\" \"<country>\" \"deployment\"`\n- `\"<sponsor name>\" \"LNG\" \"<country>\"`\n- `\"<country>\" \"liquefaction\" \"FEED\"`\n\nTrade press often leads regulator filings by weeks-to-months for early-stage projects; regulators trail trade press but offer harder evidence.\n\n### \u00a74.3 Ring C \u2014 sponsor IR / corporate sweep\n\nFor sponsors known to be active in LNG, walk their IR materials directly. The methodology's \"established LNG developer\" list as a starting point:\n\n- **US-focused exporters**: Cheniere, Venture Global, NextDecade, Sempra, Freeport LNG, Tellurian, Energy Transfer\n- **Integrated majors**: TotalEnergies, Shell, BP, ExxonMobil, Chevron, ConocoPhillips, Eni\n- **Asian state-linked**: QatarEnergy, ADNOC Gas, Petronas, Pertamina, CNPC, Sinopec, CNOOC, KOGAS, JERA\n- **FSRU operators**: Excelerate Energy, H\u00f6egh Evi, BW LNG, Energos Infrastructure, Karpowership/KARMOL, New Fortress Energy\n- **Import-side**: ENGIE, Naturgy, Snam, Fluxys, Enagas, RWE, Uniper, Sempra Infrastructure\n\nFor each sponsor in scope:\n- IR press releases (last 12-24 months)\n- Quarterly earnings calls (transcripts via Seeking Alpha, sponsor IR site)\n- Annual reports / sustainability reports\n- Investor day decks (these often disclose pipeline projects pre-PR)\n\nSponsor IR is often the earliest credible signal \u2014 sponsors disclose to investors before broad press release.\n\n### \u00a74.4 Ring D \u2014 broader scan (optional, when prior rings underyield)\n\nWhen rings A-C don't surface enough candidates to justify the batch (or when scope is intentionally broad), expand to:\n\n- **Industry conference materials** (LNG2026, Gastech, World Gas Conference) \u2014 presenter lists often include emerging projects\n- **Lender / financier announcements** \u2014 JBIC, KEXIM, ECAs, multilateral development bank disclosures often pre-date sponsor PR\n- **EPC contractor backlogs** \u2014 Bechtel, McDermott, KBR, JGC, Worley, Saipem, Technip, Wood, Fluor occasionally disclose project wins\n- **Equipment supplier wins** \u2014 GTT (containment), Air Products (liquefaction), Chart Industries, W\u00e4rtsil\u00e4 (FSRUs)\n- **NGO / opposition research** \u2014 Reclaim Finance, IEEFA, Oil Change International often track LNG projects (including unconfirmed ones); use as a lead, NOT as a primary citation\n\nRing D candidates tend to need the most verification \u2014 early-stage signals from supplier/financier channels are real but often refer to pre-public projects that shouldn't yet be added.\n\n## \u00a75 Monitor list (candidates that don't meet threshold)\n\nCandidates that fail any threshold element from \u00a73 go in `monitor_list` sheet with:\n- Sponsor (if known)\n- Country/Region\n- Source URL(s)\n- Which threshold elements are missing\n- Date first noticed\n- Suggested re-check date (typically 6-12 months later)\n\nPurpose: avoid re-discovering the same vague-rumor project in every batch, and create a re-check trigger when the project may have firmed up.\n\nThe `monitor_list` is intended to roll forward across batches \u2014 the build script should read the prior batch's monitor_list and merge with the current batch's additions, dropping items that have since moved to the real `new_terminals` sheet.\n\n## \u00a76 Dedup against existing GEM\n\nBefore staging a candidate as new, verify it's not already in GEM under a different name. `dedup_index.py` builds two indexes for this purpose:\n\n- **Project index**: `(country_normalized, terminal_name_normalized)` \u2192 TerminalIDs\n- **Sponsor-country index**: `(country_normalized, sponsor_normalized)` \u2192 list of TerminalIDs\n\nFor each candidate:\n1. Normalize the candidate's country, name, and sponsor per `normalize.py`\n2. Check project index for exact match \u2192 likely duplicate\n3. Check sponsor-country index \u2192 list of all GEM terminals from this sponsor in this country\n4. For each sponsor-country match, compare:\n   - Location (if both have lat/lng, distance in km)\n   - Capacity (if both have a value, ratio)\n   - Lifecycle status (cancelled GEM unit + new sponsor announcement = possible dead-and-revived)\n5. If similarity is high \u2192 likely duplicate, route to Update workflow (per lifecycle_rules.md dead-and-revived rules)\n6. If similarity is low \u2192 genuinely new candidate\n\n**Expansion vs new project** is a common ambiguity:\n- A new train at an existing terminal \u2192 new **unit** within an existing terminal (use `new_units` sheet, not `new_terminals`)\n- A new terminal at the same site as an existing one (e.g. import terminal added next to existing export terminal) \u2192 genuinely new terminal, but with `AssociatedTerminals` link to the existing one\n- A new phase of the same terminal proposal (e.g. NextDecade Phase 2) \u2192 new units, not new terminal\n\nThe methodology FAQ has examples; consult when ambiguous.\n\n## \u00a77 Building a candidate row\n\nFor each verified candidate that meets the threshold, build a row with as many fields populated as the sources support. **Minimum required fields** to stage in `new_terminals`:\n\n- `TerminalName` (per methodology naming conventions: usually `<Site> LNG Terminal` or `<Site> FSRU`)\n- `Country/Area`\n- `FacilityType` (`import` or `export`)\n- `Status` (typically `proposed` for newly-discovered)\n- `Substatus` (blank for `proposed`)\n- `Owner` (at least one entity \u2014 entity lookup mandatory per Update SOP \u00a78)\n- `Location` (at minimum a free-text location string; lat/lng if available with appropriate `Accuracy`)\n- `Source [ref]` or `Status [ref]` (at least one cited URL covering the threshold elements)\n\nOther fields populated when sources support:\n- `Capacity` + `CapacityUnits` (usually MTPA for LNG)\n- `ProposalYear` (year of the public announcement that establishes the project)\n- `Operator` (often same as Owner for newly proposed)\n- `Parent` (if Owner is a subsidiary)\n- `Offshore` / `Floating` booleans + `FloatingVesselName` if FSRU\n- `OriginalPlannedStartYear` (if sponsor has stated a target)\n- `FIDStatus = Pre-FID` only if explicitly stated; otherwise leave blank\n- `Pipelines`, `PowerPlantsSupplied`, `Source` (gas field) \u2014 populate when known, fine to leave blank\n\nFor multi-unit projects discovered at once (e.g. a 3-train liquefaction proposal), build one row in `new_terminals` plus N rows in `new_units` (one per train). Methodology naming: trains get `UnitName` = `T1`, `T2`, `T3` typically; phases get `Phase 1`, `Phase 2`.\n\n## \u00a78 URL verification gate (mandatory)\n\nEvery URL goes through `url_verifier.py` per Update SOP \u00a77. Discovery has the additional risk of citing sources that mention the project name but don't actually establish it (e.g. a sponsor's investor day deck mentions \"expansion opportunities including a potential terminal in X\" \u2014 passes a naive name-match, fails the threshold).\n\nFor discovery citations specifically, the `expected_string` arguments should verify:\n- The terminal name OR site name OR sponsor name\n- A specific concrete step from the threshold (e.g. \"FEED\", \"MOU signed\", \"permit filed\", \"FID\")\n- The country\n\nExample: `python url_verifier.py <url> \"Plaquemines\" \"Phase 2\" \"FERC\"`\n\nThe verifier dropping a URL for missing the threshold-step keyword is a signal that the URL doesn't actually support the candidate \u2014 re-evaluate whether the candidate meets the threshold or whether a different URL needs to be found.\n\n## \u00a79 Entity discipline\n\nPer Update SOP \u00a78, every new Owner / Operator / Parent / VesselOwner / VesselOperator goes through `entity_lookup.py` before being staged. Discovery tends to surface more new entities than Update (new projects often involve new SPVs and JV structures), so expect `entity_additions` sheet to be more active.\n\nFor SPV-style entities (special-purpose vehicles set up for a single project, often a project name + \"LLC\" or similar):\n- Create the SPV as the immediate Owner\n- Set Parent to the sponsoring company/companies\n- Note in the entity addition that this is an SPV (helps the Ownership Team distinguish from real operating entities)\n\nFor JV-style entities (e.g. \"TotalEnergies-Petronas JV\"):\n- Methodology preference is to list each JV partner as a separate Owner with their percentage, NOT to create a JV entity\n- Exception: if the JV operates as a real legal entity with its own staff and publications (e.g. NLNG Limited as a JV of NNPC, Shell, Total, ENI), treat as a single entity\n\n## \u00a710 Workflow (linear)\n\n1. **Confirm parameters** (\u00a72)\n2. **Materialize scripts** per SKILL.md\n3. `python pull_gem_db.py` \u2192 fresh CSV, column-index map. **Mandatory every batch.**\n4. `python dedup_index.py` \u2192 project + sponsor-country indexes (\u00a76)\n5. **For each ring (A \u2192 B \u2192 C \u2192 D) within the scope:**\n   a. Execute the ring's search strategy (\u00a74)\n   b. For each lead, check dedup (\u00a76) \u2014 skip if duplicate, route to Update if dead-and-revived\n   c. Apply threshold test (\u00a73) \u2014 pass \u2192 `new_terminals`/`new_units`, fail \u2192 `monitor_list`\n   d. For passing candidates, build the row (\u00a77)\n6. `python url_verifier.py` on every staged URL (\u00a78)\n7. `python entity_lookup.py` for every new entity reference (\u00a79)\n8. `python capacity_normalize.py` for any candidate with capacity in non-standard units\n9. **If batch includes any FSRU candidates:** `python fsru_sync_check.py` against carrier project backend (SKILL.md FSRU sync rule)\n10. Merge the `monitor_list` with the prior batch's monitor_list (\u00a75)\n11. **Contribute country findings** to `country_notes_contributions` sheet \u2014 new regulator URLs, search patterns that worked, country-specific gotchas\n12. `python build_review_package.py --mode discovery --batch-id <YYYYMMDD>` \u2192 staging xlsx\n13. `python recalc.py` \u2192 confirm zero formula errors\n14. `present_files`\n\n## \u00a711 Hard rules\n\n- **Threshold test before staging** \u2014 every `new_terminals` row must pass \u00a73\n- **Dedup before staging** \u2014 every candidate gets checked against existing GEM per \u00a76\n- **Every URL passes the verification gate** (\u00a78)\n- **Pull a fresh GEM CSV at the start of every batch** (\u00a710.3)\n- **Don't create duplicate entities** \u2014 `entity_lookup.py` per \u00a79\n- **No orphan `[ref]` cells** (Rule F from carrier and Update SOP)\n- **GIIGNL/IGU candidates require independent verification** \u2014 GIIGNL-only findings from reconciliation are leads, not authority.       "json_block": "{\"language\": \"markdown\", \"code\": \"# LNG Terminals Discovery SOP\\n\\nLast revised: 2026-05 (rev 1, initial draft)\\n\\nOperational rules for finding LNG terminals (both import and export, all scales except bunkering) that are NOT yet in the GEM database. Discovery feeds candidate terminals into a staging xlsx for human review and addition to the live DB.\\n\\nThe methodology doc (LNG Terminals Manual) is authoritative for what counts as a terminal, the \\\"sufficient information to add\\\" threshold, and how new units are named. This SOP is operational \\u2014 describes how to execute the discovery work, citing the methodology rather than restating it.\\n\\n## \\u00a71 When to run this SOP\\n\\nTrigger conditions:\\n- Triage SOP has scoped a country/region for discovery work this batch\\n- A reconciliation batch produced `giignl_to_action` findings routed to Discovery (GIIGNL-only candidates)\\n- The user explicitly requests a discovery run for a country, region, or sponsor\\n- A specific news event suggests new project activity in a region not covered by an upcoming Update batch (a major sponsor's quarterly announcement, a country opening a new round of bids)\\n- A \\\"catch-up sweep\\\" after a long period without coverage of a particular region\\n\\n## \\u00a72 Confirm parameters at batch start\\n\\nDiscovery is more sensitive to scope choices than Update, because the \\\"what's in scope?\\\" question genuinely affects what candidates surface. Confirm before any tool runs:\\n\\n1. **Geographic scope** \\u2014 country, region, or global. Global discovery is expensive; if the user requests global, push back unless triage justifies it.\\n2. **Project type scope** \\u2014 import, export, or both. Defaults to both per the project-wide scope (excluding bunkering).\\n3. **Lifecycle stage threshold** \\u2014 how early-stage to accept candidates. Options:\\n   - **Tight** (default): require the methodology's \\\"sufficient information to add\\\" \\u2014 sponsor identified + approximate location + concrete step taken\\n   - **Permissive**: include early-rumor-stage candidates in a `monitor_list` sheet for future tracking\\n   - **Operating-only**: only accept candidates already commissioned (rare \\u2014 usually combined with reconciliation backlog)\\n4. **Time window** \\u2014 how far back to search. Defaults to \\\"anything not in the current GEM export, regardless of age\\\" but practically the highest yield is announcements from the last 12-24 months.\\n5. **FSRU handling** \\u2014 if scope includes import discovery in countries with FSRU activity, sync rule applies (SKILL.md).\\n6. **Reconciliation-fed candidates** \\u2014 if any GIIGNL-only findings from a prior reconciliation are pending, list them in scope at batch start. Discovery for these is partly pre-done (GIIGNL provided the initial lead); workflow focuses on verification and threshold testing.\\n\\nThese parameters get written into the staging xlsx README sheet.\\n\\n## \\u00a73 The \\\"sufficient information to add\\\" threshold\\n\\nPer the methodology FAQ, a candidate qualifies for addition to GEM when all three are present:\\n\\n1. **Sponsor identified** \\u2014 a specific company or entity (not \\\"consortium being formed\\\" or \\\"TBD\\\")\\n2. **Approximate location** \\u2014 at minimum, a country + region/state/port (latitude/longitude can be approximate; methodology accepts `Accuracy = approximate`)\\n3. **Concrete step taken** \\u2014 beyond pure verbal intent. Examples that count: MOU signed, site selected, FEED contract awarded, environmental permit applied for, public consultation initiated, regulatory pre-filing, land lease secured.\\n\\nCandidates that fall short go in `monitor_list` (see \\u00a75) with a note on which threshold elements are missing. This is the equivalent of the Update SOP's \\\"yellow \\u2192 leave blank\\\" discipline: not everything we find should result in an add.\\n\\n**Edge cases:**\\n- **Vague sponsor** (e.g. \\\"a Chinese consortium\\\") \\u2014 fails the sponsor test. Monitor list.\\n- **Multiple alternative sites under consideration** (e.g. \\\"Site A or Site B in Vietnam\\\") \\u2014 usually fails the location test unless one is clearly the leading candidate per recent reporting.\\n- **Verbal intent only** (e.g. \\\"X country's energy minister said the country will build an LNG import terminal by 2030\\\") \\u2014 fails the concrete step test. Monitor list.\\n- **Genuine pre-FID with sponsor, location, FEED contract** \\u2014 passes. Add as `proposed`, FID status `Pre-FID` only if explicitly reported.\\n- **Project announced years ago but no apparent activity since** \\u2014 passes the threshold but enters as `shelved` with substatus `inferred 2 y` or `confirmed`. The age of the most recent news drives the status, not the age of the project itself.\\n\\n## \\u00a74 The four-ring discovery model\\n\\nBorrowed from the carrier project's discovery structure, adapted for terminals. The rings are searched in order; later rings catch what earlier rings miss.\\n\\n### \\u00a74.1 Ring A \\u2014 country-level regulatory sweep\\n\\nThe most authoritative ring. National regulators publish concrete project information (filings, permits, environmental assessments) that establishes both existence and several key data fields at once.\\n\\nFor each country in scope, consult:\\n\\n- **United States**: FERC eLibrary (`elibrary.ferc.gov`) for import/export terminals; DOE Office of Fossil Energy & Carbon Management export authorizations\\n- **European Union**: PCI list portal (`energy.ec.europa.eu`); per-country TSOs (e.g. GRTgaz for France, Snam for Italy)\\n- **United Kingdom**: Ofgem decisions; Planning Inspectorate (NSIP project list)\\n- **Canada**: CER (Canada Energy Regulator) for export licenses; provincial environmental assessment agencies (BC EAO, etc.)\\n- **Australia**: NOPSEMA for offshore; state EPA decisions; AEMO gas statement of opportunities\\n- **Japan**: METI announcements; JOGMEC strategic reserve plans\\n- **South Korea**: MOTIE; KOGAS IR\\n- **China**: NDRC press releases; CNPC, Sinopec, CNOOC quarterly disclosures; provincial development & reform commissions for inland regas\\n- **India**: MOPNG; PNGRB tariff orders (which require regulatory filings before operation)\\n- **Brazil**: ANP terminal authorizations; EPE planning documents\\n- **Mexico**: CRE permits; SENER strategic outlooks\\n- **Russia**: Limited public regulatory data post-sanctions; check IISS, FACTS Global Energy secondary coverage\\n- **Middle East / Gulf**: state oil company IR (Saudi Aramco, ADNOC Gas, QatarEnergy); ENOC for UAE\\n- **Africa**: country-by-country highly variable; check IEA Africa Energy Outlook, Reuters Africa, sponsor IR\\n- **Southeast Asia**: per-country, e.g. Philippines DOE, Vietnam MOIT, Indonesia ESDM\\n\\nThis list is not exhaustive. `country_research_notes.md` is the working memory for country-specific regulator URLs, filing patterns, and update cadences. Contribute findings back to that file.\\n\\n### \\u00a74.2 Ring B \\u2014 trade press sweep\\n\\nFor each country/region in scope, search trade press for new-project announcements in the time window:\\n\\n- **Workhorses**: LNG Prime, Reuters Energy, S&P Global Commodity Insights, Argus Media, Upstream Online, Energy Intelligence\\n- **Regional specialists**: Splash247 (shipping angle), Riviera Maritime Media (technical), Hellenic Shipping News (Europe), Hydrocarbons Africa, Energy Voice (UK)\\n- **Tier 1b regulatory press**: en.sedaily.com (Korean DART proxies), iMarine (Asia)\\n\\nSearch patterns that work:\\n- `\\\"LNG terminal\\\" \\\"<country>\\\" \\\"announced\\\" \\\"<year>\\\"`\\n- `\\\"<country>\\\" \\\"regasification\\\" \\\"MOU\\\"`\\n- `\\\"FSRU\\\" \\\"<country>\\\" \\\"deployment\\\"`\\n- `\\\"<sponsor name>\\\" \\\"LNG\\\" \\\"<country>\\\"`\\n- `\\\"<country>\\\" \\\"liquefaction\\\" \\\"FEED\\\"`\\n\\nTrade press often leads regulator filings by weeks-to-months for early-stage projects; regulators trail trade press but offer harder evidence.\\n\\n### \\u00a74.3 Ring C \\u2014 sponsor IR / corporate sweep\\n\\nFor sponsors known to be active in LNG, walk their IR materials directly. The methodology's \\\"established LNG developer\\\" list as a starting point:\\n\\n- **US-focused exporters**: Cheniere, Venture Global, NextDecade, Sempra, Freeport LNG, Tellurian, Energy Transfer\\n- **Integrated majors**: TotalEnergies, Shell, BP, ExxonMobil, Chevron, ConocoPhillips, Eni\\n- **Asian state-linked**: QatarEnergy, ADNOC Gas, Petronas, Pertamina, CNPC, Sinopec, CNOOC, KOGAS, JERA\\n- **FSRU operators**: Excelerate Energy, H\\u00f6egh Evi, BW LNG, Energos Infrastructure, Karpowership/KARMOL, New Fortress Energy\\n- **Import-side**: ENGIE, Naturgy, Snam, Fluxys, Enagas, RWE, Uniper, Sempra Infrastructure\\n\\nFor each sponsor in scope:\\n- IR press releases (last 12-24 months)\\n- Quarterly earnings calls (transcripts via Seeking Alpha, sponsor IR site)\\n- Annual reports / sustainability reports\\n- Investor day decks (these often disclose pipeline projects pre-PR)\\n\\nSponsor IR is often the earliest credible signal \\u2014 sponsors disclose to investors before broad press release.\\n\\n### \\u00a74.4 Ring D \\u2014 broader scan (optional, when prior rings underyield)\\n\\nWhen rings A-C don't surface enough candidates to justify the batch (or when scope is intentionally broad), expand to:\\n\\n- **Industry conference materials** (LNG2026, Gastech, World Gas Conference) \\u2014 presenter lists often include emerging projects\\n- **Lender / financier announcements** \\u2014 JBIC, KEXIM, ECAs, multilateral development bank disclosures often pre-date sponsor PR\\n- **EPC contractor backlogs** \\u2014 Bechtel, McDermott, KBR, JGC, Worley, Saipem, Technip, Wood, Fluor occasionally disclose project wins\\n- **Equipment supplier wins** \\u2014 GTT (containment), Air Products (liquefaction), Chart Industries, W\\u00e4rtsil\\u00e4 (FSRUs)\\n- **NGO / opposition research** \\u2014 Reclaim Finance, IEEFA, Oil Change International often track LNG projects (including unconfirmed ones); use as a lead, NOT as a primary citation\\n\\nRing D candidates tend to need the most verification \\u2014 early-stage signals from supplier/financier channels are real but often refer to pre-public projects that shouldn't yet be added.\\n\\n## \\u00a75 Monitor list (candidates that don't meet threshold)\\n\\nCandidates that fail any threshold element from \\u00a73 go in `monitor_list` sheet with:\\n- Sponsor (if known)\\n- Country/Region\\n- Source URL(s)\\n- Which threshold elements are missing\\n- Date first noticed\\n- Suggested re-check date (typically 6-12 months later)\\n\\nPurpose: avoid re-discovering the same vague-rumor project in every batch, and create a re-check trigger when the project may have firmed up.\\n\\nThe `monitor_list` is intended to roll forward across batches \\u2014 the build script should read the prior batch's monitor_list and merge with the current batch's additions, dropping items that have since moved to the real `new_terminals` sheet.\\n\\n## \\u00a76 Dedup against existing GEM\\n\\nBefore staging a candidate as new, verify it's not already in GEM under a different name. `dedup_index.py` builds two indexes for this purpose:\\n\\n- **Project index**: `(country_normalized, terminal_name_normalized)` \\u2192 TerminalIDs\\n- **Sponsor-country index**: `(country_normalized, sponsor_normalized)` \\u2192 list of TerminalIDs\\n\\nFor each candidate:\\n1. Normalize the candidate's country, name, and sponsor per `normalize.py`\\n2. Check project index for exact match \\u2192 likely duplicate\\n3. Check sponsor-country index \\u2192 list of all GEM terminals from this sponsor in this country\\n4. For each sponsor-country match, compare:\\n   - Location (if both have lat/lng, distance in km)\\n   - Capacity (if both have a value, ratio)\\n   - Lifecycle status (cancelled GEM unit + new sponsor announcement = possible dead-and-revived)\\n5. If similarity is high \\u2192 likely duplicate, route to Update workflow (per lifecycle_rules.md dead-and-revived rules)\\n6. If similarity is low \\u2192 genuinely new candidate\\n\\n**Expansion vs new project** is a common ambiguity:\\n- A new train at an existing terminal \\u2192 new **unit** within an existing terminal (use `new_units` sheet, not `new_terminals`)\\n- A new terminal at the same site as an existing one (e.g. import terminal added next to existing export terminal) \\u2192 genuinely new terminal, but with `AssociatedTerminals` link to the existing one\\n- A new phase of the same terminal proposal (e.g. NextDecade Phase 2) \\u2192 new units, not new terminal\\n\\nThe methodology FAQ has examples; consult when ambiguous.\\n\\n## \\u00a77 Building a candidate row\\n\\nFor each verified candidate that meets the threshold, build a row with as many fields populated as the sources support. **Minimum required fields** to stage in `new_terminals`:\\n\\n- `TerminalName` (per methodology naming conventions: usually `<Site> LNG Terminal` or `<Site> FSRU`)\\n- `Country/Area`\\n- `FacilityType` (`import` or `export`)\\n- `Status` (typically `proposed` for newly-discovered)\\n- `Substatus` (blank for `proposed`)\\n- `Owner` (at least one entity \\u2014 entity lookup mandatory per Update SOP \\u00a78)\\n- `Location` (at minimum a free-text location string; lat/lng if available with appropriate `Accuracy`)\\n- `Source [ref]` or `Status [ref]` (at least one cited URL covering the threshold elements)\\n\\nOther fields populated when sources support:\\n- `Capacity` + `CapacityUnits` (usually MTPA for LNG)\\n- `ProposalYear` (year of the public announcement that establishes the project)\\n- `Operator` (often same as Owner for newly proposed)\\n- `Parent` (if Owner is a subsidiary)\\n- `Offshore` / `Floating` booleans + `FloatingVesselName` if FSRU\\n- `OriginalPlannedStartYear` (if sponsor has stated a target)\\n- `FIDStatus = Pre-FID` only if explicitly stated; otherwise leave blank\\n- `Pipelines`, `PowerPlantsSupplied`, `Source` (gas field) \\u2014 populate when known, fine to leave blank\\n\\nFor multi-unit projects discovered at once (e.g. a 3-train liquefaction proposal), build one row in `new_terminals` plus N rows in `new_units` (one per train). Methodology naming: trains get `UnitName` = `T1`, `T2`, `T3` typically; phases get `Phase 1`, `Phase 2`.\\n\\n## \\u00a78 URL verification gate (mandatory)\\n\\nEvery URL goes through `url_verifier.py` per Update SOP \\u00a77. Discovery has the additional risk of citing sources that mention the project name but don't actually establish it (e.g. a sponsor's investor day deck mentions \\\"expansion opportunities including a potential terminal in X\\\" \\u2014 passes a naive name-match, fails the threshold).\\n\\nFor discovery citations specifically, the `expected_string` arguments should verify:\\n- The terminal name OR site name OR sponsor name\\n- A specific concrete step from the threshold (e.g. \\\"FEED\\\", \\\"MOU signed\\\", \\\"permit filed\\\", \\\"FID\\\")\\n- The country\\n\\nExample: `python url_verifier.py <url> \\\"Plaquemines\\\" \\\"Phase 2\\\" \\\"FERC\\\"`\\n\\nThe verifier dropping a URL for missing the threshold-step keyword is a signal that the URL doesn't actually support the candidate \\u2014 re-evaluate whether the candidate meets the threshold or whether a different URL needs to be found.\\n\\n## \\u00a79 Entity discipline\\n\\nPer Update SOP \\u00a78, every new Owner / Operator / Parent / VesselOwner / VesselOperator goes through `entity_lookup.py` before being staged. Discovery tends to surface more new entities than Update (new projects often involve new SPVs and JV structures), so expect `entity_additions` sheet to be more active.\\n\\nFor SPV-style entities (special-purpose vehicles set up for a single project, often a project name + \\\"LLC\\\" or similar):\\n- Create the SPV as the immediate Owner\\n- Set Parent to the sponsoring company/companies\\n- Note in the entity addition that this is an SPV (helps the Ownership Team distinguish from real operating entities)\\n\\nFor JV-style entities (e.g. \\\"TotalEnergies-Petronas JV\\\"):\\n- Methodology preference is to list each JV partner as a separate Owner with their percentage, NOT to create a JV entity\\n- Exception: if the JV operates as a real legal entity with its own staff and publications (e.g. NLNG Limited as a JV of NNPC, Shell, Total, ENI), treat as a single entity\\n\\n## \\u00a710 Workflow (linear)\\n\\n1. **Confirm parameters** (\\u00a72)\\n2. **Materialize scripts** per SKILL.md\\n3. `python pull_gem_db.py` \\u2192 fresh CSV, column-index map. **Mandatory every batch.**\\n4. `python dedup_index.py` \\u2192 project + sponsor-country indexes (\\u00a76)\\n5. **For each ring (A \\u2192 B \\u2192 C \\u2192 D) within the scope:**\\n   a. Execute the ring's search strategy (\\u00a74)\\n   b. For each lead, check dedup (\\u00a76) \\u2014 skip if duplicate, route to Update if dead-and-revived\\n   c. Apply threshold test (\\u00a73) \\u2014 pass \\u2192 `new_terminals`/`new_units`, fail \\u2192 `monitor_list`\\n   d. For passing candidates, build the row (\\u00a77)\\n6. `python url_verifier.py` on every staged URL (\\u00a78)\\n7. `python entity_lookup.py` for every new entity reference (\\u00a79)\\n8. `python capacity_normalize.py` for any candidate with capacity in non-standard units\\n9. **If batch includes any FSRU candidates:** `python fsru_sync_check.py` against carrier project backend (SKILL.md FSRU sync rule)\\n10. Merge the `monitor_list` with the prior batch's monitor_list (\\u00a75)\\n11. **Contribute country findings** to `country_notes_contributions` sheet \\u2014 new regulator URLs, search patterns that worked, country-specific gotchas\\n12. `python build_review_package.py --mode discovery --batch-id <YYYYMMDD>` \\u2192 staging xlsx\\n13. `python recalc.py` \\u2192 confirm zero formula errors\\n14. `present_files`\\n\\n## \\u00a711 Hard rules\\n\\n- **Threshold test before staging** \\u2014 every `new_terminals` row must pass \\u00a73\\n- **Dedup before staging** \\u2014 every candidate gets checked against existing GEM per \\u00a76\\n- **Every URL passes the verification gate** (\\u00a78)\\n- **Pull a fresh GEM CSV at the start of every batch** (\\u00a710.3)\\n- **Don't create duplicate entities** \\u2014 `entity_lookup.py` per \\u00a79\\n- **No orphan `[ref]` cells** (Rule F from carrier and Update SOP)\\n- **GIIGNL/IGU candidates require independent verification** \\u2014 GIIGNL-only findings from reconciliation are leads, not authority. Source-search like any other candidate.\\n- **Out-of-scope fields stay blank** \\u2014 never populate LH2/NH3/SyntheticLNG/PCI fields on a new candidate, even if sources mention them\\n- **FSRU candidates trigger sync check** \\u2014 per \\u00a710.9\\n- **Multi-train projects \\u2192 one terminal row + N unit rows**, not N terminals\\n\\n## \\u00a712 Pause-and-ask triggers\\n\\nStop and     "text": "Discovery SOP drafted. Things worth your specific attention before I move on to Triage:\n\n**Key structural choices:**\n\n- **Four-ring discovery model** ported from the carrier project: regulators (A) \u2192 trade press (B) \u2192 sponsor IR (C) \u2192 broader sources (D). The order matters because A-C are progressively earlier signals (regulator filings are hardest evidence but slowest; IR is sometimes the earliest credible signal). Tell me if you'd reorder.\n\n- **The \"sufficient information to add\" threshold (\u00a73)** turned into the most rule-bound part of the SOP. I treated it as a hard pass/fail filter rather than a confidence label, because the methodology FAQ describes it as an inclusion criterion not a quality grade. Sub-threshold candidates go to `monitor_list` rather than getting added with low confidence. If GEM staff would rather see all candidates added (even low-confidence ones) and let the human reviewer decide, that's a different design.\n\n- **The `monitor_list` rolls forward across batches.** \u00a75 says the build script should read the prior batch's monitor_list and merge. This adds a real dependency: the build script needs to know where the last batch's xlsx lives. I'm assuming the user keeps these in a known location (or in the project files). Worth confirming.\n\n**Three opinionated calls in \u00a74 (the ring details):**\n\n1. **The country regulator list** is my best attempt at a global one-paragraph guide, but it's incomplete and will mostly live in `country_research_notes.md` once that file is built up batch by batch. The SOP shouldn't try to be the country-resource doc.\n\n2. **The sponsor IR list** for Ring C is mine \u2014 I tried to cover US exporters, integrated majors, Asian state-linked, FSRU operators, and import-side. I almost certainly missed some that GEM staff would consider obvious. Worth a quick scan.\n\n3. **Trade press tiering puts LNG Prime as the workhorse first** \u2014 it has the best LNG-specific coverage. Reuters and S&P Global are general-energy and need filtering. Disagree if your team uses different defaults.\n\n**One genuine open question in \u00a79 (Entity discipline):** SPVs vs JV entities. I went with \"list each JV partner as separate Owner with percentage\" as the default, \"create JV as single entity\" only when the JV operates as a real legal entity with its own staff and publications (NLNG as the example). This is consistent with the GEM data I see (where Owner field often has comma-separated entities with percentages), but the methodology may have a clearer rule that I missed. Worth checking.\n\n**One thing I deliberately didn't include:** a rule about \"discovery from sanctions/excluded sources.\" The methodology doesn't specifically discuss this, but in practice some Russian, Iranian, etc. projects only appear in sanctioned or low-quality sources. Right now the SOP just says \"follow tier rules\" \u2014 if there's a specific policy on whether to add sanctioned-region projects from limited sources, the SOP should encode it.\n\nNext file: `lng_terminal_triage_sop.md` \u2014 the lightest of the four.
